"CHRISTIAN BIBLE The Old Testament of the King James Version of the Bible The First Book of Moses: Called Genesis 1:1 In the beginning God created the heaven and the earth. 1:2 And the earth was without form, and void; and darkness was upon the face of the deep. And the Spirit of God moved upon the face of the waters. 1:3 And God said, Let there be light: and there was light. 1:4 And God saw the light, that it was good: and God divided the light from the darkness. 1:5 And God called the light Day, and the darkness he called Night. And the evening and the morning were the first day. 1:6 And God said, Let there be a firmament in the midst of the waters, and let it divide the waters from the waters. 1:7 And God made the firmament, and divided the waters which were under the firmament from the waters which were above the firmament: and it was so. 1:8 And God called the firmament Heaven. And the evening and the morning were the second day. 1:9 And God said, Let the waters under the heaven be gathered together unto one place, and let the dry land appear: and it was so. 1:10 And God called the dry land Earth; and the gathering together of the waters called he Seas: and God saw that it was good. 1:11 And God said, Let the earth bring forth grass, the herb yielding seed, and the fruit tree yielding fruit after his kind, whose seed is in itself, upon the earth: and it was so. 1:12 And the earth brought forth grass, and herb yielding seed after his kind, and the tree yielding fruit, whose seed was in itself, after his kind: and God saw that it was good. 1:13 And the evening and the morning were the third day. 1:14 And God said, Let there be lights in the firmament of the heaven to divide the day from the night; and let them be for signs, and for seasons, and for days, and years: 1:15 And let them be for lights in the firmament of the heaven to give light upon the earth: and it was so. 1:16 And God made two great lights; the greater light to rule the day, and the lesser light to rule the night: he made the stars also. 1:17 And God set them in the firmament of the heaven to give light upon the earth, 1:18 And to rule over the day and over the night, and to divide the light from the darkness: and God saw that it was good. 1:19 And the evening and the morning were the fourth day. 1:20 And God said, Let the waters bring forth abundantly the moving creature that hath life, and fowl that may fly above the earth in the open firmament of heaven. 1:21 And God created great whales, and every living creature that moveth, which the waters brought forth abundantly, after their kind, and every winged fowl after his kind: and God saw that it was good. 1:22 And God blessed them, saying, Be fruitful, and multiply, and fill the waters in the seas, and let fowl multiply in the earth. 1:23 And the evening and the morning were the fifth day. 1:24 And God said, Let the earth bring forth the living creature after his kind, cattle, and creeping thing, and beast of the earth after his kind: and it was so. 1:25 And God made the beast of the earth after his kind, and cattle after their kind, and every thing that creepeth upon the earth after his kind: and God saw that it was good. 1:26 And God said, Let us make man in our image, after our likeness: and let them have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over the cattle, and over all the earth, and over every creeping thing that creepeth upon the earth. 1:27 So God created man in his own image, in the image of God created he him; male and female created he them. 1:28 And God blessed them, and God said unto them, Be fruitful, and multiply, and replenish the earth, and subdue it: and have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over every living thing that moveth upon the earth. 1:29 And God said, Behold, I have given you every herb bearing seed, which is upon the face of all the earth, and every tree, in the which is the fruit of a tree yielding seed; to you it shall be for meat. 1:30 And to every beast of the earth, and to every fowl of the air, and to every thing that creepeth upon the earth, wherein there is life, I have given every green herb for meat: and it was so. 1:31 And God saw every thing that he had made, and, behold, it was very good. And the evening and the morning were the sixth day. 2:1 Thus the heavens and the earth were finished, and all the host of them. 2:2 And on the seventh day God ended his work which he had made; and he rested on the seventh day from all his work which he had made. 2:3 And God blessed the seventh day, and sanctified it: because that in it he had rested from all his work which God created and made. 2:4 These are the generations of the heavens and of the earth when they were created, in the day that the LORD God made the earth and the heavens, 2:5 And every plant of the field before it was in the earth, and every herb of the field before it grew: for the LORD God had not caused it to rain upon the earth.""CHRISTIAN BIBLE The Old Testament of the King James Version of the Bible The First Book of Moses: Called Genesis 1:1 In the beginning God created the heaven and the earth. 1:2 And the earth was without form, and void; and darkness was upon the face of the deep. But a mist went up from the earth and watered the whole face of the ground. The LORD God formed man from the dust of the ground, breathed into his nostrils the breath of life, and man became a living soul. The LORD God planted a garden in Eden, where He put the man He had formed. Out of the ground, the LORD God made every tree that is pleasant to the sight and good for food, including the tree of life and the tree of knowledge of good and evil. A river went out of Eden to water the garden, dividing into four heads. The names of the rivers are Pison, Gihon, Hiddekel, and Euphrates. The LORD God took the man and put him in the Garden of Eden to tend and keep it. He commanded the man that he could eat freely of every tree in the garden except the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, for eating from it would surely result in death. The LORD God said it was not good for the man to be alone and decided to make a helper suitable for him. From the ground, the LORD God formed every beast and bird and brought them to Adam to see what he would name them. However, no suitable helper was found among them. So, the LORD God caused Adam to fall into a deep sleep, took one of his ribs, and made a woman from it, bringing her to the man. Adam recognized her as "bone of my bones, and flesh of my flesh." Therefore, a man shall leave his parents and be united with his wife, and they shall become one flesh. They were both naked and were not ashamed. The serpent, more cunning than any beast, deceived the woman into eating from the forbidden tree, and she also gave some to her husband, who ate. Their eyes were opened, realizing they were naked; they sewed fig leaves together for cover. Hearing the LORD God in the garden, they hid themselves. The LORD God questioned Adam, who blamed the woman, who in turn blamed the serpent. The LORD God cursed the serpent, promised enmity between the serpent's and the woman's offspring, and declared that the woman's offspring would crush the serpent's head. The woman was told her pain in childbirth would be greatly increased, and her desire would be for her husband, who would rule over her. To Adam, because he listened to his wife and ate from the tree, the ground was cursed, and he would toil for food all the days of his life.And there was not a man to till the ground. But there went up a mist from the earth, and watered the whole face of the ground. The LORD God formed man of the dust of the ground, and breathed into his nostrils the breath of life; and man became a living soul. The LORD God planted a garden eastward in Eden; and there he put the man whom he had formed. Out of the ground made the LORD God to grow every tree that is pleasant to the sight, and good for food; the tree of life also in the midst of the garden, and the tree of knowledge of good and evil. A river went out of Eden to water the garden; and from thence it was parted, and became into four heads. The name of the first is Pison: that is it which compasseth the whole land of Havilah, where there is gold; And the gold of that land is good: there is bdellium and the onyx stone. The name of the second river is Gihon: the same is it that compasseth the whole land of Ethiopia. The name of the third river is Hiddekel: that is it which goeth toward the east of Assyria. And the fourth river is Euphrates. The LORD God took the man, and put him into the garden of Eden to dress it and to keep it. The LORD God commanded the man, saying, Of every tree of the garden thou mayest freely eat: But of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, thou shalt not eat of it: for in the day that thou eatest thereof thou shalt surely die. The LORD God said, It is not good that the man should be alone; I will make him an help meet for him. Out of the ground the LORD God formed every beast of the field, and every fowl of the air; and brought them unto Adam to see what he would call them: and whatsoever Adam called every living creature, that was the name thereof. And Adam gave names to all cattle, and to the fowl of the air, and to every beast of the field; but for Adam there was not found an help meet for him. The LORD God caused a deep sleep to fall upon Adam, and he slept: and he took one of his ribs, and closed up the flesh instead thereof; And the rib, which the LORD God had taken from man, made he a woman, and brought her unto the man. And Adam said, This is now bone of my bones, and flesh of my flesh: she shall be called Woman, because she was taken out of Man. Therefore shall a man leave his father and his mother, and shall cleave unto his wife: and they shall be one flesh. And they were both naked, the man and his wife, and were not ashamed. Now the serpent was more subtil than any beast of the field which the LORD God had made. And he said unto the woman, Yea, hath God said, Ye shall not eat of every tree of the garden? And the woman said unto the serpent, We may eat of the fruit of the trees of the garden: But of the fruit of the tree which is in the midst of the garden, God hath said, Ye shall not eat of it, neither shall ye touch it, lest ye die. And the serpent said unto the woman, Ye shall not surely die: For God doth know that in the day ye eat thereof, then your eyes shall be opened, and ye shall be as gods, knowing good and evil. And when the woman saw that the tree was good for food, and that it was pleasant to the eyes, and a tree to be desired to make one wise, she took of the fruit thereof, and did eat, and gave also unto her husband with her; and he did eat. And the eyes of them both were opened, and they knew that they were naked; and they sewed fig leaves together, and made themselves aprons. And they heard the voice of the LORD God walking in the garden in the cool of the day: and Adam and his wife hid themselves from the presence of the LORD God amongst the trees of the garden. The LORD God called unto Adam, and said unto him, Where art thou? And he said, I heard thy voice in the garden, and I was afraid, because I was naked; and I hid myself. And he said, Who told thee that thou wast naked? Hast thou eaten of the tree, whereof I commanded thee that thou shouldest not eat? And the man said, The woman whom thou gavest to be with me, she gave me of the tree, and I did eat. The LORD God said unto the woman, What is this that thou hast done? And the woman said, The serpent beguiled me, and I did eat. The LORD God said unto the serpent, Because thou hast done this, thou art cursed above all cattle, and above every beast of the field; upon thy belly shalt thou go, and dust shalt thou eat all the days of thy life: And I will put enmity between thee and the woman, and between thy seed and her seed; it shall bruise thy head, and thou shalt bruise his heel. Unto the woman he said, I will greatly multiply thy sorrow and thy conception; in sorrow thou shalt bring forth children; and thy desire shall be to thy husband, and he shall rule over thee. And unto Adam he said, Because thou hast hearkened unto the voice of thy wife, and hast eaten of the tree,"From the moment Adam and Eve disobeyed God by eating from the forbidden tree, the ground was cursed for Adam's sake. It would produce thorns and thistles, and Adam would have to toil for his food until his death, returning to the dust from which he was made. Adam named his wife Eve, as she would become the mother of all the living. God made garments of skins for Adam and Eve, clothing them for the first time.

God then expressed concern that humans had become like divine beings, knowing good and evil. To prevent them from eating from the tree of life and becoming immortal, God expelled them from the Garden of Eden. Cherubim and a flaming sword were placed to guard the way to the tree of life.

Adam and Eve had sons, Cain and Abel. Abel became a shepherd, and Cain a farmer. Both made offerings to God, but God favored Abel's offering. Cain, in jealousy, killed Abel. God punished Cain, making him a wanderer, but also placed a mark on him to prevent others from killing him. Cain moved to the land of Nod, east of Eden, where he had a son named Enoch and built a city named after him.

Cain's descendants included Lamech, who took two wives and boasted of his violence, claiming greater vengeance than Cain if harmed. Adam and Eve had another son, Seth, in place of Abel. Seth's son was Enos, marking the beginning of people calling upon the name of the LORD.

The genealogy of Adam through Seth is documented, emphasizing the longevity of these early humans. Adam lived 930 years, and his descendants also lived for several centuries, having many sons and daughters. This lineage underscores the early human connection to the divine and the beginnings of civilization as people began to call upon God."And there was not a man to till the ground. To Adam, because he listened to his wife and ate from the tree, the ground was cursed, and he would toil for food all the days of his life. Thorns and thistles it would bring forth, and he would eat the herb of the field. In the sweat of his face, he would eat bread until he returned to the ground, for out of it he was taken; for dust he was, and unto dust he shall return. Adam named his wife Eve, because she was the mother of all living. The LORD God made coats of skins for Adam and his wife and clothed them. The LORD God said, "Behold, the man has become like one of us, knowing good and evil; now, lest he put forth his hand and take also of the tree of life, and eat, and live forever." Therefore, the LORD God sent him forth from the Garden of Eden, to till the ground from whence he was taken. He drove out the man and placed at the east of the Garden of Eden Cherubims, and a flaming sword which turned every way, to keep the way of the tree of life. Adam knew Eve his wife; she conceived and bore Cain, saying, "I have gotten a man from the LORD." She again bore his brother Abel. Abel was a keeper of sheep, but Cain was a tiller of the ground. In the process of time, Cain brought an offering of the fruit of the ground to the LORD. Abel also brought of the firstlings of his flock and of the fat thereof. The LORD had respect unto Abel and his offering, but unto Cain and his offering, He had not respect. Cain was very wroth, and his countenance fell. The LORD said unto Cain, "Why art thou wroth? and why is thy countenance fallen? If thou doest well, shalt thou not be accepted? and if thou doest not well, sin lieth at the door. And unto thee shall be his desire, and thou shalt rule over him." Cain talked with Abel his brother, and when they were in the field, Cain rose up against Abel his brother and slew him. The LORD said unto Cain, "Where is Abel thy brother?" And he said, "I know not: Am I my brother's keeper?" And He said, "What hast thou done? the voice of thy brother's blood crieth unto me from the ground. And now art thou cursed from the earth, which hath opened her mouth to receive thy brother's blood from thy hand. When thou tillest the ground, it shall not henceforth yield unto thee her strength; a fugitive and a vagabond shalt thou be in the earth." Cain said unto the LORD, "My punishment is greater than I can bear. Behold, thou hast driven me out this day from the face of the earth; and from thy face shall I be hid; and I shall be a fugitive and a vagabond in the earth; and it shall come to pass, that every one that findeth me shall slay me." The LORD said unto him, "Therefore whosoever slayeth Cain, vengeance shall be taken on him sevenfold." And the LORD set a mark upon Cain, lest any finding him should kill him. Cain went out from the presence of the LORD and dwelt in the land of Nod, on the east of Eden. Cain knew his wife, and she conceived and bore Enoch; and he built a city and called the name of the city after the name of his son, Enoch. To Enoch was born Irad, and Irad begat Mehujael, and Mehujael begat Methusael, and Methusael begat Lamech. Lamech took unto him two wives: the name of the one was Adah, and the name of the other Zillah. Adah bore Jabal; he was the father of such as dwell in tents and have cattle. His brother's name was Jubal; he was the father of all such as handle the harp and organ. Zillah also bore Tubalcain, an instructor of every artificer in brass and iron, and the sister of Tubalcain was Naamah. Lamech said unto his wives, "Adah and Zillah, hear my voice; ye wives of Lamech, hearken unto my speech: for I have slain a man to my wounding, and a young man to my hurt. If Cain shall be avenged sevenfold, truly Lamech seventy and sevenfold." Adam knew his wife again, and she bore a son and called his name Seth: "For God," said she, "hath appointed me another seed instead of Abel, whom Cain slew." To Seth also there was born a son, and he called his name Enos: then began men to call upon the name of the LORD. This is the book of the generations of Adam. In the day that God created man, in the likeness of God made he him; male and female created he them, and blessed them, and called their name Adam, in the day when they were created. And Adam lived a hundred and thirty years and begat a son in his own likeness, after his image, and called his name Seth. And the days of Adam after he had begotten Seth were eight hundred years, and he begat sons and daughters. And all the days that Adam lived were nine hundred and thirty years, and he died. And Seth lived.From the moment Adam and Eve disobeyed God, the ground was cursed, producing thorns and thistles. Adam would toil for food until his death. He named his wife Eve, the mother of all living. God clothed them with garments of skins.

God expelled them from Eden to prevent them from eating from the tree of life and becoming immortal, placing Cherubim and a flaming sword to guard it.

Their sons, Cain and Abel, offered sacrifices to God, who favored Abel's. Jealous, Cain killed Abel. God punished Cain to wander but marked him to prevent his death. Cain moved to Nod, east of Eden, had a son, Enoch, and built a city named after him.

Cain's descendant, Lamech, took two wives and boasted of his violence. Adam and Eve's son, Seth, replaced Abel. Seth's son was Enos, beginning the tradition of calling upon the LORD.

The genealogy from Adam through Seth documents their longevity, with Adam living 930 years. This lineage highlights the early human-divine connection and the beginnings of civilization.

Seth lived 912 years, Enos 905, Cainan 910, Mahalaleel 895, Jared 962, and Methuselah 969, the longest. Lamech fathered Noah, who would comfort them from the cursed ground. Noah fathered Shem, Ham, and Japheth at 500 years old.

As humanity multiplied, the "sons of God" married the "daughters of men," leading to the Nephilim, heroes of old. God, grieved by mankind's wickedness, decided to wipe out all life, sparing only Noah, a righteous man.

God instructed Noah to build an ark for his family and pairs of every living creature to survive the impending flood, establishing a covenant with him. This marked the beginning of a new era, with Noah's obedience contrasting the corruption around him.Noah complied with all of God's commands, gathering pairs of every creature and all necessary food into the ark. God then instructed Noah and his family to enter the ark, as he was deemed righteous. They brought pairs of clean and unclean animals and birds into the ark as instructed. After seven days, the floodwaters came, lasting forty days and nights, covering even the highest mountains and destroying all living beings outside the ark. Noah and those with him in the ark were the only survivors.

The floodwaters prevailed for 150 days before God remembered Noah, causing the waters to recede. The ark eventually rested on the mountains of Ararat. As the waters decreased, Noah sent out a raven and then a dove to check for dry land. The dove returned with an olive leaf, signaling that the waters had abated. Noah and his family waited until the earth was dry before leaving the ark, marking the end of the flood and the beginning of a new chapter for humanity.After the flood, Noah removed the ark's covering and saw that the earth was dry. God then instructed Noah and his family to leave the ark, bringing all the animals with them to repopulate the earth. Noah built an altar to the Lord and offered sacrifices, which pleased God. God promised never to curse the ground again or destroy all living creatures as he had done with the flood. He established a covenant with Noah and his descendants, promising that a flood would never again destroy the earth. The sign of this covenant was a rainbow in the clouds.

God blessed Noah and his sons, instructing them to be fruitful and multiply. He gave them dominion over the animals and allowed them to eat meat, with the condition not to consume blood. God also established the sanctity of human life, decreeing that anyone who sheds human blood would be held accountable.

Noah's sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth, left the ark, and from them, the earth was repopulated. Noah became a farmer and planted a vineyard. After drinking wine and becoming drunk, Noah was dishonored by his son Ham, but Shem and Japheth acted respectfully. Noah cursed Ham's son Canaan and blessed Shem and Japheth for their actions. Noah lived for 350 years after the flood, making his total lifespan 950 years."dred and five years, and begat Enos. And Seth lived after he begat Enos eight hundred and seven years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Seth were nine hundred and twelve years, and he died. Enos lived ninety years, and begat Cainan. And Enos lived after he begat Cainan eight hundred and fifteen years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Enos were nine hundred and five years, and he died. Cainan lived seventy years and begat Mahalaleel. And Cainan lived after he begat Mahalaleel eight hundred and forty years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Cainan were nine hundred and ten years, and he died. Mahalaleel lived sixty and five years, and begat Jared. And Mahalaleel lived after he begat Jared eight hundred and thirty years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Mahalaleel were eight hundred ninety and five years, and he died. Jared lived an hundred sixty and two years, and he begat Enoch. And Jared lived after he begat Enoch eight hundred years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Jared were nine hundred sixty and two years, and he died. Enoch lived sixty and five years, and begat Methuselah. And Enoch walked with God after he begat Methuselah three hundred years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Enoch were three hundred sixty and five years. And Enoch walked with God, and he was not; for God took him. Methuselah lived an hundred eighty and seven years, and begat Lamech. And Methuselah lived after he begat Lamech seven hundred eighty and two years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Methuselah were nine hundred sixty and nine years, and he died. Lamech lived an hundred eighty and two years, and begat a son. And he called his name Noah, saying, This same shall comfort us concerning our work and toil of our hands, because of the ground which the LORD hath cursed. And Lamech lived after he begat Noah five hundred ninety and five years, and begat sons and daughters. And all the days of Lamech were seven hundred seventy and seven years, and he died. Noah was five hundred years old, and Noah begat Shem, Ham, and Japheth. And it came to pass, when men began to multiply on the face of the earth, and daughters were born unto them, That the sons of God saw the daughters of men that they were fair, and they took them wives of all which they chose. And the LORD said, My spirit shall not always strive with man, for that he also is flesh: yet his days shall be an hundred and twenty years. There were giants in the earth in those days; and also after that, when the sons of God came in unto the daughters of men, and they bare children to them, the same became mighty men which were of old, men of renown. And God saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, and that every imagination of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually. And it repented the LORD that he had made man on the earth, and it grieved him at his heart. And the LORD said, I will destroy man whom I have created from the face of the earth; both man, and beast, and the creeping thing, and the fowls of the air; for it repenteth me that I have made them. But Noah found grace in the eyes of the LORD. These are the generations of Noah: Noah was a just man and perfect in his generations, and Noah walked with God. And Noah begat three sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth. The earth also was corrupt before God, and the earth was filled with violence. And God looked upon the earth, and, behold, it was corrupt; for all flesh had corrupted his way upon the earth. And God said unto Noah, The end of all flesh is come before me; for the earth is filled with violence through them; and, behold, I will destroy them with the earth. Make thee an ark of gopher wood; rooms shalt thou make in the ark, and shalt pitch it within and without with pitch. And this is the fashion which thou shalt make it of: The length of the ark shall be three hundred cubits, the breadth of it fifty cubits, and the height of it thirty cubits. A window shalt thou make to the ark, and in a cubit shalt thou finish it above; and the door of the ark shalt thou set in the side thereof; with lower, second, and third stories shalt thou make it. And, behold, I, even I, do bring a flood of waters upon the earth, to destroy all flesh, wherein is the breath of life, from under heaven; and every thing that is in the earth shall die. But with thee will I establish my covenant; and thou shalt come into the ark, thou, and thy sons, and thy wife, and thy sons' wives with thee. And of every living thing of all flesh, two of every sort shalt thou bring into the ark, to keep them alive with thee; they shall be male and female. Of fowls after their kind, and of cattle."After the flood, Noah's sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth, had sons born to them. The descendants of Japheth included Gomer, Magog, Madai, Javan, Tubal, Meshech, and Tiras. The descendants of Ham included Cush, Mizraim, Phut, and Canaan. Cush's descendants were Seba, Havilah, Sabtah, Raamah, and Sabtechah. Cush also begat Nimrod, who became a mighty hunter and established his kingdom in Babel, Erech, Accad, and Calneh, in the land of Shinar. From there, Asshur built Nineveh and other cities. Mizraim begat Ludim, Anamim, Lehabim, Naphtuhim, Pathrusim, Casluhim, and Caphtorim. Canaan's descendants included Sidon, Heth, the Jebusite, the Amorite, the Girgasite, the Hivite, the Arkite, the Sinite, the Arvadite, the Zemarite, and the Hamathite. The Canaanites' territory extended from Sidon to Gaza and towards Sodom, Gomorrah, Admah, and Zeboim.

Shem's descendants included Elam, Asshur, Arphaxad, Lud, and Aram. Arphaxad begat Salah, who begat Eber. Eber had two sons, Peleg, in whose time the earth was divided, and Joktan. Joktan begat Almodad, Sheleph, Hazarmaveth, Jerah, Hadoram, Uzal, Diklah, Obal, Abimael, Sheba, Ophir, Havilah, and Jobab. Their territory stretched from Mesha to Sephar, a mountain of the east.

The whole earth spoke one language. As people moved eastward, they settled in the land of Shinar and decided to build a city and a tower reaching to heaven to make a name for themselves. God observed their city and tower and confused their language to scatter them across the earth. This place was called Babel because there God confused the language of the whole earth.

Shem lived 500 years after he begat Arphaxad, and Arphaxad lived 403 years after he begat Salah. Salah lived 403 years after he begat Eber, and Eber lived 430 years after he begat Peleg. Peleg lived 209 years, indicating the generations that followed.After Reu lived 209 years, he had sons and daughters. Reu was 32 when he fathered Serug, and lived another 207 years after that, having more children. Serug was 30 when Nahor was born, and after that, lived 200 years, fathering more children. Nahor was 29 when he fathered Terah, and lived another 119 years, having more sons and daughters. Terah was 70 when he had Abram, Nahor, and Haran. Haran fathered Lot but died in Ur of the Chaldees, his birthplace. Abram married Sarai, and Nahor married Milcah, Haran's daughter. Sarai was barren. Terah, with Abram, Sarai, and Lot, left Ur for Canaan but settled in Haran, where Terah died at 205.

God told Abram to leave his home for a land He would show, promising to make him a great nation, bless him, and bless or curse others through him. At 75, Abram, with Sarai and Lot, left Haran for Canaan, arriving in Sichem at the Moreh plain. There, God promised the land to Abram's descendants, and Abram built an altar. Abram then moved near Bethel, built another altar, and called on God. He journeyed south, but a famine led him to Egypt. Fearing for his life because of Sarai's beauty, Abram asked her to say she was his sister. Pharaoh took Sarai into his house, treating Abram well until God plagued Pharaoh's house because of Sarai. Pharaoh, realizing the truth, sent them away with their possessions.

Abram returned to Canaan, wealthy in livestock and gold. He and Lot, also wealthy, found the land couldn't support both their flocks. This caused strife between their herdsmen."After their kind, of every creeping thing of the earth after his kind, two of every sort shall come unto thee, to keep them alive. And take thou unto thee of all food that is eaten, and thou shalt gather it to thee; and it shall be for food for thee, and for them. Thus did Noah; according to all that God commanded him, so did he. And the LORD said unto Noah, Come thou and all thy house into the ark; for thee have I seen righteous before me in this generation. Of every clean beast thou shalt take to thee by sevens, the male and his female: and of beasts that are not clean by two, the male and his female. Of fowls also of the air by sevens, the male and the female; to keep seed alive upon the face of all the earth. For yet seven days, and I will cause it to rain upon the earth forty days and forty nights; and every living substance that I have made will I destroy from off the face of the earth. And Noah went in, and his sons, and his wife, and his sons' wives with him, into the ark, because of the waters of the flood. Of clean beasts, and of beasts that are not clean, and of fowls, and of everything that creepeth upon the earth, there went in two and two unto Noah into the ark, the male and the female, as God had commanded Noah. And it came to pass after seven days, that the waters of the flood were upon the earth. In the six hundredth year of Noah's life, in the second month, the seventeenth day of the month, the same day were all the fountains of the great deep broken up, and the windows of heaven were opened. And the rain was upon the earth forty days and forty nights. In the selfsame day entered Noah, and Shem, and Ham, and Japheth, the sons of Noah, and Noah's wife, and the three wives of his sons with them, into the ark; They, and every beast after his kind, and all the cattle after their kind, and every creeping thing that creepeth upon the earth after his kind, and every fowl after his kind, every bird of every sort. And they went in unto Noah into the ark, two and two of all flesh, wherein is the breath of life. And they that went in, went in male and female of all flesh, as God had commanded him: and the LORD shut him in. And the flood was forty days upon the earth; and the waters increased, and bare up the ark, and it was lift up above the earth. And the waters prevailed, and were increased greatly upon the earth; and the ark went upon the face of the waters. And the waters prevailed exceedingly upon the earth; and all the high hills, that were under the whole heaven, were covered. Fifteen cubits upward did the waters prevail; and the mountains were covered. And all flesh died that moved upon the earth, both of fowl, and of cattle, and of beast, and of every creeping thing that creepeth upon the earth, and every man: All in whose nostrils was the breath of life, of all that was in the dry land, died. And every living substance was destroyed which was upon the face of the ground, both man, and cattle, and the creeping things, and the fowl of the heaven; and they were destroyed from the earth: and Noah only remained alive, and they that were with him in the ark. And the waters prevailed upon the earth a hundred and fifty days. And God remembered Noah, and every living thing, and all the cattle that was with him in the ark: and God made a wind to pass over the earth, and the waters assuaged; The fountains also of the deep and the windows of heaven were stopped, and the rain from heaven was restrained; And the waters returned from off the earth continually: and after the end of the hundred and fifty days the waters were abated. And the ark rested in the seventh month, on the seventeenth day of the month, upon the mountains of Ararat. And the waters decreased continually until the tenth month: in the tenth month, on the first day of the month, were the tops of the mountains seen. And it came to pass at the end of forty days, that Noah opened the window of the ark which he had made: And he sent forth a raven, which went forth to and fro, until the waters were dried up from off the earth. Also he sent forth a dove from him, to see if the waters were abated from off the face of the ground; But the dove found no rest for the sole of her foot, and she returned unto him into the ark, for the waters were on the face of the whole earth: then he put forth his hand, and took her, and pulled her in unto him into the ark. And he stayed yet other seven days; and again he sent forth the dove out of the ark; And the dove came in to him in the evening; and, lo, in her mouth was an olive leaf pluckt off: so Noah knew that the waters were abated from off the earth. In the time of kings Amraphel, Arioch, Chedorlaomer, and Tidal, a war broke out against the kings of Sodom, Gomorrah, Admah, Zeboiim, and Bela (Zoar). After serving Chedorlaomer for twelve years, they rebelled. Chedorlaomer and allies defeated various peoples and returned, defeating the kings of Sodom and Gomorrah in the Vale of Siddim, taking Lot, Abram's nephew, captive. Abram, informed by an escapee, armed his men, pursued the captors, and rescued Lot, his goods, and other captives. Melchizedek, king of Salem and priest of the most high God, blessed Abram, who gave him a tenth of the spoils. In the six hundredth and first year, on the first day of the first month, the waters were dried up from off the earth; Noah then removed the covering of the ark, looked out, and saw that the ground was dry. By the second month, on the twenty-seventh day, the earth was completely dry. God then instructed Noah to leave the ark with his family and all the living creatures, so they could multiply and fill the earth. Noah and his family, along with all the animals, left the ark. Noah built an altar to the LORD and offered burnt offerings. The LORD, pleased by the offerings, promised never to curse the ground again for man's sake or destroy every living thing as He had done. While the earth remains, there will be planting and harvest, cold and heat, summer and winter, day and night.

God blessed Noah and his sons, instructing them to be fruitful and multiply. He established a covenant with Noah, his descendants, and every living creature, promising never to destroy the earth with a flood again. As a sign of this covenant, God set a rainbow in the clouds. Noah's sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth, left the ark, and from them, the earth was repopulated. Noah became a farmer and planted a vineyard. After drinking wine from his vineyard, Noah became drunk and was uncovered within his tent. Ham saw his father's nakedness and told his brothers, who respectfully covered their father without looking at him. When Noah awoke and learned what Ham had done, he cursed Ham's son Canaan to be a servant of servants to his brothers. Noah blessed the LORD God of Shem and declared that Canaan would be the servant of Shem and Japheth. Noah lived for three hundred and fifty years after the flood, making his total lifespan nine hundred and fifty years.After these events, the LORD spoke to Abram in a vision, reassuring him not to fear, for He would be Abram's shield and great reward. Abram, concerned about having no children to inherit his legacy, voiced his worry to God, mentioning Eliezer of Damascus as his potential heir. God responded, promising Abram a biological heir and a multitude of descendants, as numerous as the stars. Abram's faith in the LORD was acknowledged as righteousness.

God further promised Abram the land from the river of Egypt to the Euphrates, including territories of various peoples. Despite Sarai, Abram's wife, being barren, she suggested Abram have a child with her Egyptian maid, Hagar. Abram agreed, leading to Hagar's pregnancy and subsequent mistreatment by Sarai, causing Hagar to flee. An angel of the LORD encountered Hagar in the wilderness, instructing her to return and submit to Sarai, promising her descendants would be too numerous to count and foretelling the birth of her son, Ishmael.

Abram was 86 years old when Ishmael was born. When Abram was 99, God appeared to him, reaffirming His covenant, promising to multiply Abram's descendants, and instructing him to walk faithfully.After these events, God spoke to Abram, promising him a multitude of descendants and changing his name to Abraham, signifying "a father of many nations." God established an everlasting covenant with Abraham and his descendants, promising them the land of Canaan and requiring circumcision as a sign of this covenant. Every male in Abraham's household, including himself and his son Ishmael, was circumcised in accordance with God's command.

God also changed Sarai's name to Sarah and promised that she would bear a son, Isaac, with whom God would establish His covenant. Abraham laughed at the thought, considering their old age, but God reassured him. After the flood, Noah's sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth, had sons. The descendants of Japheth included Gomer, Magog, Madai, Javan, Tubal, Meshech, and Tiras. The descendants of Gomer were Ashkenaz, Riphath, and Togarmah, and the descendants of Javan were Elishah, Tarshish, Kittim, and Dodanim. These families spread out into their own lands and nations, each with its own language.

The sons of Ham included Cush, Mizraim, Phut, and Canaan. Cush's descendants were Seba, Havilah, Sabtah, Raamah, and Sabtechah, and Raamah's were Sheba and Dedan. Cush also begat Nimrod, who became a mighty hunter and established his kingdom in Babel, Erech, Accad, and Calneh, in the land of Shinar. From there, Asshur built Nineveh and other cities. Mizraim begat the Ludim, Anamim, Lehabim, Naphtuhim, Pathrusim, Casluhim (from whom the Philistines came), and Caphtorim. Canaan's descendants included Sidon, Heth, the Jebusite, Amorite, Girgasite, Hivite, Arkite, Sinite, Arvadite, Zemarite, and Hamathite, and their territory stretched from Sidon to Gaza, and towards Sodom, Gomorrah, Admah, and Zeboim.

Shem, the elder brother of Japheth, also had sons, including Elam, Asshur, Arphaxad, Lud, and Aram, with Aram's children being Uz, Hul, Gether, and Mash. Arphaxad begat Salah, who begat Eber, from whom came Peleg (in his time the earth was divided) and Joktan. These are the families of Noah's sons, by their generations, in their nations, and from these, the nations were divided on the earth after the flood. The whole earth used one language until people moved eastward to Shinar, where they decided to build a city and a tower reaching to heaven to make a name for themselves. God, observing their city and tower, confused their language to prevent them from understanding each other, causing them to scatter across the earth. This place was called Babel. Despite Abraham's plea for Ishmael, God confirmed that His covenant would be with Isaac, though He also promised to make Ishmael into a great nation.

Later, the LORD appeared to Abraham by the oaks of Mamre. As Abraham sat at the entrance of his tent, he saw three men standing near. He hurried to greet them, offering hospitality and refreshment. Abraham and Sarah prepared food for their guests, during which the visitors reiterated the promise of Sarah bearing a son. Sarah laughed at the idea, given her and Abraham's advanced age.

Sarah doubted, questioning the possibility of having a child in her old age. The LORD questioned Abraham about Sarah's laughter and disbelief, affirming that nothing is too hard for the LORD and promising Sarah a son at the appointed time. Sarah, out of fear, denied laughing, but the LORD knew the truth.

The men set out towards Sodom, and the LORD contemplated whether to share His plans for Sodom with Abraham, acknowledging Abraham's future significance and his role in leading his family in the ways of the LORD. The LORD revealed His intention to verify the outcry against Sodom and Gomorrah for their grievous sin.

Abraham then interceded for Sodom, questioning if the LORD would spare the city if fifty righteous people were found within it. The LORD agreed to spare the city for the sake of fifty righteous. Abraham continued to plead for mercy, lowering the number incrementally until the LORD agreed to not destroy the city if even ten righteous people were found. After their conversation, the LORD left, and Abraham returned home.

Two angels arrived in Sodom, and Lot, Abraham's nephew, offered them hospitality. Despite the angels' initial refusal, Lot insisted, and they entered his home. However, the men of Sodom surrounded Lot's house, demanding the guests be brought out to them. Lot pleaded with them to not act wickedly and offered his daughters instead, but the men refused and threatened Lot. The angels intervened, pulling Lot inside and striking the men with blindness to protect Lot's household. They then instructed Lot to gather his family and leave the city to escape the impending destruction.The Canaanite and the Perizzite dwelled in the land. Abram proposed to Lot to avoid strife between their herdsmen by separating, offering Lot the choice of direction, ensuring peace as they were brethren. Lot chose the well-watered plain of Jordan, moving east, while Abram stayed in Canaan. The men of Sodom were notably wicked. God then promised Abram all the land he could see, promising his descendants would be as numerous as the dust of the earth. Abram moved to Hebron, building an altar to the Lord.

In the time of Amraphel king of Shinar, Arioch king of Ellasar, Chedorlaomer king of Elam, and Tidal king of nations, a war broke out against the kings of Sodom and Gomorrah among others. After serving Chedorlaomer for twelve years, they rebelled. Chedorlaomer and his allies defeated several territories, including the Rephaims and the Amalekites. The kings of Sodom and Gomorrah were defeated in the vale of Siddim, filled with slime pits, leading to their defeat and capture of Lot, Abram's nephew.

Abram, upon hearing of Lot's capture, led a successful rescue mission with his trained men, defeating Chedorlaomer's forces and recovering all the captives and goods. Melchizedek, king of Salem and priest of the most high God, blessed Abram, who gave him a tenth of everything. The king of Sodom offered Abram the goods, but Abram refused, not wanting to be said to have been made rich by the king, except for what his men had consumed and the share for his allies, Aner, Eshcol, and Mamre.The angels warned Lot to escape Sodom with his family as they were sent to destroy it due to the city's wickedness. Despite Lot's warnings, his sons-in-law did not believe the imminent danger. The next morning, the angels urged Lot to take his wife and daughters and flee without looking back to avoid being consumed by the city's destruction. Lot hesitated, so the angels physically led them out of the city. Lot requested to flee to a nearby smaller city, Zoar, instead of the mountains for fear of harm. The request was granted, and as they reached Zoar, the LORD rained brimstone and fire on Sodom and Gomorrah, destroying everything. Lot's wife looked back and turned into a pillar of salt. Abraham observed the destruction from afar, and God remembered Abraham, sparing Lot as a result.

Lot and his daughters, fearing to stay in Zoar, lived in a cave. Believing they were the last people on Earth, his daughters decided to preserve their lineage through their father. They intoxicated Lot on two consecutive nights, and each daughter conceived a son, Moab and Ben-ammi, ancestors of the Moabites and Ammonites.

Abraham moved to the region between Kadesh and Shur and claimed Sarah was his sister. Abimelech, king of Gerar, took Sarah, but God warned him in a dream that Sarah was Abraham's wife. Abimelech, who had not touched Sarah, argued his innocence. God acknowledged Abimelech's integrity, instructing him to return Sarah and have Abraham pray for him to avoid death. Abimelech complied, questioning Abraham's actions before returning Sarah.After these events, the LORD spoke to Abram in a vision, reassuring him not to fear, for He was Abram's protector and great reward. Abram, concerned about his lack of an heir since Eliezer of Damascus stood to inherit his estate, voiced his worry to God. The LORD responded, promising Abram that his own offspring would be his heir and that his descendants would be as numerous as the stars in the sky. Abram believed the LORD, and this faith was credited to him as righteousness.

The LORD further promised to give Abram's descendants the land from the river of Egypt to the Euphrates, including territories of various peoples. Despite Abram's wife Sarai being barren, she suggested Abram have a child with her Egyptian maid, Hagar. Abram agreed, and Hagar conceived, leading to tension between her and Sarai. Sarai mistreated Hagar, causing her to flee. An angel of the LORD found Hagar in the wilderness, instructing her to return and submit to Sarai, promising her descendants would be too numerous to count and that her son, to be named Ishmael, would live in conflict with his relatives.

Hagar returned, bore Ishmael to Abram when he was eighty-six. When Abram was ninety-nine, the LORD appeared again, reaffirming His covenant, promising to make Abram's descendants numerous and changing Abram's name to Abraham, signifying "father of many nations."Abimelech called Abraham, questioning him about his actions that brought potential sin upon Abimelech's kingdom by claiming Sarah was his sister. Abraham explained he feared for his life due to the perceived lack of godliness in the area. Despite Sarah being his half-sister, Abraham had her claim to be his sister to protect himself. Abimelech returned Sarah to Abraham, compensating him with livestock and servants, and offered land for him to dwell in. He also gave Sarah silver as a symbol of her innocence. Abraham prayed for Abimelech, and God healed his household, allowing them to bear children again, as their ability had been divinely closed because of Sarah.

The LORD fulfilled His promise to Sarah, and she bore Abraham a son, Isaac, at the appointed time. Abraham circumcised Isaac as commanded by God. Sarah expressed joy that she could bear a child at her old age, making a feast when Isaac was weaned. However, tension arose when Sarah saw Ishmael, Hagar's son with Abraham, mocking. She demanded Abraham send Hagar and Ishmael away, causing distress to Abraham. God instructed Abraham to listen to Sarah, promising that Ishmael would also become a great nation. Abraham sent Hagar and Ishmael away, and when they ran out of water, God provided for them and promised to make Ishmael a great nation.

Abimelech, recognizing God's favor upon Abraham, sought a treaty, ensuring kindness between their descendants. Abraham agreed but rebuked Abimelech over a disputed well, which they resolved by making a covenant, solidifying their peaceful relations.In a profound moment of covenant, God spoke to Abram, declaring that his name would henceforth be Abraham, symbolizing his destiny as the father of many nations. This covenant extended beyond Abraham to his descendants, promising them a multitude of nations and kings. God pledged an everlasting covenant with Abraham and his offspring, promising the land of Canaan as an everlasting possession and affirming His role as their God.

God introduced the practice of circumcision as a sign of this covenant, mandating it for every male in Abraham's lineage and household, marking an eternal bond between them and God. This rite was to be performed on the eighth day of a male's life, signifying their inclusion in God's covenant.

The narrative then shifts to God's promise to Abraham and Sarah, who were advanced in age, that they would bear a son named Isaac. This announcement brought a mix of disbelief and joy, leading Abraham to laugh and question the possibility due to their old age. Despite Abraham's plea for Ishmael, God affirmed that His covenant would be established through Isaac, born to Sarah the following year, while also blessing Ishmael to become a great nation.

Following God's departure, Abraham obediently circumcised every male in his household, including himself and his son Ishmael, aligning his family with God's covenant.

The story continues with the LORD appearing to Abraham as he sat at the entrance of his tent. Upon seeing three men, Abraham showed great hospitality, offering them water, rest, and a meal. This encounter led to the reaffirmation of the promise that Sarah would bear a son, a statement overheard by Sarah, leading her to laugh in disbelief due to her and Abraham's old age.Abraham set seven ewe lambs aside as a witness that he had dug a well, leading to the naming of the place Beersheba, where he and Abimelech made a covenant. Abraham then planted a grove in Beersheba, calling on the name of the LORD, the everlasting God, and lived in the Philistines' land for many days. God tested Abraham by asking him to sacrifice his son Isaac on Moriah. Abraham prepared for the sacrifice, but an angel of the LORD stopped him, providing a ram as an alternative offering. This act confirmed Abraham's fear of God, leading to a blessing that his descendants would be as numerous as the stars and possess their enemies' gates. All nations would be blessed through Abraham's seed due to his obedience. Abraham returned to Beersheba with his young men.

It was later reported to Abraham that his brother Nahor's wife, Milcah, had borne children, listing their names and the names of Nahor's concubine Reumah's children. Sarah died at the age of 127 in Hebron, and Abraham negotiated with the Hittites to buy a burial site, emphasizing his status as a stranger and sojourner among them. The Hittites recognized Abraham as a mighty prince and offered him a choice of sepulchres to bury Sarah, leading to Abraham's purchase of the cave of Machpelah for her burial.In a moment of disbelief, Sarah laughed to herself at the idea of bearing a child in her old age, questioning the possibility given both her and Abraham's advanced years. The LORD, aware of Sarah's laughter and doubt, questioned Abraham about it, emphasizing that nothing is too hard for the LORD and promising Sarah would have a son at the appointed time. Sarah, out of fear, denied laughing, but the LORD knew the truth.

As the men prepared to leave, they looked toward Sodom, and Abraham accompanied them to set them on their way. The LORD contemplated whether to share with Abraham the impending judgment on Sodom and Gomorrah, recognizing Abraham's future significance and his role in leading his family in the ways of the LORD. Deciding to reveal His plans, the LORD explained the great sin of Sodom and Gomorrah and His intention to verify the cries against the cities.

Abraham, standing before the LORD, pleaded for the cities, questioning if the LORD would spare them if fifty righteous people were found within. The LORD agreed to spare the cities for the sake of fifty righteous. Abraham continued to negotiate, lowering the number from fifty to ten, with the LORD agreeing each time not to destroy the cities if even a small number of righteous people were found.

The narrative then shifts to Lot in Sodom, who welcomed two angels into his home with great hospitality, despite the city's inhabitants demanding to harm the visitors. Lot offered his daughters to protect his guests, highlighting the depth of the city's wickedness. The men of Sodom attempted to break into Lot's home, but the angels protected Lot, striking the attackers with blindness and urging Lot to gather his family to leave the city, signaling the impending judgment on Sodom and Gomorrah.Abraham requested Ephron the Hittite to sell him the cave of Machpelah for a burial site. Ephron offered the cave and the field to Abraham at no cost, but Abraham insisted on paying. Eventually, Ephron agreed to sell it for four hundred shekels of silver, a price Abraham paid in front of witnesses, securing the land as a burial place for Sarah and establishing ownership among the Hittites.

After Sarah's burial, Abraham, now old and blessed by the LORD in every way, tasked his eldest servant with finding a wife for Isaac, his son, but not from the Canaanites. Instead, the servant was to go to Abraham's homeland to find a suitable wife. Abraham made the servant swear an oath to this effect, emphasizing that Isaac must not return to Abraham's homeland.

The servant took ten camels and all necessary goods, traveling to Mesopotamia, to the city of Nahor. At a well outside the city, he prayed for a sign from God to identify the right woman for Isaac. Before he finished praying, Rebekah appeared. She was very beautiful, a virgin, and related to Abraham. She offered the servant water and also drew water for his camels, fulfilling the conditions of the servant's prayer as a sign from God that she was the chosen one for Isaac.Abraham's servant, after witnessing Rebekah's kindness and fulfilling the conditions of his prayer, gifts her with a golden earring and bracelets, inquiring about her family and if they could accommodate him. Rebekah identifies herself as Bethuel's daughter, offering lodging. The servant worships the LORD, grateful for the guidance to his master's kin. Rebekah informs her family, leading her brother Laban to welcome the servant into their home.

The servant refuses to eat before explaining his mission, revealing his identity as Abraham's servant and recounting Abraham's blessings and the task of finding a wife for Isaac from his kin, not the Canaanites. He describes the sign he prayed for at the well and how Rebekah met all the conditions, proving she was the chosen one for Isaac.

Laban and Bethuel acknowledge the match as God's will, consenting to Rebekah's marriage to Isaac. The servant worships the LORD, presents gifts to Rebekah and her family, and requests to return to Abraham. Despite her family's wish for her to stay longer, the servant insists on departing immediately with Rebekah.In a moment of urgency, the angels warned Lot to escape Sodom with his family to avoid the impending destruction. Despite Lot's hesitation and his sons-in-law's disbelief, the angels led Lot, his wife, and his daughters out of the city, instructing them not to look back. Lot pleaded for permission to flee to a smaller nearby city, Zoar, instead of the mountains to ensure his safety. The LORD agreed, and as Lot reached Zoar, Sodom and Gomorrah were destroyed with brimstone and fire from heaven. Lot's wife, disobeying the command not to look back, turned into a pillar of salt.

Abraham, witnessing the destruction from afar, remembered the LORD's mercy in saving Lot. Lot, fearing to stay in Zoar, moved to the mountains with his daughters. In isolation, his daughters, believing they were the last people on Earth, intoxicated Lot to conceive children by him, leading to the origins of the Moabites and Ammonites.

To rectify the situation, Abimelech returned Sarah to Abraham, compensated him with livestock and servants, and offered him land to dwell in. He also gave Sarah silver as a symbol of her vindication. Following Abraham's prayer, God healed Abimelech's household, allowing them to bear children again, as their ability had been divinely obstructed due to the situation with Sarah.

The narrative then shifts to the fulfillment of God's promise to Sarah and Abraham with the birth of Isaac. Abraham faithfully followed God's command to circumcise Isaac. Sarah expressed her joy and amazement at the birth of her son in her old age. However, tension arose when Sarah demanded the expulsion of Hagar and her son Ishmael, leading to their departure into the wilderness. In their despair, God reassured Hagar about Ishmael's future and provided for their immediate needs, promising that Ishmael would father a nation.

Abraham's interactions with Abimelech continued with a dispute over a well, which was resolved by a treaty, reaffirming Abraham's right to reside in the land and ensuring mutual respect between the two parties. This section of the narrative highlights themes of fear, deception, divine intervention, fulfillment of promises, and the establishment of covenants, reflecting the complex relationships between humans and the divine, as well as the importance of faith, obedience, and reconciliation.Abraham set seven ewe lambs aside as a witness to his ownership of a well, leading to a covenant with Abimelech at Beersheba. This act confirmed Abraham's fear of God, leading to a divine promise of abundant blessings and descendants as numerous as the stars and sand. Abraham's obedience was said to bring blessings to all nations through his seed.

After these events, Abraham returned to Beersheba, where he lived. News came to Abraham of his brother Nahor's descendants, including Rebekah. The servant took ten camels and journeyed to the city of Nahor, where he prayed for a sign from God to identify the right woman. He inquired about her family and if there was room at her father's house for them to stay. Rebekah identified herself as the daughter of Bethuel, son of Milcah and Nahor, and assured him there was enough straw, provender, and room to lodge.

Jacob rebuked them, fearing retaliation from neighboring tribes. They justified their actions, citing Dinah's dishonor. God instructed Jacob to return to Bethel and build an altar. They journeyed to Bethel, where Jacob built an altar, calling it Elbethel, in gratitude for God's guidance and protection.Reuben intervened when his brothers plotted to kill Joseph, suggesting they cast him into a pit instead, sparing his life with the intention of rescuing him later. However, while Reuben was away, the others sold Joseph to Ishmaelite traders heading to Egypt. Upon discovering Joseph's absence, Reuben was distraught. The brothers then deceived their father Jacob, presenting Joseph's blood-stained coat as evidence of his supposed death by a wild animal, leading Jacob into deep mourning.

Meanwhile, the narrative shifts to Judah, who married a Canaanite woman and had three sons. The eldest, Er, was killed by the Lord for his wickedness, and Onan, the second son, also died by divine action for refusing to provide offspring for his brother's widow, Tamar. Judah promised Tamar his youngest son, Shelah, but failed to fulfill this promise. After Judah's wife died, Tamar disguised herself as a prostitute and seduced Judah, resulting in pregnancy. This act was part of her plan to secure her place within the family lineage.Jacob learned of Dinah's defilement by Shechem, son of Hamor, while his sons were in the field. Hamor sought to negotiate with Jacob for Dinah's marriage to Shechem, offering marriages between their peoples and land for settlement. Shechem, expressing his love for Dinah, agreed to any dowry. Jacob's sons deceitfully agreed, requiring all males in Shechem's city to be circumcised. On the third day post-circumcision, Simeon and Levi killed all the males, including Hamor and Shechem, and rescued Dinah. Jacob's sons then plundered the city, taking livestock, wealth, and captives. Jacob rebuked them, fearing retaliation from neighboring tribes. They justified their actions, citing Dinah's dishonor. God instructed Jacob to return to Bethel and build an altar. Jacob commanded his household to discard foreign gods and purify themselves. They journeyed to Bethel, where Jacob built an altar, calling it Elbethel, in gratitude for God's guidance and protection. Deborah, Rebekah's nurse, died and was buried beneath Bethel. God appeared to Jacob again, blessing him and renaming him Israel, promising that a nation and a company of nations would come from him, and kings would descend from him. The land given to Abraham and Isaac was reaffirmed to Jacob and his descendants. Jacob set up a pillar at the place where God spoke to him, pouring a drink offering and oil on it, and named the place Bethel. Rachel died giving birth to Benjamin and was buried on the way to Ephrath, which is Bethlehem. Jacob set a pillar upon her grave. Reuben lay with Bilhah, his father's concubine, which Jacob heard of. The narrative lists the sons of Jacob, born to him in Padanaram, and concludes with Jacob's return to his father Isaac in Mamre, Hebron, where Isaac died at 180 years old, and was buried by his sons Esau and Jacob. The text then transitions to the generations of Esau, detailing his wives, sons, and the dukes that came from him, highlighting the separate paths Jacob and Esau took, with Esau moving to Mount Seir, illustrating the fulfillment of God's promise to Abraham and Isaac through their descendants.Judah, unable to find the woman he thought was a prostitute, decided to let her keep the items he had given as a pledge to avoid shame. However, three months later, he learned that Tamar, his daughter-in-law, was pregnant through prostitution. Judah recognized his items and admitted Tamar was more righteous than he for not giving her to his son Shelah. Tamar gave birth to twins, Perez and Zerah, with Perez being born first after a midwife marked Zerah with a scarlet thread for appearing first.

The narrative then returns to Joseph in Egypt, who was sold to Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh. The Lord's presence made Joseph successful, and Potiphar noticed this, making Joseph overseer of his house. The Lord blessed Potiphar's household because of Joseph. However, Potiphar's wife desired Joseph, but he refused her advances, citing his loyalty to Potiphar and God. When she falsely accused him of trying to lie with her, Potiphar had Joseph imprisoned. Yet, the Lord was with Joseph in prison, granting him favor with the prison keeper, who put Joseph in charge of the other prisoners.The LORD was with Joseph, making everything he did prosper. After some time, the king of Egypt's butler and baker offended him and were imprisoned where Joseph was held. The captain of the guard assigned Joseph to serve them. Both officials had dreams on the same night, each with its own meaning. When Joseph saw they were troubled by their dreams, he offered to interpret them, saying interpretations belong to God.

The butler's dream involved a vine with three branches that budded and produced ripe grapes, which he pressed into Pharaoh's cup. Joseph interpreted that the three branches represented three days, after which the butler would be restored to his position and serve Pharaoh as before. Joseph asked the butler to remember him and mention him to Pharaoh to help secure his release, as he was unjustly imprisoned.

The baker, encouraged by the positive interpretation, shared his dream with Joseph, which involved three baskets of baked goods for Pharaoh, which birds ate. Joseph interpreted that in three days, the baker would be executed, and birds would eat his flesh. The interpretations came true: the butler was restored to his position, but the baker was hanged. However, the butler forgot about Joseph.

Two years later, Pharaoh had troubling dreams that none could interpret. The butler then remembered Joseph and his accurate interpretations. Pharaoh sent for Joseph, who was then brought from the dungeon to interpret Pharaoh's dreams.The dukes of the Horites in the land of Edom included Zibeon, Anah, Dishon, Ezer, and Dishan. Joseph suggested appointing a wise overseer for Egypt and collecting a fifth of the harvest during the seven plentiful years to prepare for the famine. Pharaoh then commanded all his people to throw every Hebrew son born into the river but to let every daughter live.

In this context, a Levite woman bore a son, hid him for three months, and then placed him in a basket on the river's edge, where he was found and adopted by Pharaoh's daughter, who named him Moses. When Moses grew up, he saw the suffering of his people and killed an Egyptian who was beating a Hebrew. Fearing for his life after the incident became known, Moses fled to Midian.In Midian, God instructed Moses to return to Egypt, promising that the Israelites would leave with silver, gold, and clothing from their Egyptian neighbors. Moses doubted his ability to convince the Israelites and Pharaoh of God's message. God then gave Moses signs to prove His power: turning a rod into a serpent, making Moses' hand leprous and then healing it, and turning river water into blood.

Despite these signs, Moses expressed concern about his eloquence. God reassured him, stating He would help Moses speak and also appointed Aaron, Moses' brother, as his spokesman. God commanded Moses to perform wonders before Pharaoh but warned that He would harden Pharaoh's heart.

Upon returning to Egypt, Moses and Aaron gathered the Israelite elders, sharing God's promises and performing the signs, which led the people to believe and worship God. Moses and Aaron then confronted Pharaoh, demanding the release of the Israelites to worship God in the wilderness. Pharaoh's initial response was dismissive, questioning who the Lord was and refusing to let the Israelites go.In Midian, Moses encountered the seven daughters of the priest of Midian at a well. He helped them water their flock, defending them against shepherds who tried to drive them away. Their father, Reuel, invited Moses to stay, and he eventually married Zipporah, one of the daughters, with whom he had a son named Gershom. During this time, the king of Egypt died, and the Israelites' cries of suffering reached God, who remembered His covenant with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob.

God appeared to Moses in a burning bush that was not consumed by the fire on Mount Horeb, the mountain of God. He called Moses to lead the Israelites out of Egypt, promising to be with him. God revealed Himself as "I AM THAT I AM" and instructed Moses to gather the elders of Israel and go to Pharaoh to demand their release, promising signs and wonders to compel Pharaoh to let His people go. God assured Moses of His support and the eventual freedom of the Israelites, promising them a land flowing with milk and honey.Pharaoh questioned Moses and Aaron's demand to let the Israelites go, expressing ignorance of the Lord and refusing their request. Moses and Aaron pleaded for a three-day journey into the desert to sacrifice to their God, warning of divine retribution if denied. Pharaoh, unmoved, accused them of distracting the people from their work and increased their labor by no longer providing straw for brick-making, yet demanding the same output. This decree forced the Israelites to scavenge for straw, exacerbating their hardship. When the Israelite overseers, unable to meet the quotas, protested to Pharaoh, he dismissed them as idle and maintained his demands. The overseers blamed Moses and Aaron for their worsened condition, fearing Pharaoh's wrath. Moses, distressed by the increased suffering of his people, questioned God's intentions. God reassured Moses, promising deliverance through His power and reaffirming His covenant with the Israelites. Despite Moses' efforts, the Israelites, broken in spirit, did not listen. God then instructed Moses to confront Pharaoh again, emphasizing the divine mandate to release the Israelites. Despite Moses' self-doubt due to his lack of eloquence, God reaffirmed the mission for both Moses and Aaron, setting the stage for the eventual liberation of the Israelites from Egypt.In Midian, God instructed Moses to return to Egypt, promising that the Egyptians who sought his life were dead. This ordinance was to be observed forever, and when questioned by future generations, they were to explain it commemorates the LORD's Passover, when He spared the Israelites in Egypt but smote the Egyptians.
