The LORD instructed Moses to stretch out his hand over the sea to divide it, allowing the Israelites to cross on dry ground. He also said He would harden the Egyptians' hearts to follow, gaining honor upon Pharaoh and his forces. The angel of God and the pillar of cloud moved to protect the Israelites, creating darkness for the Egyptians and light for the Israelites, preventing the two camps from coming near each other. Moses stretched his hand over the sea, and the LORD caused the sea to part with a strong east wind, creating dry land. The Israelites crossed, but when the Egyptians followed, the LORD troubled their chariots and told Moses to stretch his hand over the sea again, causing the waters to return and drown the Egyptians. The Israelites saw the Egyptians dead on the shore, feared the LORD, believed in Him and Moses. Moses and the Israelites then sang a song to the LORD, celebrating their deliverance, proclaiming the LORD as their strength, salvation, and a warrior, acknowledging His power in overthrowing their enemies and leading them to safety.The children of Israel were told by God that in the evening they would eat flesh, and in the morning they would be filled with bread, recognizing the Lord as their God. Quails covered the camp in the evening, and in the morning, dew surrounded the host. When the dew lifted, a small, round substance, like hoar frost, covered the ground. The Israelites, unsure of what it was, called it manna. Moses explained it was the bread given by the Lord for them to eat. Each person was to gather an omer per person. Some collected more, others less, but everyone had enough according to their need. Moses instructed not to keep any manna until the morning, but some disobeyed, and the leftover manna bred worms and stank. The manna had to be gathered every morning, and it melted when the sun grew hot. On the sixth day, they collected double the amount, and Moses explained this was because the next day was the Sabbath, a day of rest, when no manna would appear. The people rested on the Sabbath, and the manna was described as white like coriander seed and tasted like wafers made with honey. Moses commanded to keep an omer of manna as a testimony for future generations. The Israelites ate manna for forty years until they reached the borders of Canaan.

The congregation then journeyed to Rephidim, where there was no water. The people quarreled with Moses, demanding water, and questioned why Moses had brought them out of Egypt to die of thirst. Moses, distressed, asked God for guidance. God instructed Moses to strike a rock at Horeb with his staff, and water flowed out for the people to drink. The place was named Massah and Meribah because of the Israelites' quarreling and testing of the Lord. Then, Amalek came and fought with Israel at Rephidim. Moses told Joshua to choose men to fight Amalek, marking the beginning of a battle.Joshua fought Amalek as Moses had instructed, with Moses, Aaron, and Hur on a hilltop. Moses' raised hands led Israel to prevail, but when lowered, Amalek gained the upper hand. To support Moses' arms, Aaron and Hur held them steady until sunset, leading to Joshua's victory over Amalek. The Lord commanded Moses to record this event as a reminder of His promise to erase Amalek's memory from the earth. Moses built an altar named Jehovahnissi, signifying the Lord's vow to battle Amalek across generations.

When Jethro, Moses' father-in-law, heard of the Israelites' triumphs, he brought Moses' wife and sons to him in the wilderness. Jethro rejoiced at the Lord's deliverance of Israel from Egypt, acknowledging the Lord's superiority over other gods. He offered sacrifices to God, and together with Aaron and the elders, shared a meal before God. Observing Moses' exhaustive efforts in judging the people's disputes, Jethro advised delegating responsibilities to capable, God-fearing men to ease Moses' burden and ensure efficient governance. Moses implemented Jethro's advice, appointing leaders over various group sizes to handle minor disputes, reserving major issues for himself. This system allowed Moses to endure, and the people to live in peace.The Egyptians pursued the Israelites, overtaking them by the sea. The Israelites, terrified, cried out to the LORD and questioned Moses for leading them out of Egypt, fearing death in the wilderness. Moses assured them to not fear, for the LORD would show them salvation and fight for them. The LORD instructed Moses to stretch out his hand over the sea to divide it, allowing the Israelites to cross on dry ground. He also said He would harden the Egyptians' hearts to follow, gaining honor upon Pharaoh and his forces. The angel of God and the pillar of cloud moved to protect the Israelites, creating darkness for the Egyptians and light for the Israelites, preventing the two camps from coming near each other. Moses stretched his hand over the sea, and the LORD caused the sea to part with a strong east wind, creating dry land. The Israelites crossed, but when the Egyptians followed, the LORD troubled their chariots and told Moses to stretch his hand over the sea again, causing the waters to return and drown the Egyptians. The Israelites saw the Egyptians dead on the shore, feared the LORD, believed in Him and Moses. Moses and the Israelites then sang a song to the LORD, celebrating their deliverance, proclaiming the LORD as their strength, salvation, and a warrior, acknowledging His power in overthrowing their enemies and leading them to safety. The floods stood upright as a heap, and the depths were congealed in the heart of the sea. The enemy boasted of pursuing, overtaking, and destroying the Israelites, but with a divine blow, they sank as lead in the mighty waters. The LORD's unmatched holiness, praise, and wonder were proclaimed. With His mighty arm, He led the redeemed people, causing fear among the nations. The LORD's promise to bring His people into their inheritance was affirmed. Miriam and the women celebrated with dances and songs of triumph. The journey continued through the wilderness, facing challenges like bitter waters at Marah, which the LORD sweetened, promising health if they obeyed His commandments. They found refreshment at Elim with its wells and palm trees. In the wilderness of Sin, the Israelites murmured against Moses and Aaron, longing for Egypt. The LORD responded by promising bread from heaven to test their obedience. Moses and Aaron reassured the people of the LORD's provision, emphasizing that their complaints were against the LORD, not human leaders. The LORD's glory was revealed in the cloud, affirming His attentive response to their needs.In the third month after leaving Egypt, the Israelites reached the wilderness of Sinai and camped before the mountain. Moses ascended the mountain where God called to him, instructing him to convey to the Israelites that if they obey His voice and keep His covenant, they would be His treasured possession among all peoples, a kingdom of priests, and a holy nation. Moses relayed God's words to the elders and the people, who unanimously agreed to do all that the Lord had spoken.

God then instructed Moses to sanctify the people and prepare them for the third day when He would descend upon Mount Sinai in the sight of all. He warned that no one should touch the mountain or they would face death. On the appointed day, with thunder, lightning, and a thick cloud covering the mountain, and the sound of the trumpet growing louder, the Lord descended in fire, causing the mountain to smoke and quake. Moses spoke, and God answered him with a voice.

The Lord warned Moses to keep the people from breaking through to gaze at Him, lest many perish. Only Moses and Aaron were permitted to come up the mountain. God then spoke the Ten Commandments, starting with the declaration that He is the Lord who brought them out of Egypt and commanding them to have no other gods, not to make idols, to keep the Sabbath holy, and to honor their parents, among others. These laws laid the foundation for the Israelites' covenant with God, emphasizing worship, rest, and social ethics.The children of Israel were told by God that in the evening they would eat meat and in the morning they would be filled with bread, recognizing Him as their Lord. As promised, quails covered the camp in the evening, and in the morning, manna, described as a small round thing, appeared on the ground. Moses instructed them to gather an omer per person, and miraculously, those who gathered much or little had exactly what they needed, emphasizing the importance of following God's command to not keep any manna until the morning, which some disobeyed, resulting in spoiled manna.

On the sixth day, they collected double the amount of bread, preparing for the Sabbath as instructed by Moses, highlighting the sanctity of the Sabbath and God's provision. The manna did not spoil overnight as it did on other days, and on the Sabbath, there was no manna to gather, reinforcing the command to rest. The Israelites called the bread manna, noting its taste like wafers made with honey. Moses commanded to keep an omer of manna as a testimony for future generations, showing God's provision in the wilderness. The Israelites ate manna for forty years until reaching the borders of Canaan.

The narrative continues with the Israelites' journey to Rephidim, where they faced a lack of water, leading to complaints against Moses and testing of the Lord. God instructed Moses to strike a rock with his staff to provide water, which he did, and water flowed out for the people to drink. This place was named Massah and Meribah due to the Israelites' testing of the Lord. The Amalekites then attacked the Israelites at Rephidim, prompting Moses to instruct Joshua to choose men for battle.In the continuation of God's commandments, the Sabbath is emphasized as a day of rest, blessed and hallowed by the Lord, following His example of resting on the seventh day after creating the heavens and the earth. The commandments further instruct to honor one's parents, prohibit murder, adultery, theft, bearing false witness, and coveting anything that belongs to one's neighbor. The people witnessed the awe-inspiring event of God's presence on Mount Sinai with thunder, lightning, and the sound of a trumpet, causing them to keep their distance and ask Moses to speak to God on their behalf, fearing death if God spoke directly to them. Moses reassured them that God's appearance was to test and instill the fear of Him so they would not sin.

God's instructions continued with laws regarding altars, emphasizing simplicity and reverence to prevent desecration. Detailed judgments were then provided on various aspects of social justice, including the treatment of servants, personal injury laws, and the principle of lex talionis - an eye for an eye, tooth for a tooth, ensuring fair retribution for injuries. These laws covered a wide range of social interactions, from the treatment of servants and the consequences of personal injuries to the protection of property and the sanctity of life, laying the foundation for a just and orderly society among the Israelites.Joshua fought Amalek as Moses, Aaron, and Hur went to the top of the hill. When Moses held up his hand, Israel prevailed; when he lowered it, Amalek prevailed. Moses' hands were supported by Aaron and Hur until sunset, leading to Joshua's victory. The Lord instructed Moses to record this event as a memorial and built an altar named Jehovahnissi, signifying ongoing conflict with Amalek across generations.

Jethro, Moses' father-in-law, hearing of the Israelites' successes, brought Moses' wife and sons to him. They rejoiced over the deliverance from Egypt, acknowledging the Lord's superiority over other gods. Jethro observed Moses judging the people alone, suggesting a system of delegation for minor issues to ease Moses' burden. Moses implemented this, appointing capable men as leaders over various group sizes, improving the administration of justice and reducing his workload.Moses let his father-in-law depart, and he returned to his own land. In the third month after leaving Egypt, the Israelites reached the wilderness of Sinai and camped before the mountain. Moses ascended to God, who instructed him to remind the Israelites of their deliverance from Egypt and the covenant they must keep to become a treasured nation above all others, a kingdom of priests, and a holy nation.

Moses conveyed God's words to the elders and the people, who agreed to obey. God then planned to appear in a thick cloud so the people would hear Him speak to Moses and believe forever. He instructed Moses to sanctify the people and set boundaries around the mountain, warning that touching it would result in death. On the third day, amidst thunder, lightning, and thick cloud, God descended on Mount Sinai in fire, and the mountain trembled. Moses spoke, and God answered him.

God warned against the people breaking through to gaze upon Him, which could lead to their demise, and instructed that even the priests must sanctify themselves. Moses relayed these instructions, emphasizing the importance of setting boundaries around the mountain.

God then delivered the Ten Commandments, starting with the declaration of His sovereignty and the prohibition of other gods, idolatry, misuse of His name, and instructions to observe the Sabbath, honor one's parents, and prohibitions against murder, adultery, theft, false witness, and covetousness. These laws laid the foundation for the Israelites' covenant with God, emphasizing worship, social ethics, and personal morality.In six days, the LORD created heaven, earth, the sea, and all within them, resting on the seventh day, thus blessing and sanctifying the Sabbath. The commandments continue with honoring one's parents for a long life in the land given by God, and prohibitions against murder, adultery, theft, bearing false witness, and coveting anything that belongs to one's neighbor. The people witnessed thunder, lightning, and the mountain smoking; they stood afar, asking Moses to speak with God on their behalf, fearing death if God spoke directly to them. Moses assured them that God's appearance was to test and instill fear to keep them from sinning.

God instructed Moses on the proper worship, including making altars of earth or uncut stone for sacrifices, emphasizing the importance of not using tools on the altar stones or ascending steps to it, to maintain purity.

Laws regarding Hebrew servants are detailed, including their rights and the conditions for their freedom. Specific judgments for various offenses are outlined, such as penalties for murder, assault, theft, and personal injury, including the principle of "an eye for an eye." Special considerations are given for the treatment of servants and the protection of pregnant women, highlighting the value of life and the importance of justice and fairness in the community."go free for his eye's sake. And if he smite out his manservant's tooth, or his maidservant's tooth; he shall let him go free for his tooth's sake. If an ox gore a man or a woman, that they die: then the ox shall be surely stoned, and his flesh shall not be eaten; but the owner of the ox shall be quit. But if the ox were wont to push with his horn in time past, and it hath been testified to his owner, and he hath not kept him in, but that he hath killed a man or a woman; the ox shall be stoned, and his owner also shall be put to death. If there be laid on him a sum of money, then he shall give for the ransom of his life whatsoever is laid upon him. Whether he have gored a son, or have gored a daughter, according to this judgment shall it be done unto him. If the ox shall push a manservant or a maidservant; he shall give unto their master thirty shekels of silver, and the ox shall be stoned. And if a man shall open a pit, or if a man shall dig a pit, and not cover it, and an ox or an ass fall therein; the owner of the pit shall make it good, and give money unto the owner of them; and the dead beast shall be his. And if one man's ox hurt another's, that he die; then they shall sell the live ox, and divide the money of it; and the dead ox also they shall divide. Or if it be known that the ox hath used to push in time past, and his owner hath not kept him in; he shall surely pay ox for ox; and the dead shall be his own. If a man shall steal an ox, or a sheep, and kill it, or sell it; he shall restore five oxen for an ox, and four sheep for a sheep. If a thief be found breaking up, and be smitten that he die, there shall no blood be shed for him. If the sun be risen upon him, there shall be blood shed for him; for he should make full restitution; if he have nothing, then he shall be sold for his theft. If the theft be certainly found in his hand alive, whether it be ox, or ass, or sheep; he shall restore double. If a man shall cause a field or vineyard to be eaten, and shall put in his beast, and shall feed in another man's field; of the best of his own field, and of the best of his own vineyard, shall he make restitution. If fire break out, and catch in thorns, so that the stacks of corn, or the standing corn, or the field, be consumed therewith; he that kindled the fire shall surely make restitution. If a man shall deliver unto his neighbour money or stuff to keep, and it be stolen out of the man's house; if the thief be found, let him pay double. If the thief be not found, then the master of the house shall be brought unto the judges, to see whether he have put his hand unto his neighbour's goods. For all manner of trespass, whether it be for ox, for ass, for sheep, for raiment, or for any manner of lost thing which another challengeth to be his, the cause of both parties shall come before the judges; and whom the judges shall condemn, he shall pay double unto his neighbour. If a man deliver unto his neighbour an ass, or an ox, or a sheep, or any beast, to keep; and it die, or be hurt, or driven away, no man seeing it: Then shall an oath of the LORD be between them both, that he hath not put his hand unto his neighbour's goods; and the owner of it shall accept thereof, and he shall not make it good. And if it be stolen from him, he shall make restitution unto the owner thereof. If it be torn in pieces, then let him bring it for witness, and he shall not make good that which was torn. And if a man borrow ought of his neighbour, and it be hurt, or die, the owner thereof being not with it, he shall surely make it good. But if the owner thereof be with it, he shall not make it good: if it be an hired thing, it came for his hire. And if a man entice a maid that is not betrothed, and lie with her, he shall surely endow her to be his wife. If her father utterly refuse to give her unto him, he shall pay money according to the dowry of virgins. Thou shalt not suffer a witch to live. Whosoever lieth with a beast shall surely be put to death. He that sacrificeth unto any god, save unto the LORD only, he shall be utterly destroyed. Thou shalt neither vex a stranger, nor oppress him: for ye were strangers in the land of Egypt. Ye shall not afflict any widow, or fatherless child. If thou afflict them in any wise, and they cry at all unto me, I will surely hear their cry; And my wrath shall wax hot, and I will kill you with the sword; and your wives shall be widows, and your children fatherless. If thou lend money to any of my people that is poor by thee, thou shalt not be to him as an usurer, neither shalt thou lay upon him usury. If thou at all take thy neighbour's raiment to pledge, thou shalt deliver it unto him by that the sun goeth down: For that is his covering only, it is his raiment for his skin: wherein shall he sleep.""go free for his eye's sake. Thou shalt not revile the gods, nor curse the ruler of thy people. Thou shalt not delay to offer the first of thy ripe fruits, and of thy liquors: the firstborn of thy sons shalt thou give unto me. Likewise shalt thou do with thine oxen, and with thy sheep: seven days it shall be with his dam; on the eighth day thou shalt give it me. And ye shall be holy men unto me: neither shall ye eat any flesh that is torn of beasts in the field; ye shall cast it to the dogs. Thou shalt not raise a false report: put not thine hand with the wicked to be an unrighteous witness. Thou shalt not follow a multitude to do evil; neither shalt thou speak in a cause to decline after many to wrest judgment: Neither shalt thou countenance a poor man in his cause. If thou meet thine enemy's ox or his ass going astray, thou shalt surely bring it back to him again. If thou see the ass of him that hateth thee lying under his burden, and wouldest forbear to help him, thou shalt surely help with him. Thou shalt not wrest the judgment of thy poor in his cause. Keep thee far from a false matter; and the innocent and righteous slay thou not: for I will not justify the wicked. And thou shalt take no gift: for the gift blindeth the wise, and perverteth the words of the righteous. Also thou shalt not oppress a stranger: for ye know the heart of a stranger, seeing ye were strangers in the land of Egypt. And six years thou shalt sow thy land, and shalt gather in the fruits thereof: But the seventh year thou shalt let it rest and lie still; that the poor of thy people may eat: and what they leave the beasts of the field shall eat. In like manner thou shalt deal with thy vineyard, and with thy oliveyard. Six days thou shalt do thy work, and on the seventh day thou shalt rest: that thine ox and thine ass may rest, and the son of thy handmaid, and the stranger, may be refreshed. And in all things that I have said unto you be circumspect: and make no mention of the name of other gods, neither let it be heard out of thy mouth. Three times thou shalt keep a feast unto me in the year. Thou shalt keep the feast of unleavened bread: (thou shalt eat unleavened bread seven days, as I commanded thee, in the time appointed of the month Abib; for in it thou camest out from Egypt: and none shall appear before me empty:) And the feast of harvest, the firstfruits of thy labours, which thou hast sown in the field: and the feast of ingathering, which is in the end of the year, when thou hast gathered in thy labours out of the field. Three times in the year all thy males shall appear before the LORD God. Thou shalt not offer the blood of my sacrifice with leavened bread; neither shall the fat of my sacrifice remain until the morning. The first of the firstfruits of thy land thou shalt bring into the house of the LORD thy God. Thou shalt not seethe a kid in his mother's milk. Behold, I send an Angel before thee, to keep thee in the way, and to bring thee into the place which I have prepared. Beware of him, and obey his voice, provoke him not; for he will not pardon your transgressions: for my name is in him. But if thou shalt indeed obey his voice, and do all that I speak; then I will be an enemy unto thine enemies, and an adversary unto thine adversaries. For mine Angel shall go before thee, and bring thee in unto the Amorites, and the Hittites, and the Perizzites, and the Canaanites, the Hivites, and the Jebusites: and I will cut them off. Thou shalt not bow down to their gods, nor serve them, nor do after their works: but thou shalt utterly overthrow them, and quite break down their images. And ye shall serve the LORD your God, and he shall bless thy bread, and thy water; and I will take sickness away from the midst of thee. There shall nothing cast their young, nor be barren, in thy land: the number of thy days I will fulfil. I will send my fear before thee, and will destroy all the people to whom thou shalt come, and I will make all thine enemies turn their backs unto thee. And I will send hornets before thee, which shall drive out the Hivite, the Canaanite, and the Hittite, from before thee. I will not drive them out from before thee in one year; lest the land become desolate, and the beast of the field multiply against thee. By little and little I will drive them out from before thee, until thou be increased, and inherit the land. And I will set thy bounds from the Red sea even unto the sea of the Philistines, and from the desert unto the river: for I will deliver the inhabitants of the land into your hand; and thou shalt drive them out before thee. Thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor with their gods. They shall not dwell in thy land, lest they make thee sin.""Against serving foreign gods, for it will become a snare. Moses, Aaron, Nadab, Abihu, and seventy elders were called to worship from a distance, while only Moses would approach the LORD. Moses relayed God's words and judgments to the people, who pledged obedience. Moses then wrote down all the LORD's words, built an altar and twelve pillars for the twelve tribes, and conducted offerings. He sprinkled half the blood on the altar and the other half on the people, signifying the covenant. Moses, Aaron, and the elders saw God, and they ate and drank in His presence. The LORD then instructed Moses to come to Mount Sinai to receive stone tablets with laws and commandments. Moses and Joshua ascended the mountain, leaving Aaron and Hur in charge. The LORD's glory covered the mountain for six days, and on the seventh, He called Moses into the cloud, where he stayed for forty days and nights.

The LORD then instructed Moses on offerings needed from the Israelites to build a sanctuary, detailing materials like gold, silver, brass, fine linen, and specific woods and stones. Instructions were given for constructing the Ark of the Covenant, including dimensions, materials, and the mercy seat with cherubim. The purpose was to create a dwelling place for God among the people, following the exact pattern shown to Moses."In the ark, you shall place the testimony I will give you. I will meet with you there, and communicate from above the mercy seat, between the two cherubim on the ark of the testimony, about all I command for the children of Israel. You shall also make a table of acacia wood, two cubits long, a cubit wide, and a cubit and a half high. Overlay it with pure gold and make a gold crown around it. Create a border a handbreadth wide with a gold crown around that too. Make four gold rings for it and place them at its four corners, on its feet. The rings will hold the poles to carry the table, which you shall make of acacia wood and overlay with gold. Make its dishes, spoons, covers, and bowls of pure gold. Set shewbread on the table before me always.

Make a candlestick of pure gold, hammered out. It will have a central shaft with six branches, three on each side, each decorated with almond-shaped bowls, knops, and flowers. The candlestick itself will have four almond-shaped bowls with knops and flowers. Each pair of branches will have a knop under it, all of one piece with the candlestick, hammered out of pure gold. Make its seven lamps, and they shall light the area in front of it. Its tongs and snuffdishes shall also be of pure gold. Use a talent of pure gold for it and all these vessels. Ensure you make them according to the pattern shown to you on the mountain.

Moreover, make the tabernacle with ten curtains of fine twined linen, blue, purple, and scarlet, with cherubim of skilled work. Each curtain shall be twenty-eight cubits long and four cubits wide, all of the same size. Five curtains shall be joined together, and the other five likewise. Make loops of blue on the edges of one curtain and do the same on the outer edge of the second set, so the loops can catch each other. Use fifty gold clasps to connect the curtains, making it one tabernacle. Make additional curtains of goats' hair for a covering over the tabernacle, eleven curtains in total, each thirty cubits long and four cubits wide. Couple five curtains separately and six curtains separately, doubling the sixth curtain at the front of the tabernacle. Make fifty loops on the edge of the outermost curtain in one set, and fifty loops on the edge of the second set, with fifty bronze clasps to join the tent together as one. The remaining curtains shall extend over the sides and back of the tabernacle. Cover the tent with rams' skins dyed red and a covering above of fine leather. Make upright boards for the tabernacle of acacia wood, ten cubits long."p? and it shall come to pass, when he crieth unto me, that I will hear; for I am gracious. Thou shalt not revile the gods, nor curse the ruler of thy people. Thou shalt not delay to offer the first of thy ripe fruits, and of thy liquors: the firstborn of thy sons shalt thou give unto me. Likewise shalt thou do with thine oxen, and with thy sheep: seven days it shall be with his dam; on the eighth day thou shalt give it me. And ye shall be holy men unto me: neither shall ye eat any flesh that is torn of beasts in the field; ye shall cast it to the dogs. Thou shalt not raise a false report: put not thine hand with the wicked to be an unrighteous witness. Thou shalt not follow a multitude to do evil; neither shalt thou speak in a cause to decline after many to wrest judgment: Neither shalt thou countenance a poor man in his cause. If thou meet thine enemy's ox or his ass going astray, thou shalt surely bring it back to him again. If thou see the ass of him that hateth thee lying under his burden, and wouldest forbear to help him, thou shalt surely help with him. Thou shalt not wrest the judgment of thy poor in his cause. Keep thee far from a false matter; and the innocent and righteous slay thou not: for I will not justify the wicked. And thou shalt take no gift: for the gift blindeth the wise, and perverteth the words of the righteous. Also thou shalt not oppress a stranger: for ye know the heart of a stranger, seeing ye were strangers in the land of Egypt. And six years thou shalt sow thy land, and shalt gather in the fruits thereof: But the seventh year thou shalt let it rest and lie still; that the poor of thy people may eat: and what they leave the beasts of the field shall eat. In like manner thou shalt deal with thy vineyard, and with thy oliveyard. Six days thou shalt do thy work, and on the seventh day thou shalt rest: that thine ox and thine ass may rest, and the son of thy handmaid, and the stranger, may be refreshed. And in all things that I have said unto you be circumspect: and make no mention of the name of other gods, neither let it be heard out of thy mouth. Three times thou shalt keep a feast unto me in the year. Thou shalt keep the feast of unleavened bread: (thou shalt eat unleavened bread seven days, as I commanded thee, in the time appointed of the month Abib; for in it thou camest out from Egypt: and none shall appear before me empty:) And the feast of harvest, the firstfruits of thy labours, which thou hast sown in the field: and the feast of ingathering, which is in the end of the year, when thou hast gathered in thy labours out of the field. Three times in the year all thy males shall appear before the LORD God. Thou shalt not offer the blood of my sacrifice with leavened bread; neither shall the fat of my sacrifice remain until the morning. The first of the firstfruits of thy land thou shalt bring into the house of the LORD thy God. Thou shalt not seethe a kid in his mother's milk. Behold, I send an Angel before thee, to keep thee in the way, and to bring thee into the place which I have prepared. Beware of him, and obey his voice, provoke him not; for he will not pardon your transgressions: for my name is in him. But if thou shalt indeed obey his voice, and do all that I speak; then I will be an enemy unto thine enemies, and an adversary unto thine adversaries. For mine Angel shall go before thee, and bring thee in unto the Amorites, and the Hittites, and the Perizzites, and the Canaanites, the Hivites, and the Jebusites: and I will cut them off. Thou shalt not bow down to their gods, nor serve them, nor do after their works: but thou shalt utterly overthrow them, and quite break down their images. And ye shall serve the LORD your God, and he shall bless thy bread, and thy water; and I will take sickness away from the midst of thee. There shall nothing cast their young, nor be barren, in thy land: the number of thy days I will fulfil. I will send my fear before thee, and will destroy all the people to whom thou shalt come, and I will make all thine enemies turn their backs unto thee. And I will send hornets before thee, which shall drive out the Hivite, the Canaanite, and the Hittite, from before thee. I will not drive them out from before thee in one year; lest the land become desolate, and the beast of the field multiply against thee. By little and little I will drive them out from before thee, until thou be increased, and inherit the land. And I will set thy bounds from the Red sea even unto the sea of the Philistines, and from the desert unto the river: for I will deliver the inhabitants of the land into your hand; and thou shalt drive them out before thee. Thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor with their gods. They shall not dwell in thy land, lest they make thee sin."Make the boards for the tabernacle twenty on the south side, with forty silver sockets; two sockets under each board. For the north side, also make twenty boards with their forty silver sockets. For the west side of the tabernacle, make six boards and two additional boards for the corners. These corner boards will be coupled together at both the bottom and the top into a single ring, forming the two corners. There will be eight boards in total for the corners, with sixteen silver sockets; two under each board.

Create bars of acacia wood; five for the boards on one side of the tabernacle, five for the other side, and five for the west side. The middle bar will run through the center of the boards from end to end. Overlay the boards and bars with gold and make gold rings for the bars. Set up the tabernacle as shown to you on the mountain.

Make a veil of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and fine twined linen, crafted with cherubim. Hang it on four acacia wood pillars overlaid with gold, with gold hooks on four silver sockets. The veil will separate the Holy Place from the Most Holy Place. Place the mercy seat on the Ark of the Testimony in the Most Holy Place. Set the table outside the veil on the north side and the lampstand opposite the table on the south side.

For the tent's entrance, make a screen of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and fine twined linen, embroidered with needlework. Use five acacia wood pillars overlaid with gold for the screen, with gold hooks and five bronze bases.

Construct an altar of acacia wood, five cubits long and wide, and three cubits high, with horns on the four corners. Overlay it with bronze. Make all its utensils of bronzepans, shovels, basins, forks, and firepans. Create a bronze grating for it with four bronze rings at its corners. Place it under the altar's ledge, centered. Make poles of acacia wood, overlay them with bronze, and insert them into the rings for carrying. The altar should be hollow, made from boards, as shown to you on the mountain.

For the tabernacle's courtyard, make hangings of fine twined linen for the south side, one hundred cubits long, with twenty pillars and twenty bronze bases; the hooks and bands of the pillars are of silver. Do the same for the north side. For the west side, make hangings fifty cubits long, with ten pillars and ten bases. The east side, also fifty cubits wide, will have hangings for the gate fifteen cubits long on both sides, with three pillars and three bases on each side.Instructed by the LORD, Moses, along with Aaron, Nadab, Abihu, and seventy elders of Israel, were to worship from a distance, while only Moses was to approach the LORD directly. Moses relayed the LORD's commands and judgments to the people, who unanimously agreed to follow them. Moses then documented all the LORD's words, built an altar and twelve pillars for the twelve tribes of Israel, and conducted offerings to the LORD. He also read the book of the covenant to the people, who pledged obedience. Moses then sprinkled blood on the altar and the people, signifying the covenant between them and the LORD.

Moses, Aaron, Nadab, Abihu, and the seventy elders saw the God of Israel, experiencing a vision of divine glory. The LORD then called Moses to Mount Sinai to receive stone tablets with laws and commandments. Moses instructed the elders to wait for his return, leaving Aaron and Hur in charge. Upon entering the cloud covering Mount Sinai, Moses stayed on the mountain for forty days and nights.

The LORD then instructed Moses to collect offerings from the Israelites to build a sanctuary, detailing the materials required for its construction and the ark of the covenant. Specific instructions were given for the ark's construction, including dimensions, materials, and the placement of the mercy seat with cherubim. This sanctuary was to be a dwelling place for the LORD among the people, constructed according to the divine pattern shown to Moses.In the ark, you shall place the testimony I will give you. I will meet with you there, and communicate from above the mercy seat, between the two cherubim on the ark of the testimony, about all I command for the children of Israel. You shall also construct a table from acacia wood, measuring two cubits in length, a cubit in width, and a cubit and a half in height. Overlay it with pure gold and create a gold crown around it. Add a border a handbreadth wide with a gold crown around that too. Make four gold rings for it and place them at its four corners, on its legs. The rings will hold the poles to carry the table, which you shall make from acacia wood and overlay with gold. Create its dishes, spoons, pitchers, and bowls for pouring offerings, all in pure gold. Always set showbread on the table before me.

Craft a candlestick of pure gold, hammered out. It will have a central shaft with six branches, three on each side, each decorated with almond-shaped bowls, knops, and flowers. The candlestick itself will have four almond-shaped bowls with knops and flowers. Each pair of branches will share a knop, made from one piece in a hammered work of pure gold. Make seven lamps for it, and they shall illuminate the space in front of it. Its tongs and snuff dishes shall also be of pure gold. Use a talent of pure gold for it and all these accessories. Ensure you make them according to the pattern shown to you on the mountain.

Moreover, construct the tabernacle with ten curtains of fine twined linen, blue, purple, and scarlet, adorned with cherubim. Each curtain shall be twenty-eight cubits long and four cubits wide, all of the same size. Join five curtains together and do the same with the other five. Make loops of blue on the edges of one curtain and on the outer edge of the second curtain to link them. Create fifty loops on one curtain and fifty on the other, so the loops match up. Use fifty gold clasps to connect the curtains, forming one tabernacle. Make additional curtains of goats' hair for a covering over the tabernacle, eleven in total. The length of one curtain shall be thirty cubits, and the width four cubits, with all eleven curtains being the same size. Couple five curtains separately and six curtains separately, doubling the sixth curtain at the front of the tabernacle. Attach fifty loops to the edge of the outermost curtain and fifty to the second, joining them with fifty bronze clasps, so the tent becomes one unit. The remaining curtains shall extend over the tabernacle's back and sides to cover it. Make a covering for the tent of rams' skins dyed red and another covering of badger skins. Construct upright boards for the tabernacle from acacia wood, each ten cubits high.Make hangings of twenty cubits of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, wrought with needlework, supported by four pillars and four sockets. All pillars around the court shall be filleted with silver, their hooks of silver, and sockets of brass. The court shall measure a hundred cubits in length, fifty cubits in width everywhere, and five cubits in height, made of fine twined linen, with brass sockets. All vessels of the tabernacle for all its service, and all its pins, and all the pins of the court, shall be of brass. Command the children of Israel to bring pure olive oil beaten for the light, to keep the lamp burning always. In the tabernacle of the congregation outside the veil, which is before the testimony, Aaron and his sons shall maintain it from evening to morning before the LORD; it shall be a perpetual statute for their generations on behalf of the children of Israel.

Take Aaron your brother, and his sons with him, from among the children of Israel, to minister in the priest's office: Aaron, Nadab and Abihu, Eleazar and Ithamar, Aaron's sons. Make holy garments for Aaron your brother for glory and beauty. Speak to all wise-hearted individuals whom I have filled with the spirit of wisdom, to make Aaron's garments to consecrate him, so he may minister in the priest's office. These garments shall include a breastplate, an ephod, a robe, a broidered coat, a mitre, and a girdle. They shall make holy garments for Aaron your brother and his sons, to minister in the priest's office, using gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen.

The ephod shall be made of gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, with cunning work. It shall have two shoulder pieces joined at the edges, so it shall be joined together. The curious girdle of the ephod shall be of the same materials, according to its workmanship. Take two onyx stones and engrave on them the names of the children of Israel: six names on one stone and the other six names on the other stone, according to their birth. With the work of an engraver in stone, like the engravings of a signet, engrave the two stones with the names of the children of Israel. Set them in gold settings. Place the two stones on the shoulders of the ephod as memorial stones for the children of Israel; Aaron shall bear their names before the LORD on his two shoulders for a memorial. Make settings of gold and two chains of pure gold at the ends; of wreathen work, and fasten the wreathen chains to the settings.

Make the breastplate of judgment with cunning work, like the ephod. It shall be made of gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen. It shall be square and doubled, a span in length and breadth. Set in it four rows of stones: the first row shall be a sardius, a topaz, and a carbuncle; the second row an emerald, a sapphire, and a diamond; the third row a ligure, an agate, and an amethyst; the fourth row a beryl, an onyx, and a jasper. They shall be set in gold in their enclosures. The stones shall bear the names of the children of Israel, twelve according to their names, like the engravings of a signet, each with his name for the twelve tribes. Make upon the breastplate chains at the ends of wreathen work of pure gold. Make two rings of gold for the breastplate and put the two rings on the two ends of the breastplate. Put the two wreathen chains of gold in the two rings at the ends of the breastplate. The other two ends of the two wreathen chains fasten in the two settings, and put them on the shoulder pieces of the ephod at the front. Make two rings of gold and put them on the two ends of the breastplate on the edge, which is on the side of the ephod inward. Make two other rings of gold and put them on the two sides of the ephod underneath, toward the forepart thereof, over against the other coupling thereof, above the curious girdle of the ephod. They shall bind the breastplate by its rings to the rings of the ephod with a lace of blue, that it may be above the curious girdle of the ephod, and that the breastplate be not loosed from the ephod.Length of a board shall be ten cubits, and a cubit and a half the breadth of one board. Each board will have two tenons for joining. Make twenty boards for the south side of the tabernacle and forty silver sockets for them, with two sockets under each board. For the north side, also make twenty boards and forty silver sockets. For the west side, make six boards and two additional boards for the corners, which will be coupled together at the bottom and top into one ring, making eight boards in total with sixteen silver sockets. Construct bars of acacia wood, five for each side of the tabernacle and the west side, with the middle bar reaching from end to end. Overlay the boards and bars with gold and make gold rings for the bars. Erect the tabernacle as shown on the mountain.

Create a veil of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen with cherubim. Hang it on four acacia wood pillars overlaid with gold, with gold hooks and silver sockets. The veil will separate the Holy Place from the Most Holy Place, where the Ark of the Testimony and the mercy seat will be placed. Outside the veil, set the table and the candlestick on the south side, with the table on the north side. Make a hanging for the tent door of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen with needlework, supported by five acacia wood pillars overlaid with gold and brass sockets.

Construct an altar of acacia wood, five cubits long and broad, and three cubits high, with horns on the four corners overlaid with brass. Make all its utensils of brass. Create a brass grate with four rings at its corners and place it under the altar's compass. Make staves of acacia wood overlaid with brass for carrying the altar, which should be hollow as shown on the mountain.

For the tabernacle's court, make hangings of fine twined linen, one hundred cubits long for the south and north sides, with twenty pillars and brass sockets, and silver hooks and fillets. For the west side, make hangings of fifty cubits with ten pillars and sockets. The east side shall also be fifty cubits wide. The gate of the court will have hangings of fifteen cubits on each side, with three pillars and sockets.Aaron shall bear the names of the children of Israel in the breastplate of judgment upon his heart when he enters the holy place, as a continual memorial before the LORD. The Urim and Thummim shall be placed in the breastplate of judgment, resting on Aaron's heart when he stands before the LORD, symbolizing his bearing the judgment of the children of Israel on his heart at all times. The robe of the ephod shall be entirely blue, with a hole at the top for the head, reinforced around the edge to prevent tearing. Around the hem, make pomegranates of blue, purple, and scarlet, with gold bells between them, so Aaron's movements can be heard as he ministers in the holy place, ensuring his safety. A pure gold plate engraved with "HOLINESS TO THE LORD" shall be attached to the mitre by a blue lace, signifying Aaron's role in bearing the iniquity of the sacred offerings of the children of Israel, making them acceptable to the LORD. Fine linen garments, including a coat, mitre, and a girdle of needlework, shall be made for Aaron, and similar attire for his sons, to be anointed, consecrated, and sanctified for ministering as priests. Linen breeches shall cover their nakedness during service to avoid incurring guilt and death, a perpetual statute. For their consecration, offer a young bullock and two rams without blemish, along with unleavened bread, cakes mixed with oil, and wafers anointed with oil, made from wheaten flour. These offerings, placed in a basket, shall be brought to the tabernacle's entrance with Aaron and his sons, who are to be washed with water and dressed in their sacred garments. Anoint Aaron by pouring oil on his head, and similarly dress and consecrate his sons. The ordination involves laying hands on a bullock before the LORD, slaughtering it, and applying its blood to the altar as a sin offering, with its flesh, skin, and dung burned outside the camp. The same process is followed with one ram, its blood sprinkled around the altar, and after being cut into pieces, its inwards and legs washed and burned as an offering to the LORD.Aaron and his sons shall lay their hands on the head of the ram, then kill it, taking its blood to put on the tips of their right ears, thumbs of their right hands, and big toes of their right feet, and sprinkle the blood around the altar. The blood from the altar and anointing oil shall be sprinkled on Aaron, his garments, his sons, and their garments, consecrating them. From the ram, take the fat, rump, organs, and right shoulder for a consecration offering, along with bread, cakes, and wafers from the unleavened bread basket before the LORD. These items shall be waved as an offering before the LORD, then burned on the altar as a pleasing aroma. The breast of the ram shall be waved as an offering and shall be the priest's portion. The holy garments of Aaron will be passed to his sons for their anointing and consecration. The priest's son shall wear these garments for seven days when he serves in the holy place. The ram of consecration's flesh, along with the bread, shall be eaten by Aaron and his sons in a holy place; any leftovers by morning shall be burned. This consecration process for Aaron and his sons shall last seven days, with a daily sin offering to atone and sanctify the altar, making it most holy. A continual burnt offering of two lambs each day shall be made, with accompanying grain, oil, and wine offerings. This shall be a perpetual ordinance, where the LORD will meet and speak to the children of Israel, sanctifying the tabernacle and altar, and consecrating Aaron and his sons to serve as priests. The LORD promises to dwell among the Israelites and be their God, reminding them of their deliverance from Egypt. An altar for burning incense shall also be made."Make the altar of incense from acacia wood, measuring one cubit long, one cubit wide, and two cubits high, with horns of the same piece. Overlay it with pure goldtop, sides, and hornsand add a gold molding around it. Make two gold rings under the molding on opposite sides to hold poles for carrying, made of acacia wood overlaid with gold. Place the altar in front of the veil near the Ark of the Testimony, before the mercy seat. Aaron shall burn sweet incense on it every morning and evening, a perpetual incense before the LORD for generations. Do not offer unauthorized incense, burnt offerings, grain offerings, or drink offerings on it. Once a year, Aaron shall make atonement on its horns with the blood of the sin offering. This is most holy to the LORD.

The LORD instructs Moses on a census, requiring each person counted to give a ransom for themselves to avoid a plague. The contribution is half a shekel per person, as an offering to the LORD, from those twenty years old and above. This money is for the service of the Tent of Meeting, serving as a memorial for the Israelites. 

Additionally, make a bronze basin with a bronze stand for washing. Place it between the Tent of Meeting and the altar, filled with water for Aaron and his sons to wash their hands and feet, ensuring they do not die when they enter the Tent of Meeting or approach the altar. This is a permanent law for them.

The LORD also instructs Moses to make a holy anointing oil from myrrh, cinnamon, calamus, cassia, and olive oil, and to use it to anoint the Tabernacle and everything in it, consecrating them. Aaron and his sons are to be anointed and consecrated as priests. This holy anointing oil is sacred and must not be replicated or used on ordinary people. Anyone who does so will be cut off from their people.

Finally, the LORD commands Moses to make a sacred incense from spices like stacte, onycha, galbanum, and frankincense, to be pure and holy, used in the Tabernacle.The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him on the creation of sacred items and practices. Bezaleel, son of Uri from the tribe of Judah, was chosen by God, filled with the spirit of wisdom, understanding, knowledge, and craftsmanship to create works in gold, silver, and brass, among other materials. Aholiab, from the tribe of Dan, was also selected to assist Bezaleel, along with other skilled individuals, to construct the Tabernacle, the Ark of the Testimony, the mercy seat, and all associated furnishings. This included the table, candlestick, altars for incense and burnt offerings, the laver, and the holy garments for Aaron and his sons to serve as priests. The anointing oil and incense, made as per God's command, were to be used in the holy place.

God also emphasized the importance of observing the Sabbath as a sign of the covenant between Him and the Israelites, highlighting it as a day of rest and holiness. Anyone who desecrated the Sabbath was to be put to death, underscoring the day's sanctity. The Sabbath served as a perpetual covenant and a reminder of God's creation.

When Moses delayed returning from Mount Sinai, the people, led by Aaron, created a golden calf to worship, prompting God's anger. Despite God's readiness to destroy the people for their idolatry, Moses interceded, pleading for their forgiveness and reminding God of the promise made to Abraham, Isaac, and Israel.All the pillars around the court shall be adorned with silver fillets; their hooks shall be of silver, and their sockets of brass. The court's length shall be a hundred cubits, its breadth fifty cubits everywhere, and its height five cubits, made of fine twined linen, with brass sockets. All the vessels of the tabernacle for all its service, and all its pegs, and all the pegs of the court, shall be of brass. Command the children of Israel to bring pure olive oil beaten for the light, to keep the lamp burning continuously. In the tabernacle of the congregation outside the veil, which is before the testimony, Aaron and his sons shall tend it from evening to morning before the LORD. It shall be a perpetual statute for the generations of the children of Israel.

Take Aaron your brother, and his sons with him, from among the children of Israel, that he may serve as priest to meAaron, Nadab and Abihu, Eleazar and Ithamar, Aaron's sons. You shall make holy garments for Aaron your brother for glory and beauty. Speak to all the wise-hearted, whom I have filled with the spirit of wisdom, that they make Aaron's garments to consecrate him, so he may serve as priest to me. These are the garments they shall make: a breastplate, an ephod, a robe, a broidered coat, a mitre, and a girdle. They shall make holy garments for Aaron your brother and his sons, that he may serve as priest to me. They shall take gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen. They shall make the ephod of gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, with skilled work. It shall have two shoulder pieces joined at its two edges; thus, it shall be joined together. The skillfully woven band of the ephod, which is on it, shall be of the same workmanship and materials: gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen.

Take two onyx stones and engrave on them the names of the children of Israel: six of their names on one stone, and the names of the remaining six on the other stone, according to their birth. With the work of an engraver in stone, like the engravings of a signet, you shall engrave the two stones with the names of the children of Israel. You shall set them in settings of gold. You shall put the two stones on the shoulders of the ephod as stones of memorial for the children of Israel. Aaron shall bear their names before the LORD on his two shoulders for a memorial. Make settings of gold and two chains of pure gold; you shall make them of twisted work and attach the twisted chains to the settings. You shall make the breastplate of judgment with skilled work; in the style of the ephod you shall make itof gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen. It shall be square and doubled, a span in length and a span in breadth. You shall set in it settings of stones, four rows of stones: the first row shall be a sardius, a topaz, and a carbuncle; the second row an emerald, a sapphire, and a diamond; the third row a ligure, an agate, and an amethyst; the fourth row a beryl, an onyx, and a jasper. They shall be set in gold in their mountings. The stones shall bear the names of the children of Israel, twelve according to their names, like the engravings of a signet, each with its name for the twelve tribes. You shall make on the breastplate chains at the ends of twisted work of pure gold. You shall make two rings of gold for the breastplate and put the two rings on the two ends of the breastplate. You shall put the two twisted chains of gold in the two rings at the ends of the breastplate. The other two ends of the two twisted chains you shall fasten to the two settings, and put them on the shoulder pieces of the ephod, at the front. Make two rings of gold and put them on the two ends of the breastplate, on its edge, which is on the inward side of the ephod. Make two more rings of gold and put them on the two sides of the ephod, underneath, toward the front, close to its coupling, above the skillfully woven band of the ephod. They shall bind the breastplate by its rings to the rings of the ephod with a lace of blue, so that it may lie on the skillfully woven band of the ephod and that the breastplate does not come loose from the ephod.Aaron shall bear the names of the children of Israel in the breastplate of judgment upon his heart when he enters the holy place, as a continual memorial before the LORD. The Urim and Thummim shall be placed in the breastplate of judgment, resting on Aaron's heart when he stands before the LORD, symbolizing his bearing the judgment of the children of Israel on his heart at all times. The robe of the ephod shall be entirely blue, with a hole at the top and a woven binding around it to prevent tearing. Around the hem, make pomegranates of blue, purple, and scarlet, with gold bells between them, so Aaron's sound is heard when he enters and leaves the holy place, preventing his death. A pure gold plate engraved with "HOLINESS TO THE LORD" shall be attached to the mitre with a blue lace. This plate on Aaron's forehead signifies bearing the iniquity of the holy offerings of the children of Israel, ensuring their acceptance before the LORD. Embroider a coat of fine linen, make a fine linen mitre, and a needlework girdle. Make linen garments, girdles, and bonnets for Aaron's sons, for dignity and adornment. Anoint, consecrate, and sanctify Aaron and his sons to minister as priests. They shall wear linen breeches to cover their nakedness when they enter the tabernacle or approach the altar, as a perpetual statute. To consecrate them, use one young bullock and two rams without blemish, unleavened bread, cakes mixed with oil, and wafers anointed with oil, made from wheaten flour. Bring these offerings in a basket to the tabernacle, wash Aaron and his sons with water, and dress Aaron in the sacred garments, anointing him with oil. Dress his sons, consecrate them, and they shall serve as priests forever. Present a bullock at the tabernacle, lay hands on it, and sacrifice it before the LORD, using its blood for purification and burning its fat on the altar as a sin offering, with the remainder burned outside the camp. Sacrifice a ram, sprinkle its blood on the altar, cut it in pieces, wash its inwards and legs, and burn them as an offering to the LORD."Remember Abraham, Isaac, and Israel, your servants, to whom you swore by yourself, saying, 'I will multiply your descendants as the stars of heaven, and all this land that I have spoken of I will give to your descendants, and they shall inherit it forever.' And the LORD relented from the disaster that he had spoken of bringing on his people. Moses turned and went down from the mountain with the two tablets of the testimony in his hands, written on both sides. The tablets were the work of God, and the writing was the writing of God, engraved on the tablets. When Joshua heard the noise of the people shouting, he said to Moses, 'There is a noise of war in the camp.' But Moses said, 'It is not the sound of victory, it is not the sound of defeat; it is the sound of singing that I hear.' As soon as he came near the camp and saw the calf and the dancing, Moses' anger burned hot, and he threw the tablets out of his hands and broke them at the foot of the mountain. He took the calf they had made, burned it with fire, ground it to powder, scattered it on the water, and made the Israelites drink it.

Moses said to Aaron, 'What did this people do to you that you have brought such a great sin upon them?' Aaron said, 'Do not let your anger burn hot; you know the people, that they are set on evil. For they said to me, "Make us gods who shall go before us. As for this Moses, the man who brought us up out of the land of Egypt, we do not know what has become of him." So I said to them, "Let any who have gold take it off." So they gave it to me, and I threw it into the fire, and out came this calf.' When Moses saw that the people had broken loose (for Aaron had let them break loose, to the derision of their enemies), Moses stood in the gate of the camp and said, 'Who is on the LORD's side? Come to me.' And all the sons of Levi gathered around him. He said to them, 'Thus says the LORD God of Israel, "Put your sword on your side, each of you, and go to and fro from gate to gate throughout the camp, and each of you kill his brother and his companion and his neighbor."' The sons of Levi did according to the word of Moses, and about three thousand men of the people fell that day. Moses said, 'Today you have been ordained for the service of the LORD, each one at the cost of his son and of his brother, so that he might bestow a blessing upon you this day.'

The next day Moses said to the people, 'You have sinned a great sin. And now I will go up to the LORD; perhaps I can make atonement for your sin.' Moses returned to the LORD and said, 'Alas, this people has sinned a great sin. They have made for themselves gods of gold. But now, if you will forgive their sinbut if not, please blot me out of your book that you have written.' The LORD said to Moses, 'Whoever has sinned against me, I will blot out of my book. Now go, lead the people to the place of which I have spoken to you. Behold, my angel shall go before you. Nevertheless, in the day when I visit, I will visit their sin upon them.' The LORD sent a plague on the people because they made the calf, the one that Aaron made.

The LORD said to Moses, 'Depart, go up from here, you and the people whom you have brought up out of the land of Egypt, to the land of which I swore to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, saying, "To your offspring I will give it." I will send an angel before you, and I will drive out the Canaanite, the Amorite, the Hittite, the Perizzite, the Hivite, and the Jebusite, to a land flowing with milk and honey. But I will not go up among you, lest I consume you on the way, for you are a stiff-necked people.' When the people heard this disastrous word, they mourned, and no one put on his ornaments. For the LORD had said to Moses, 'Say to the children of Israel, "You are a stiff-necked people; if for a single moment I should go up among you, I would consume you. So now take off your ornaments, that I may know what to do with you."' The children of Israel stripped themselves of their ornaments by Mount Horeb.

Moses took the tent and pitched it outside the camp, far off from the camp, and called it the Tent of Meeting. And everyone who sought the LORD would go out to the Tent of Meeting, which was outside the camp. Whenever Moses went out to the tent, all the people would rise up and each would stand at his tent door and watch Moses until he had gone into the tent."After Moses entered the tabernacle, the cloudy pillar descended and stood at the door, and the Lord spoke with Moses. All the people saw the cloudy pillar at the tabernacle door and worshipped from their tents. The Lord spoke to Moses face to face, as a friend. Moses requested to know whom God would send with him, emphasizing the nation as God's people. God assured Moses of His presence and rest, emphasizing the distinction of Moses and his people from others on earth due to God's accompaniment.

Moses sought to see God's glory, to which God responded by agreeing to show His goodness and proclaim His name, highlighting His mercy and sovereignty in showing grace. However, God stated that no one could see His face and live. He provided a way for Moses to glimpse His glory without seeing His face directly.

God instructed Moses to prepare new tablets like the first ones for the words that were broken. Moses was to meet God on Mount Sinai without anyone else present. God descended in a cloud, proclaimed His name, and passed by Moses, declaring His nature as merciful, gracious, longsuffering, and abundant in goodness and truth, while also emphasizing justice.

Moses worshipped and pleaded for God's presence among the people despite their stubbornness, asking for forgiveness and to be taken as God's inheritance. God agreed, promising to perform wonders and drive out nations before them but warned against making covenants with the land's inhabitants or adopting their practices. God emphasized the importance of worshiping Him alone and outlined specific instructions, including the celebration of the Feast of Unleavened Bread, to maintain the covenant relationship."Then you shall burn the whole ram on the altar; it is a burnt offering to the LORD, a pleasing aroma, an offering made by fire to the LORD. Take the other ram; Aaron and his sons shall lay their hands on its head. Kill the ram, take some of its blood and put it on the lobes of the right ears of Aaron and his sons, on the thumbs of their right hands, and on the big toes of their right feet. Sprinkle the blood around the altar. Take some blood from the altar and some anointing oil and sprinkle it on Aaron and his garments, as well as on his sons and their garments. This will consecrate Aaron, his garments, his sons, and their garments. From this ram, take the fat, the fat tail, the fat that covers the entrails, the lobe of the liver, the two kidneys with the fat on them, and the right thigh; this is a ram of ordination. Also take one loaf of bread, one cake made with oil, and one wafer from the basket of unleavened bread before the LORD; put all these in the hands of Aaron and his sons and wave them as a wave offering before the LORD. Then burn them on the altar on top of the burnt offering, as a pleasing aroma before the LORD; it is an offering made by fire to the LORD. Take the breast of the ram of Aaron's ordination and wave it as a wave offering before the LORD; it will be your portion. Consecrate the breast of the wave offering and the thigh of the contribution, which are waved and raised up, from the ram of ordination, from what was for Aaron and his sons. It is a perpetual share from the Israelites for Aaron and his descendants from the peace offerings of the Israelites. The sacred garments of Aaron will be his sons' after him, to be anointed and ordained in them. The son who succeeds him as priest shall wear them for seven days when he enters the tent of meeting to serve in the Holy Place. Cook the meat of the ordination ram and eat it with the bread in the basket at the entrance to the tent of meeting. This is for Aaron and his sons; they are to eat the offerings with which atonement was made to ordain and consecrate them, but no one else may eat them because they are sacred. If any of the meat of the ordination or any bread is left over till morning, burn it up. It must not be eaten because it is sacred. Do this for Aaron and his sons, exactly as I have commanded you. The ordination will last seven days. Each day offer a bull as a sin offering for atonement. Purify the altar by making atonement for it, and anoint it to consecrate it. For seven days make atonement for the altar and consecrate it. Then the altar will be most holy, and whatever touches it will be holy. Now this is what you shall offer on the altar: two lambs a year old every day, continuously. Offer one lamb in the morning and the other at twilight, with a tenth of an ephah of fine flour mixed with a quarter of a hin of beaten oil, and a quarter of a hin of wine as a drink offering with the second lamb. Offer this as a regular burnt offering throughout your generations at the entrance to the tent of meeting, where I will meet you to speak to you there. There I will meet with the Israelites, and the tent will be consecrated by my glory. I will consecrate the tent of meeting and the altar; I will also consecrate Aaron and his sons to serve me as priests. I will dwell among the Israelites and be their God. They will know that I am the LORD their God, who brought them out of Egypt so that I might dwell among them. I am the LORD their God. You shall make an altar to burn incense on; make it of acacia wood."In the month of Abib, as commanded, observe the Feast of Unleavened Bread, commemorating your exodus from Egypt. Every firstborn among your cattle and your sons belongs to Me. The firstborn of an ass must be redeemed with a lamb, or its neck broken if not redeemed. Work six days, but rest on the seventh, even during plowing and harvest. Celebrate the Feast of Weeks with the firstfruits of wheat harvest, and the Feast of Ingathering at year's end. All your males must appear before the LORD thrice a year, ensuring no one covets your land as I will enlarge your borders. Do not mix My sacrifice with leaven, and ensure the Passover sacrifice is not left until morning. Bring the firstfruits to the LORD's house and do not cook a young goat in its mother's milk.

The LORD instructed Moses to write these commands as part of the covenant with Israel. Moses spent forty days and nights with the LORD without eating or drinking and wrote the covenant's words on tablets. Upon descending, Moses' face shone, causing fear among the Israelites until he reassured them and communicated God's commands, wearing a veil thereafter except when speaking with the LORD.

Moses convened the Israelites, emphasizing the importance of observing a Sabbath of rest on the seventh day, under penalty of death for any work done. No fires were to be kindled on the Sabbath. He called for contributions of materials and craftsmanship for the tabernacle's construction, listing specific needs for its various parts and the priestly garments, engaging the community in this divine project.In the spirit of willingness, both men and women brought offerings for the tabernacle's construction and the holy garments. They donated gold jewelry, and materials like blue, purple, and scarlet yarns, fine linen, goat hair, ram skins dyed red, and badger skins. Contributions also included silver, bronze, and acacia wood for various parts of the service. Women skilled in spinning provided yarns of different colors, while the leaders brought precious stones for the ephod and breastplate, along with spices and oil for the light, anointing oil, and incense.

The community's generosity was overwhelming, with everyone whose heart was moved bringing offerings for the work commanded by the LORD through Moses. Bezaleel of the tribe of Judah and Aholiab of the tribe of Dan were filled with the spirit of God, granting them wisdom, understanding, knowledge, and skill in all kinds of craftsmanship. They were to lead in crafting intricate works in gold, silver, bronze, stone setting, wood carving, and in teaching others.

The work for the sanctuary began with Bezaleel, Aholiab, and every skilled person whom the LORD had endowed with wisdom and understanding. They executed all the tasks as commanded. The people continued to bring free-will offerings each morning until Moses had to command them to stop because they had supplied more than enough materials for the work.

The craftsmen made the tabernacle's curtains of fine twined linen, blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, with cherubim designs. Each curtain was precisely made to specifications, and they were joined together with loops and clasps of gold and bronze, ensuring the structure was unified and complete. The attention to detail and dedication to following the LORD's instructions underscored the community's commitment to creating a sacred space for worship.In the construction of the tabernacle, a covering was made of rams' skins dyed red, topped with a layer of badger skins. Boards for the structure were crafted from acacia wood, each ten cubits long and one and a half cubits wide, designed with two tenons for joining. For the south side, twenty boards were made, supported by forty silver sockets. The north side and the westward sides were similarly constructed, with a total of eight boards for the west, each supported by two silver sockets. Bars of acacia wood were made to reinforce the boards, overlaid with gold, including the rings for the bars. 

A veil of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen was crafted with cherubim designs, supported by four acacia wood pillars overlaid with gold. The entrance hanging was made from the same materials, supported by five pillars with gold decorations and brass sockets. 

Bezaleel crafted the Ark of the Covenant from acacia wood, overlaying it inside and out with pure gold, and adorned with a gold crown. Gold rings were attached for carrying. The mercy seat, also of pure gold, featured two cherubim of beaten gold at each end, facing each other with wings spread above the mercy seat. 

A table of acacia wood was made for the showbread, overlaid with pure gold and surrounded by a gold crown. Rings of gold were added for carrying. The vessels for the table, including dishes, spoons, bowls, and covers, were made of pure gold. 

The candlestick for the tabernacle was of pure gold, with a central shaft, six branches, and decorative elements like almond-shaped bowls, knops, and flowers, all of beaten work. Each branch had three bowls shaped like almonds, with a knop and a flower, mirroring the design throughout the candlestick."Make the altar of incense from acacia wood, measuring one cubit long, one cubit wide, and two cubits high, with horns of the same material. Overlay it with pure goldits top, sides, and hornsand add a gold molding around it. Make two gold rings for it under the molding on opposite sides to hold the poles used to carry it, which are to be made of acacia wood and overlaid with gold. Place the altar in front of the veil that shields the Ark of the Testimony, before the mercy seat that is over the Testimony, where I will meet with you. Aaron must burn fragrant incense on it every morning when he tends the lamps and again when he lights them at twilight so that incense will burn regularly before the LORD for the generations to come. Do not offer any unauthorized incense or burnt offering or grain offering on it, nor pour a drink offering on it. Once a year Aaron shall make atonement on its horns with the blood of the sin offering of atonement. This annual atonement must be made for the generations to come. It is most holy to the LORD."

"When you take a census of the Israelites to count them, each one must pay the LORD a ransom for his life so that no plague will come on them when you number them. Each one who crosses over to those already counted is to give a half shekel, according to the sanctuary shekel, which weighs twenty gerahs. This half shekel is an offering to the LORD. All who cross over, those twenty years old or more, are to give an offering to the LORD. The rich are not to give more than a half shekel and the poor are not to give less when you make the offering to the LORD to atone for your lives. Receive the atonement money from the Israelites and use it for the service of the Tent of Meeting. It will serve as a memorial for the Israelites before the LORD, making atonement for your lives."

"Make a bronze basin, with its bronze stand, for washing. Place it between the Tent of Meeting and the altar and put water in it. Aaron and his sons are to wash their hands and feet with water from it. Whenever they enter the Tent of Meeting, they shall wash with water so that they will not die. Also, when they approach the altar to minister by presenting a food offering to the LORD, they shall wash their hands and feet so that they will not die. This is to be a lasting ordinance for Aaron and his descendants for the generations to come."

"Take the finest spices: of liquid myrrh 500 shekels, and of sweet-smelling cinnamon half as much, that is, 250 shekels, of fragrant calamus 250 shekels, and of cassia 500 shekels, according to the sanctuary shekel, and a hin of olive oil. Make these into a sacred anointing oil, a fragrant blend, the work of a perfumer. It will be the sacred anointing oil. Then use it to anoint the Tent of Meeting, the Ark of the Testimony, the table and all its articles, the lampstand and its accessories, the altar of incense, the altar of burnt offering and all its utensils, and the basin with its stand. You shall consecrate them so they will be most holy, and whatever touches them will be holy. Anoint Aaron and his sons and consecrate them so they may serve me as priests. Say to the Israelites, 'This is to be my sacred anointing oil for the generations to come. Do not pour it on anyone else's body nor make any other oil using the same formula. It is sacred, and you are to consider it sacred. Whoever makes perfume like it and puts it on anyone other than a priest must be cut off from their people.'"

"Make a fragrant blend of incense, the work of a perfumer. It is to be salted and pure and sacred. Grind some of it to powder and place it in front of the Testimony in the Tent of Meeting, where I will meet with you. It shall be most holy to you. Do not make any incense with this formula for yourselves; consider it holy to the LORD. Whoever makes incense like it to enjoy its fragrance must be cut off from their people."The LORD instructed Moses on the creation of sacred items and practices for worship, emphasizing the importance of the Sabbath as a sign of the covenant between God and the Israelites. Bezaleel and Aholiab were appointed to craft the Tabernacle and its furnishings under divine inspiration, highlighting the significance of skilled workmanship in service to God. The Israelites were commanded to keep the Sabbath holy as a perpetual covenant, with strict penalties for those who defiled it, underscoring the Sabbath's role in maintaining their relationship with God. The narrative shifts to the people's impatience during Moses' absence, leading them to create and worship a golden calf, an act of disobedience that angers God. Despite God's wrath, Moses intercedes on behalf of the Israelites, showcasing his role as a mediator between God and his people.In the construction of the tabernacle, the candlestick was made entirely of pure gold, including its seven lamps, snuffers, and snuffdishes, crafted from a talent of pure gold. The incense altar, constructed from acacia wood, measured a cubit in length and breadth, was foursquare, and stood two cubits high with horns of the same material. It was overlaid with pure gold, including the top, sides, and horns, and featured a gold crown around it. Rings of gold were added under the crown for carrying, and the staves made of acacia wood were also overlaid with gold. Additionally, the holy anointing oil and pure incense were made according to the apothecary's craft.

The altar of burnt offering was made of acacia wood, measuring five cubits in length and breadth, and three cubits in height, foursquare, with horns overlaid with brass. All the vessels of the altar, including pots, shovels, basins, fleshhooks, and firepans, were made of brass.
