A brass grate was placed under the altar's compass, with rings at the four ends for staves, which were made of acacia wood and overlaid with brass. The altar was hollow, constructed with boards. A laver of brass was made from the mirrors of the women who assembled at the tabernacle door.

For the court, hangings of fine twined linen were made for the south, north, and west sides, with pillars and sockets of brass, and hooks and fillets of silver. The east side featured a gate with hangings of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, with pillars and sockets of brass, and hooks and fillets of silver. All the pins of the tabernacle and court were made of brass.

The materials used in the tabernacle's construction were accounted for according to Moses' commandment, under the oversight of Ithamar, Aaron's son. Bezaleel, of the tribe of Judah, and Aholiab, of the tribe of Dan, were the chief craftsmen, skilled in engraving, working, and embroidering in blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen. The total gold used was twenty-nine talents and seven hundred and thirty shekels, according to the sanctuary's shekel. The silver from those numbered in the congregation amounted to one hundred talents and one thousand seven hundred and seventy-five shekels, with a half shekel per person, as per the sanctuary's shekel, for all those numbered.Remember Abraham, Isaac, and Israel, your servants, to whom you swore by yourself, saying, "I will multiply your descendants like the stars of heaven, and all this land that I have spoken of I will give to your descendants, and they shall inherit it forever." The LORD relented from the harm which he thought to do to his people. Moses turned and went down from the mountain with the two tablets of the testimony in his hand, written on both sides. The tablets were the work of God, and the writing was the writing of God, engraved on the tablets. When Joshua heard the noise of the people shouting, he said to Moses, "There is a noise of war in the camp." But Moses said, "It is not the sound of victory, nor the sound of defeat; it is the sound of singing I hear." As soon as he came near the camp and saw the calf and the dancing, Moses' anger burned, and he threw the tablets from his hands and broke them at the foot of the mountain. He took the calf they had made, burned it with fire, ground it to powder, scattered it on the water, and made the Israelites drink it.

Moses asked Aaron, "What did this people do to you that you have brought such a great sin upon them?" Aaron replied, "Do not let your anger burn; you know the people are prone to evil. They said to me, 'Make us gods who will go before us. As for this Moses, we don't know what has happened to him.' So I told them, 'Whoever has gold, take it off.' They gave it to me, and I threw it into the fire, and out came this calf." When Moses saw that the people were running wild and that Aaron had let them get out of control, to the derision of their enemies, he stood at the camp's entrance and said, "Whoever is for the LORD, come to me." And all the Levites rallied to him. He told them, "This is what the LORD, the God of Israel, says: 'Each man strap a sword to his side. Go back and forth through the camp from one end to the other, each killing his brother and friend and neighbor.'" The Levites did as Moses commanded, and about three thousand men died that day. Moses said, "Dedicate yourselves today to the LORD, for each man has been against his son and brother, that he may bring you a blessing today."

The next day Moses said to the people, "You have committed a great sin. Now I will go up to the LORD; perhaps I can make atonement for your sin." Moses went back to the LORD and said, "Oh, these people have committed a great sin, and have made themselves gods of gold. Yet now, if you will forgive their sinbut if not, please blot me out of your book which you have written." The LORD replied to Moses, "Whoever has sinned against me, I will blot out of my book. Now go, lead the people to the place I spoke of, and my angel will go before you. However, when the time comes for me to punish, I will punish them for their sin." And the LORD struck the people with a plague because of what they did with the calf Aaron had made.

The LORD told Moses to leave and take the people up from Egypt to the land he swore to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, saying, "I will give it to your descendants. I will send an angel before you and drive out the Canaanites, Amorites, Hittites, Perizzites, Hivites, and Jebusites. Go up to a land flowing with milk and honey. But I will not go with you because you are a stiff-necked people and I might destroy you on the way." When the people heard these distressing words, they mourned and no one put on any ornaments. For the LORD had said to Moses, "Tell the Israelites, 'You are a stiff-necked people. If I were to go with you even for a moment, I might destroy you. Now take off your ornaments and I will decide what to do with you.'" So the Israelites stripped off their ornaments at Mount Horeb.

Moses took the tent and pitched it outside the camp, far off from the camp, and called it the Tent of Meeting. Anyone seeking the LORD would go out to the Tent of Meeting outside the camp. Whenever Moses went out to the tent, all the people would rise and stand at the entrance to their tents, watching Moses until he entered the tent.As Moses entered the tabernacle, the cloudy pillar descended, standing at the door, and the Lord spoke with Moses. The people saw the cloudy pillar and worshipped from their tents. The Lord and Moses spoke face to face, as friends do. Moses expressed concern about leading the people without knowing who would accompany him, despite being assured of God's favor. He requested to know God's ways more intimately, emphasizing the nation's identity as God's people. God promised His presence and rest, which Moses deemed essential for distinguishing themselves from other nations. God agreed to Moses' request because of the favor he found in God's sight.

Moses then asked to see God's glory. God responded that He would make all His goodness pass before Moses, proclaiming His name and showing mercy and grace. However, He stated that no one could see His face and live. God arranged for Moses to stand on a rock, sheltered by God's hand, to see His back as He passed by.

God instructed Moses to prepare new stone tablets like the first ones and meet Him on Mount Sinai without any company. Moses did as commanded, and God descended in a cloud, proclaiming His nature as merciful, gracious, longsuffering, and abundant in goodness and truth. He emphasized His commitment to mercy, forgiveness, and justice.

Moses quickly worshipped and pleaded for God's presence among the people, acknowledging their stubbornness and seeking forgiveness and acceptance as God's inheritance. God promised to perform unprecedented marvels for them, warning Moses to obey His commands and not to assimilate with the local inhabitants or their gods upon entering the promised land. He instructed the destruction of pagan altars and idols, emphasizing exclusive worship of the Lord and the avoidance of idolatry, including making covenants with locals or intermarrying, which could lead to idol worship. God reiterated the importance of celebrating the feast of unleavened bread and other commandments, establishing a covenant of distinction and protection for His people.In the construction of the tabernacle, the candlestick was made entirely of pure gold, including its seven lamps, snuffers, and snuffdishes, crafted from a talent of pure gold. The incense altar, constructed from acacia wood, measured a cubit in length and breadth, was foursquare, and stood two cubits high with horns of the same material. It was overlaid with pure gold, including the top, sides, and horns, and featured a gold crown around it. Rings of gold were added under the crown for carrying, and the staves made of acacia wood were also overlaid with gold. Additionally, the holy anointing oil and pure incense were made according to the apothecary's craft.

The altar of burnt offering was made of acacia wood, measuring five cubits in length and breadth, and three cubits in height, foursquare, with horns overlaid with brass. All the vessels of the altar, including pots, shovels, basins, fleshhooks, and firepans, were made of brass. A brass grate was placed under the altar's compass, with rings at the four ends for staves, which were made of acacia wood and overlaid with brass. The altar was hollow, constructed with boards. A laver of brass was made from the mirrors of the women who assembled at the tabernacle door.

For the court, hangings of fine twined linen were made for the south, north, and west sides, with pillars and sockets of brass, and hooks and fillets of silver. The east side featured a gate with hangings of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, with pillars and sockets of brass, and hooks and fillets of silver. All the pins of the tabernacle and court were made of brass.

The materials used in the tabernacle's construction were accounted for according to Moses' commandment, under the oversight of Ithamar, Aaron's son. Bezaleel, of the tribe of Judah, and Aholiab, of the tribe of Dan, were the chief craftsmen, skilled in engraving, working, and embroidering in blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen. The total gold used was twenty-nine talents and seven hundred and thirty shekels, according to the sanctuary's shekel. The silver from those numbered in the congregation amounted to one hundred talents and one thousand seven hundred and seventy-five shekels, with a half shekel per person, as per the sanctuary's shekel, for all those numbered, from twenty years old and upward, for six hundred thousand and three thousand and five hundred and fifty men. And of the hundred talents of silver were cast the sockets of the sanctuary, and the sockets of the veil; a hundred sockets of the hundred talents, a talent for a socket. And of the thousand seven hundred seventy and five shekels he made hooks for the pillars, and overlaid their chapiters, and filleted them. And the brass of the offering was seventy talents, and two thousand and four hundred shekels. Therewith he made the sockets to the door of the tabernacle of the congregation, and the brasen altar, and the brasen grate for it, and all the vessels of the altar, and the sockets of the court round about, and the sockets of the court gate, and all the pins of the tabernacle, and all the pins of the court round about.

And of the blue, and purple, and scarlet, they made cloths of service, to do service in the holy place, and made the holy garments for Aaron; as the LORD commanded Moses. He made the ephod of gold, blue, and purple, and scarlet, and fine twined linen. They did beat the gold into thin plates, and cut it into wires, to work it in the blue, and in the purple, and in the scarlet, and in the fine linen, with cunning work. They made shoulderpieces for it, to couple it together: by the two edges was it coupled together. And the curious girdle of his ephod, that was upon it, was of the same, according to the work thereof; of gold, blue, and purple, and scarlet, and fine twined linen; as the LORD commanded Moses. They wrought onyx stones inclosed in ouches of gold, graven, as signets are graven, with the names of the children of Israel. He put them on the shoulders of the ephod, that they should be stones for a memorial to the children of Israel; as the LORD commanded Moses. He made the breastplate of cunning work, like the work of the ephod; of gold, blue, and purple, and scarlet, and fine twined linen. It was foursquare; they made the breastplate double: a span was the length thereof, and a span the breadth thereof, being doubled. And they set in it four rows of stones: the first row was a sardius, a topaz, and a carbuncle: this was the first row. And the second row, an emerald, a sapphire, and a diamond. And the third row, a ligure, an agate, and an amethyst. And the fourth row, a beryl, an onyx, and a jasper: they were inclosed in ouches of gold in their inclosings. And the stones were according to the names of the children of Israel, twelve, according to their names, like the engravings of a signet, every one with his name, according to the twelve tribes. And they made upon the breastplate chains at the ends, of wreathen work of pure gold. And they made two ouches of gold, and two gold rings; and put the two rings in the two ends of the breastplate. And they put the two wreathen chains of gold in the two rings on the ends of the breastplate. And the two ends of the two wreathen chains they fastened in the two ouches, and put them on the shoulderpieces of the ephod, before it. And they made two rings of gold, and put them on the two ends of the breastplate, upon the border of it, which was on the side of the ephod inward. And they made two other golden rings, and put them on the two sides of the ephod underneath, toward the forepart of it, over against the other coupling thereof, above the curious girdle of the ephod. And they did bind the breastplate by his rings unto the rings of the ephod with a lace of blue, that it might be above the curious girdle of the ephod, and that the breastplate might not be loosed from the ephod; as the LORD commanded Moses. And he made the robe of the ephod of woven work, all of blue. And there was a hole in the midst of the robe, as the hole of an habergeon, with a band round about the hole, that it should not rend. And they made upon the hems of the robe pomegranates of blue, and purple, and scarlet, and twined linen. And they made bells of pure gold, and put the bells between the pomegranates upon the hem of the robe, round about between the pomegranates; A bell and a pomegranate, a bell and a pomegranate, round about the hem of the robe to minister in; as the LORD commanded Moses. And they made coats of fine linen of woven work for Aaron, and for his sons, And a mitre of fine linen, and goodly bonnets of fine linen, and linen breeches of fine twined linen, And a girdle of fine twined linen, and blue, and purple, and scarlet, of needlework; as the LORD commanded Moses. And they made the plate of the holy crown of pure gold, and wrote upon it a writing, like to the engravings of a signet, HOLINESS TO THE LORD. And they tied unto it a lace of blue, to fasten it on high upon the mitre; as the LORD commanded Moses.The work of the tabernacle of the tent of the congregation was completed by the children of Israel, following all the LORD's commands to Moses. They brought the tabernacle, the tent, and all its furnishings, coverings, and the veil to Moses. This included the ark of the testimony, the table with its vessels and showbread, the pure candlestick with its lamps and oil for light, the golden altar with anointing oil and sweet incense, and the hanging for the tabernacle door. Also, the bronze altar, its brass grate, staves, vessels, the laver and its foot, the court hangings, pillars, sockets, and the gate hanging, along with all service vessels and the holy garments for Aaron and his sons to minister in the priest's office, were made as the LORD commanded Moses. Moses inspected the work and blessed them for their obedience.

The LORD then instructed Moses to set up the tabernacle on the first day of the first month, place the ark of the testimony inside, and arrange the table, candlestick, and the gold altar for incense before the ark. The altar of burnt offering was to be placed before the tabernacle entrance, the laver between the tent and the altar, and the court around the tabernacle. The tabernacle and all within it were to be anointed and consecrated. Aaron and his sons were to be brought to the tabernacle entrance, washed, dressed in holy garments, anointed, and sanctified to serve as priests. This anointing established an everlasting priesthood through their generations.

Moses did everything as the LORD commanded. On the first day of the first month in the second year, the tabernacle was erected. Moses set up its structure, covered it, placed the ark with the testimony inside, arranged the table, candlestick, and the golden altar, and offered incense and burnt offerings as the LORD had instructed.In the month of Abib, as commanded, you shall celebrate the feast of unleavened bread, commemorating your exodus from Egypt. Every firstborn among your livestock, whether ox or sheep, is mine. However, the firstborn of an ass must be redeemed with a lamb, or its neck broken. All your firstborn sons you must redeem. No one shall appear before me empty-handed. Work six days, but rest on the seventh, even during plowing and harvest seasons. Observe the feast of weeks with the firstfruits of wheat harvest, and the feast of ingathering at year's end. Thrice a year, all your men shall appear before the LORD God, the God of Israel. I will ensure your lands are undisturbed during these times by casting out nations and enlarging your borders. Do not offer my sacrifice with leaven, and ensure the passover sacrifice is not left until morning. Bring the first of your land's firstfruits to the LORD's house. Do not cook a young goat in its mother's milk.

The LORD instructed Moses to write these commands as they form the covenant with Israel. Moses spent forty days and nights with the LORD without eating or drinking, and wrote the covenant's words, the ten commandments, on the tablets. Upon descending from Mount Sinai, Moses' face shone, though he was unaware. Aaron and the Israelites were initially afraid to approach him, but Moses called them, and communicated all the LORD had instructed. He covered his face with a veil after speaking, removing it only to speak with the LORD or relay His commands to the people.

Moses then gathered the Israelites to convey the LORD's commands, emphasizing a sabbath of rest on the seventh day, during which no work or fire lighting is permitted. He called for contributions for the LORD from those willing, specifying materials like gold, silver, brass, fine linens, and oils. He detailed the construction of the tabernacle and its furnishings, the ark, the table for showbread, the candlestick, and the altars for burnt offerings and incense, along with the priestly garments. The community responded, bringing materials and crafting the tabernacle and its contents as commanded.Moses set the laver between the tent of the congregation and the altar, filling it with water for washing. Moses, Aaron, and his sons used it to wash their hands and feet before entering the tent of the congregation or approaching the altar, following the LORD's command. Moses then erected the court around the tabernacle and altar and set up the court gate's hanging, completing the work. A cloud covered the tent of the congregation, and the glory of the LORD filled the tabernacle, preventing Moses from entering. The cloud's presence directed the Israelites' journeys; they moved when it lifted and stayed when it remained. The cloud was over the tabernacle by day and fire by night, visible to all Israelites.

In Leviticus, the LORD speaks to Moses from the tabernacle, instructing on offerings. For a burnt offering from the herd, a male without blemish should be offered voluntarily. The offerer places his hand on the offering's head for atonement. Aaron's sons, the priests, sprinkle its blood around the altar. The offering is cut into pieces, with the priests arranging the wood and fire on the altar, burning the offering as a sweet savour to the LORD. Offerings can also be from the flock or fowls, with specific instructions for preparation and offering to ensure a pleasing aroma to the LORD. Meat offerings should be of fine flour with oil and frankincense, with parts burned on the altar as a memorial, and the remainder for Aaron and his sons. Different preparations like baked, pan, or frying pan offerings are detailed, emphasizing the use of fine flour and oil.In the month of Abib, celebrate the feast of unleavened bread, remembering your exodus from Egypt. Dedicate every firstborn livestock to me, but redeem the firstborn of an ass with a lamb. Redeem all your firstborn sons. No one shall appear before me empty-handed. Work six days and rest on the seventh, even during plowing and harvest. Observe the feast of weeks with the firstfruits of wheat harvest, and the feast of ingathering at year's end. Thrice a year, all men shall appear before the LORD God. I will protect your lands during these times by casting out nations and enlarging your borders. Do not offer my sacrifice with leaven, and do not leave the passover sacrifice until morning. Bring the first of your land's firstfruits to the LORD's house. Do not cook a young goat in its mother's milk.

Moses was instructed to write these commands as the covenant with Israel. He spent forty days and nights with the LORD, writing the ten commandments on tablets. Upon descending, Moses' face shone, though he was unaware. Aaron and the Israelites were initially afraid to approach him. Moses communicated all the LORD had instructed and covered his face with a veil after speaking. He gathered the Israelites to convey the LORD's commands, emphasizing a sabbath of rest and calling for contributions for the LORD from those willing, specifying materials for the tabernacle and its furnishings. The community responded, bringing materials and crafting the tabernacle as commanded.

Men and women, willing-hearted, brought gold, silver, brass, fine linens, and other materials for the tabernacle and holy garments. The rulers brought onyx stones and other precious items for the ephod and breastplate. Bezaleel and Aholiab, filled with the spirit of God, led the work in crafting the sanctuary, as the LORD had commanded. The people brought more than enough materials, prompting Moses to halt further contributions. The skilled workers made the tabernacle with fine twined linen, blue, purple, and scarlet, and cherubims of cunning work. They made curtains, loops, and taches of gold and brass to couple the tent together, ensuring it was one unified structure.He made a covering for the tent of rams' skins dyed red, and a covering of badgers' skins above that. Boards for the tabernacle were made of shittim wood, standing up. Each board was ten cubits long and one and a half cubits wide, with two tenons equally distant from each other. For the tabernacle's south side, twenty boards were made, and forty silver sockets were placed under them. Similarly, for the north side, twenty boards and forty silver sockets were made. For the tabernacle's west side, six boards were constructed, with two additional boards for the corners. These were coupled together at the bottom and the top to one ring, resulting in eight boards and sixteen silver sockets. Bars of shittim wood were made for the sides of the tabernacle, with the middle bar shooting through the boards from one end to the other. The boards were overlaid with gold, and their rings, made of gold, served as places for the bars, which were also overlaid with gold.

A veil of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen was made, featuring cherubims of cunning work. Four pillars of shittim wood were made for it, overlaid with gold, with gold hooks and four silver sockets. An hanging for the tabernacle door was made of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, of needlework, supported by five pillars with gold chapiters and fillets, but their five sockets were of brass.

Bezaleel made the ark of shittim wood, two and a half cubits long, a cubit and a half wide, and a cubit and a half high, overlaying it with pure gold inside and out, and adding a gold crown around it. Four gold rings were cast for it, to be set by its four corners, and staves of shittim wood, overlaid with gold, were made to bear the ark. The mercy seat was made of pure gold, two and a half cubits long and one and a half cubits wide, with two cherubims of gold beaten out of one piece on the two ends. The cherubims had their wings spread out on high, covering the mercy seat, facing each other.

He also made the table of shittim wood, two cubits long, a cubit wide, and a cubit and a half high, overlaying it with pure gold and adding a gold crown around it. A border of a handbreadth was made around it, with a gold crown for the border. Four gold rings were cast for it, placed on the four corners at its four feet. Staves of shittim wood, overlaid with gold, were made to bear the table. The vessels for the table, including dishes, spoons, bowls, and covers, were made of pure gold.

The candlestick was made of pure gold, of beaten work, including its shaft, branches, bowls, knops, and flowers. Six branches extended from its sides, three from one side and three from the other, each with three bowls made like almonds, a knop, and a flower. The candlestick itself had four bowls made like almonds, with knops and flowers.Moses set the laver between the tent of the congregation and the altar, filling it with water for washing. Moses, Aaron, and his sons used it to wash their hands and feet before entering the tent of the congregation or approaching the altar, as commanded by the LORD. Moses then erected the court around the tabernacle and altar, setting up the court gate's hanging, thus completing the work. A cloud covered the tent of the congregation, and the glory of the LORD filled the tabernacle, preventing Moses from entering. The presence of the cloud directed the Israelites' journeys; they moved when it lifted and stayed when it remained. By day, the cloud was over the tabernacle, and by night it appeared as fire, visible to all Israelites.

In Leviticus, the LORD instructs Moses from the tabernacle on offerings. For a burnt offering from the herd, a male without blemish should be offered voluntarily. The offerer places his hand on the offering's head for atonement. Aaron's sons, the priests, sprinkle its blood around the altar. The offering is cut into pieces, with the priests arranging the wood and fire on the altar, burning the offering as a sweet savour to the LORD. Offerings can also be from the flock or fowls, with specific instructions for preparation and offering to ensure a pleasing aroma to the LORD. Meat offerings should be of fine flour with oil and frankincense, with parts burned on the altar as a memorial, and the remainder for Aaron and his sons. Different preparations like baked, pan, or frying pan offerings are detailed, emphasizing the use of fine flour and oil.

The priest shall take from the meat offering a memorial thereof, and burn it upon the altar as an offering made by fire, of a sweet savour unto the LORD. That which is left of the meat offering shall be Aaron's and his sons': it is most holy of the offerings of the LORD made by fire. No meat offering brought to the LORD shall be made with leaven or honey. For the oblation of the firstfruits, they shall not be burnt on the altar for a sweet savour. Every meat offering shall be seasoned with salt, the covenant of God not to be lacking from the meat offering; with all offerings, salt shall be offered. For a meat offering of the firstfruits, green ears of corn dried by the fire, even corn beaten out of full ears, shall be offered. Oil and frankincense shall be put upon it, making it a meat offering. The priest shall burn the memorial of it, part of the beaten corn and oil, with all the frankincense, as an offering made by fire unto the LORD.

For a sacrifice of peace offering, whether from the herd or flock, male or female, it shall be offered without blemish. The offerer shall lay his hand upon the head of the offering, and it shall be killed at the door of the tabernacle of the congregation; Aaron's sons shall sprinkle the blood upon the altar round about. The fat covering the inwards and all the fat upon the inwards, the two kidneys, and the fat on them by the flanks, and the caul above the liver, with the kidneys, shall be taken away and burned on the altar as an offering made by fire, of a sweet savour unto the LORD. If the offering is a goat, the same procedure follows, with the priest burning the fat upon the altar as the food of the offering made by fire for a sweet savour; all the fat is the LORD's. It shall be a perpetual statute that neither fat nor blood shall be eaten.

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying, if a soul sins through ignorance against any of the commandments of the LORD concerning things which ought not to be done, and does against any of them: If the priest that is anointed sins according to the sin of the people, he shall bring for his sin a young bullock without blemish unto the LORD for a sin offering. He shall bring the bullock to the door of the tabernacle of the congregation before the LORD, lay his hand upon the bullock's head, and kill the bullock before the LORD. The priest shall take of the bullock's blood to the tabernacle of the congregation, dip his finger in the blood, and sprinkle the blood seven times before the LORD.Bezaleel crafted the candlestick entirely of pure gold, with its knops and branches forming a single piece of beaten work. He also made seven lamps, snuffers, and snuffdishes of pure gold, using a talent of gold for these items. The incense altar, made of shittim wood, measured a cubit in length and breadth, was foursquare, and stood two cubits high, with its horns of the same material. It was overlaid with pure gold on the top, sides, and horns, and adorned with a gold crown. Gold rings were added under the crown at two corners for carrying. The staves for carrying the altar were made of shittim wood and overlaid with gold. Additionally, Bezaleel made the holy anointing oil and pure incense of sweet spices.

The altar of burnt offering was constructed of shittim wood, measuring five cubits in length and breadth, and three cubits in height, with horns on its four corners overlaid with brass. All vessels of the altar, including pots, shovels, basins, fleshhooks, and firepans, were made of brass. A brasen grate of network was placed under the compass of the altar, with four rings at its four ends for the staves, which were made of shittim wood and overlaid with brass. The altar was hollow with boards. The laver and its foot were made of brass from the mirrors of the women who assembled at the tabernacle door.

For the court, hangings of fine twined linen were made for the south, north, and west sides, with their respective pillars and sockets. The east side featured hangings for the gate of fifteen cubits on each side. All hangings of the court were of fine twined linen, with brass sockets for the pillars, and silver hooks and fillets. The hanging for the gate of the court was of blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen, twenty cubits in length. All pins of the tabernacle and court were of brass.

The materials used in the tabernacle, as commanded by Moses, were accounted for by the Levites under Ithamar, Aaron's son. Bezaleel, son of Uri, of the tribe of Judah, and Aholiab, son of Ahisamach, of the tribe of Dan, crafted all items as commanded by the LORD. They were skilled in engraving, cunning work, and embroidery in blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen. The gold used in the holy place was twenty-nine talents and seven hundred and thirty shekels, according to the sanctuary shekel. The silver from the numbered congregation amounted to one hundred talents and one thousand seven hundred seventy-five shekels, with a bekah per person, half a shekel according to the sanctuary shekel, for everyone counted.The priest shall put some of the blood on the horns of the altar of sweet incense before the LORD in the tabernacle of the congregation and pour the rest at the base of the altar of the burnt offering at the tabernacle's entrance. He shall remove all the fat of the sin offering bull, including the fat covering the innards and all fat upon them, the two kidneys, and the fat on them by the flanks, and the caul above the liver with the kidneys. This is similar to the removal for the peace offering sacrifice, and the priest shall burn them on the altar of burnt offering. The bull's skin, flesh, head, legs, innards, and dung shall be taken outside the camp to a clean place where ashes are poured out and burned on wood with fire; this place shall be where he is burnt.

If the whole congregation of Israel sins through ignorance and the sin is hidden from the assembly but they have violated any of the LORD's commandments unintentionally, they are guilty. Once the sin is recognized, the congregation shall offer a young bull for the sin and bring it before the tabernacle of the congregation. The elders shall lay their hands on the bull's head before the LORD, and it shall be killed. The anointed priest shall bring the bull's blood inside the tabernacle, dip his finger in the blood, sprinkle it seven times before the LORD, before the veil, put some blood on the horns of the altar within the tabernacle, and pour out the rest at the base of the altar of burnt offering at the entrance. He shall remove all the fat and burn it on the altar. The priest shall make atonement for them, and they shall be forgiven. The bull shall be carried outside the camp and burned as the first bull was; it is a sin offering for the congregation.

When a ruler sins through ignorance against any of the LORD's commandments and is guilty, or if his sin comes to his knowledge, he shall bring a male goat without blemish as his offering. He shall lay his hand on the goat's head, kill it at the place of the burnt offering before the LORD; it is a sin offering. The priest shall take some of the sin offering's blood, put it on the horns of the altar of burnt offering, and pour out the rest at the base of the altar. He shall burn all the fat on the altar, as with the peace offering, and make atonement for the ruler's sin, which shall be forgiven.

If any of the common people sin through ignorance against the LORD's commandments and are guilty, or if their sin comes to their knowledge, they shall bring a female goat without blemish for their sin. They shall lay their hand on the sin offering's head, kill it in the place of the burnt offering. The priest shall take some of the blood, put it on the horns of the altar of burnt offering, and pour out the rest at the base of the altar. He shall remove all the fat, as with the peace offering, and burn it on the altar for a sweet savour to the LORD; the priest shall make atonement, and it shall be forgiven. If a lamb is brought for a sin offering, it must be a female without blemish. The procedure for the sin offering shall be the same as for the goat, ensuring atonement and forgiveness.From twenty years old and upward, the count was six hundred thousand and three thousand and five hundred and fifty men. For the sanctuary's construction, one hundred talents of silver were used to cast the sockets of the sanctuary and the veil; each socket was made from a talent of silver. Additionally, one thousand seven hundred seventy-five shekels of silver were used to make hooks for the pillars, overlay their capitals, and fillet them. The brass offering amounted to seventy talents and two thousand and four hundred shekels. This brass was used for the sockets at the tabernacle of the congregation's door, the bronze altar and its grate, and all the altar's vessels, as well as the sockets of the court round about, the court gate, and all the pins of the tabernacle and court.

Cloths of service were made from blue, purple, and scarlet, and the holy garments for Aaron were crafted as the LORD commanded Moses. The ephod was made of gold, blue, purple, scarlet, and fine twined linen. Gold was beaten into thin plates and cut into wires to work into the blue, purple, scarlet, and fine linen with cunning work. Shoulder pieces were made for the ephod, coupled together at the edges. The ephod's curious girdle was of the same materials and craftsmanship as commanded by the LORD. Onyx stones set in gold ouches were engraved with the names of the children of Israel and placed on the ephod's shoulders as a memorial. The breastplate was made with the same craftsmanship as the ephod, set with four rows of stones corresponding to the twelve tribes of Israel, and had chains of pure gold. The robe of the ephod was all of blue with a hole in the middle, similar to an habergeon, and had a band around the hole to prevent tearing. Pomegranates of blue, purple, scarlet, and twined linen were made for the robe's hems, with bells of pure gold placed between them. Coats of fine linen, mitres, bonnets, linen breeches, and a girdle of fine twined linen, blue, purple, and scarlet needlework were made for Aaron and his sons as the LORD commanded Moses. The holy crown was made of pure gold with "HOLINESS TO THE LORD" engraved on it, fastened with a lace of blue on the mitre as commanded by the LORD.If a person sins by hearing a public adjuration to testify and, being a witness, either has seen or knows of the matter yet does not speak up, they bear their guilt. If someone touches anything unclean, whether the carcass of an unclean wild animal, unclean livestock, or unclean swarming things, and it is hidden from them, they are unclean and guilty. Or if they touch human uncleannessanything that would make them uncleanand it is hidden from them, when they come to know it, they will be guilty. If someone swears rashly to do evil or goodany sort of rash oath that people might swearand it is hidden from them, when they come to know it, they will be guilty in any of these matters. They must confess the sin they have committed, bring a female from the flock, a lamb or a goat, as a sin offering to make atonement for their sin. If unable to bring a lamb, they must bring two doves or two young pigeons to the LORD, one for a sin offering and the other for a burnt offering. The priest will make atonement for them, and they will be forgiven. If they cannot afford two doves or two young pigeons, they must bring as their offering for the sin they committed a tenth of an ephah of fine flour for a sin offering. The priest will make atonement for them for any of these sins, and they will be forgiven. For a trespass in the holy things of the LORD, they must bring a ram without blemish and make restitution for what they have failed to do in the holy things, adding a fifth to it. The priest will make atonement with the ram of the trespass offering, and they will be forgiven. If someone sins by violating any of the LORD's commandments without realizing it, they are guilty and must bring a ram without blemish as a trespass offering. The priest will make atonement for them, and they will be forgiven. If someone deceives their neighbor in a matter of deposit or security, or through robbery, or if they have defrauded their neighbor, or found something lost and lied about it, or sworn falsely, they must restore what they took by robbery or fraud, or the deposit entrusted to them, or the lost thing they found, or anything about which they have sworn falsely. They must make restitution in full, add a fifth more, and bring a ram without blemish as a trespass offering to the LORD.The work of the tabernacle of the tent of the congregation was completed by the children of Israel, following all the LORD's commands to Moses. They brought the tabernacle, the tent, and all its furnishings, coverings, and the veil to Moses. This included the ark of the testimony, the mercy seat, the table with its vessels and the shewbread, the pure candlestick with its lamps and oil for light, the golden altar with the anointing oil and sweet incense, and the brasen altar with its brass grate, laver, and all its vessels. The court's hangings, pillars, and the court gate's hanging, along with all service vessels, were also presented. The cloths of service and the holy garments for Aaron and his sons to minister in the priest's office were made as commanded by the LORD.

Moses inspected all the work and blessed the people for their obedience. The LORD then instructed Moses to set up the tabernacle on the first day of the first month, place the ark of the testimony inside, and arrange the table, candlestick, and the gold altar for incense before it. The altar of burnt offering was to be placed at the tabernacle's entrance, with the laver between the tent of the congregation and the altar. The court was to be set up with its hangings. The tabernacle and all within it were to be anointed and consecrated, making them holy, along with the altar of burnt offering and its vessels, and the laver and its base.

Aaron and his sons were to be brought to the tabernacle's entrance, washed, and dressed in holy garments. Aaron was to be anointed and sanctified to minister as a priest, and his sons were to be clothed and anointed for a perpetual priesthood. Moses did everything as the LORD commanded. On the first day of the first month in the second year, the tabernacle was erected. Moses set up the structure, placed the ark with the testimony inside, arranged the table, and set the bread upon it as the LORD had instructed. The candlestick was placed and lit, the golden altar was set for incense, and the burnt offering altar was placed at the tabernacle's entrance where Moses made offerings as commanded by the LORD.The priest shall make atonement for him before the LORD, and he will be forgiven for any trespasses. The LORD instructed Moses on the law of the burnt offering, which is to remain on the altar all night until morning, with the fire kept burning. The priest is to wear linen garments while handling the ashes of the burnt offering, which are then to be taken outside the camp to a clean place. The fire on the altar must never go out, and the priest is to add wood every morning and arrange the burnt offering and the fat of the peace offerings on it.

The law of the meat offering requires Aaron's sons to present it before the LORD. A portion of the flour, oil, and all the frankincense on the meat offering is to be burned as a sweet aroma to the LORD. The remainder is for Aaron and his sons to eat in a holy place without leaven, as it is considered most holy, like the sin and trespass offerings. This statute is eternal, and anyone who touches these offerings will be considered holy.

Aaron and his sons are to offer a meat offering to the LORD on the day he is anointed, consisting of fine flour with oil, baked and divided into two parts for morning and evening offerings. This offering is to be completely burned, a perpetual statute for the priests, and must not be eaten.

The sin offering is to be killed in the same place as the burnt offering and is most holy. The priest who offers it shall eat it in a holy place. Anything that touches its flesh becomes holy. If any of its blood is sprinkled on a garment, the garment must be washed in a holy place. An earthen vessel used to cook the offering must be broken, while a bronze pot must be scoured and rinsed. All male priests may eat it, but no sin offering blood brought into the tabernacle shall be eaten; it must be burned.

The law of the trespass offering states it is most holy. It is to be killed in the same place as the burnt offering, with its blood sprinkled around the altar. The priest is to offer all its fat, including the rump and internal fat, and burn them as an offering to the LORD. Every male priest may eat it in a holy place. The sin offering and trespass offering share the same law; the priest who makes atonement with it shall have it. The priest offering a burnt offering shall keep its skin, and all meat offerings, whether baked, fried, or prepared in a pan, belong to the priest who offers them.Moses set the laver between the tent of the congregation and the altar, filling it with water for washing. Moses, Aaron, and his sons used it to wash their hands and feet before entering the tent of the congregation or approaching the altar, as commanded by the LORD. Moses then completed the setup by erecting the court around the tabernacle and altar and hanging the court gate. Upon finishing, a cloud covered the tent of the congregation, and the glory of the LORD filled the tabernacle, preventing Moses from entering. The cloud's presence indicated when the Israelites should journey or stay. The cloud of the LORD was over the tabernacle by day, and fire was on it by night, visible to all Israelites throughout their journeys.

The LORD then spoke to Moses from the tabernacle, instructing him on offerings. For a burnt offering from the herd, a male without blemish was required, to be offered voluntarily at the tabernacle entrance. The offerer was to lay hands on the offering, symbolizing acceptance and atonement. Aaron's sons, the priests, would sprinkle its blood around the altar, cut the offering into pieces, and burn it as a pleasing aroma to the LORD. Offerings could also include flocks or fowls, each with specific instructions for preparation and offering to ensure a sweet savour unto the LORD.

For grain offerings, fine flour with oil and frankincense was to be brought to Aaron's sons. A portion would be burned on the altar as a memorial, with the remainder for Aaron and his sons, considered most holy. Grain offerings could be baked in various ways, with specific instructions for each to ensure they were acceptable to the LORD.The law of the sacrifice of peace offerings is detailed, specifying offerings for thanksgiving, including unleavened cakes mingled with oil, unleavened wafers anointed with oil, and fried cakes of fine flour. Additionally, leavened bread is to accompany the thanksgiving peace offerings. A portion of these offerings is designated as a heave offering to the LORD, handled by the priest who sprinkles the blood of the peace offerings. The flesh of these offerings must be consumed on the day they are offered, with no leftovers by morning. If the offering is a vow or voluntary, it can be eaten the next day, but any remaining by the third day must be burned. Consuming any of this offering on the third day disqualifies it, making it unacceptable and the consumer bearing iniquity. Flesh touching anything unclean must not be eaten and is to be burned. Only those who are clean may eat of the offerings, and anyone unclean consuming the offerings will be cut off from their people.

The LORD commands that no fat from oxen, sheep, or goats be eaten, and the fat of animals that die naturally or are torn by beasts is forbidden for consumption but can be used for other purposes. Eating the fat of an animal offered to the LORD results in being cut off from one's people. Similarly, consuming any blood is strictly prohibited, with violators being cut off from their community.

Instructions are given for presenting peace offerings to the LORD, including how to handle the fat and the breast for a wave offering, and the right shoulder for a heave offering. Specific portions of these offerings are designated for Aaron and his sons, establishing a perpetual statute. This section concludes with a summary of the laws for various offerings and the consecration of Aaron and his sons, as commanded by the LORD to Moses on Mount Sinai. For grain offerings, fine flour with oil and frankincense was to be brought to Aaron's sons. A portion would be burned on the altar as a memorial, with the remainder for Aaron and his sons, considered most holy. Grain offerings could be baked in various ways, with specific instructions for each to ensure they were acceptable to the LORD.

No meat offering brought to the LORD shall be made with leaven or honey. Oblations of the firstfruits are to be offered to the LORD but not burnt on the altar. Every meat offering must be seasoned with salt, symbolizing the covenant with God. For a meat offering of the firstfruits, green ears of corn dried by the fire, beaten out of full ears, should be used. Oil and frankincense are to be added to these offerings, which the priest will burn as a memorial on the altar.

If offering a sacrifice of peace from the herd, it must be without blemish. The offerer shall lay hands on the offering and kill it at the tabernacle entrance. Aaron's sons will sprinkle the blood around the altar. The fat covering the inwards and all other specified fats must be offered as a fire sacrifice to the LORD. This applies to offerings from the flock as well, with specific instructions for lambs and goats.

It is a perpetual statute that neither fat nor blood shall be eaten. If a soul sins through ignorance against the LORD's commandments, a sin offering of a young bullock without blemish must be brought. The anointed priest shall bring the bullock's blood into the tabernacle, sprinkle it seven times before the LORD, symbolizing purification and atonement for the sin.Moses said to the congregation that they were to do as the LORD commanded. He then prepared Aaron and his sons for their priestly duties, washing them and dressing them in their sacred garments, including the ephod and breastplate with the Urim and Thummim. Moses anointed the tabernacle and all within it, sanctifying them with oil and blood, as per the LORD's instructions. Aaron and his sons were anointed to sanctify them for their service to the LORD.

Moses conducted offerings, including a sin offering and burnt offerings, following the LORD's commands meticulously. He placed the blood of the offerings on Aaron and his sons as part of their consecration, signifying their purification and readiness to serve. The offerings were made by fire, a pleasing aroma to the LORD. Moses also performed wave offerings with parts of the sacrifices and the unleavened bread, indicating the offerings' acceptance by the LORD.

Aaron and his sons were instructed to boil the flesh of the offerings and eat it with unleavened bread as part of their consecration, with any leftovers to be burned. They were to remain at the tabernacle's entrance for seven days, completing their consecration process, ensuring they followed the LORD's charge to avoid death. This period of consecration was a direct command from the LORD to atone and prepare them for their priestly duties. Aaron and his sons followed all the LORD's commands through Moses, marking the beginning of their service. On the eighth day, Moses gathered Aaron, his sons, and the elders of Israel to continue with the LORD's instructions.The LORD instructed that some of the blood from the sin offering should be placed on the horns of the altar of sweet incense, with the remainder poured at the base of the burnt offering altar. All the fat, kidneys, and liver from the offering were to be removed and burned on the altar. The entire bull, including its skin, flesh, head, legs, inwards, and dung, was to be taken outside the camp to a clean place and burned.

If the whole congregation of Israel sinned unknowingly, they were to offer a young bull for the sin once it was realized. The elders would lay their hands on the bull's head, and it would be killed before the LORD. The anointed priest would then bring the bull's blood into the tabernacle, sprinkle it seven times before the LORD, and place some on the altar's horns. The fat was to be burned on the altar to make atonement, and the bull was to be burned outside the camp.

For a ruler who sinned unknowingly, a male goat without blemish was to be offered. The ruler would lay his hand on the goat's head, kill it, and the priest would apply some of the blood to the altar's horns and pour out the rest at the base. The fat was burned on the altar to make atonement, and the sin would be forgiven.

If a common person sinned unknowingly, they were to bring a female goat without blemish for their sin. They would lay their hand on its head, kill it, and the priest would handle the blood in the same manner as for the ruler's offering. The fat was burned on the altar for a pleasing aroma to the LORD, making atonement for the individual.

For a sin offering, a lamb could also be brought. It had to be a female without blemish. The procedure for offering the lamb was similar to that for the goat, with the blood and fat handled in the same way to make atonement for the sin.The fat from the sacrifice is to be burned on the altar as an offering to the LORD, making atonement for the individual's sin, which will then be forgiven. If a person hears an oath and knows of the sin but does not speak out, they bear the guilt. Touching any unclean thing, whether knowingly or unknowingly, results in guilt and uncleanness. Swearing to do something, either good or evil, and forgetting about it also results in guilt once the person remembers. To atone for such sins, a person must confess and bring a sin offering to the LORD, which could be a lamb, kid of the goats, two turtledoves, or two young pigeons, depending on their ability. If unable to bring these, a tenth of an ephah of fine flour without oil or frankincense is acceptable. The priest will then perform rituals to make atonement, and the sin will be forgiven.

For trespasses against the holy things of the LORD done unknowingly, a ram without blemish and a compensation plus a fifth part extra are to be offered for atonement. Similarly, for sins committed out of ignorance against the LORD's commandments, a ram is offered for atonement and forgiveness. Trespasses involving deceit or theft require restitution plus a fifth part extra, and a ram without blemish as a trespass offering to the LORD for atonement and forgiveness.Aaron was instructed to offer a young calf for a sin offering and a ram for a burnt offering, both without blemish, before the LORD. He was also to tell the Israelites to bring a kid of the goats for a sin offering, and a calf and a lamb, both of the first year and without blemish, for a burnt offering, along with a bullock and a ram for peace offerings, and a meat offering mingled with oil, as the LORD would appear to them that day. Following Moses' commands, the offerings were brought before the tabernacle, and the congregation stood before the LORD. Moses emphasized that these actions were commanded by the LORD and that His glory would appear to them.

Aaron went to the altar to offer the sin offering and burnt offering for himself and the people, as instructed. He killed the calf for his sin offering and followed the LORD's commands for the offering, including burning the fat, kidneys, and liver on the altar and the flesh and hide outside the camp. Aaron and his sons then handled the blood of the burnt offering, sprinkling it around the altar, and presented the burnt offering in pieces, which Aaron burned on the altar. The sin offering for the people was handled similarly, with Aaron slaughtering the goat and offering it as prescribed.

Aaron also offered the meat offering and the peace offerings, following the LORD's instructions for each. The fat of the peace offerings was burned on the altar, and Aaron waved the breasts and right shoulder as a wave offering before the LORD. After completing the offerings, Aaron blessed the people, and he and Moses entered and then exited the tabernacle to bless the people again, at which point the LORD's glory appeared to all, and a fire from the LORD consumed the offerings on the altar, leading the people to shout and fall on their faces.

However, Nadab and Abihu, Aaron's sons, offered unauthorized fire before the LORD, which was not commanded, and were consumed by fire from the LORD, resulting in their death. Moses reminded Aaron that the LORD demands to be sanctified by those who come near Him and glorified before all the people. Aaron's remaining sons were instructed not to show signs of mourning in a way that would bring wrath upon the people but to let the house of Israel mourn for them. They were also warned not to leave the tabernacle's entrance to avoid death, as they were anointed with the LORD's oil. The LORD then instructed Aaron and his sons not to drink wine or strong drink when entering the tabernacle to distinguish between the holy and unholy, and clean and unclean, and to teach the Israelites the LORD's statutes as conveyed by Moses.The LORD instructed Moses on the laws of various offerings, including the trespass offering, burnt offering, meat offering, and sin offering. For a trespass, one must bring a ram to the priest for atonement. The burnt offering is to be kept burning on the altar throughout the night until morning, symbolizing a continuous commitment to God. The priest, wearing linen garments, is responsible for collecting the ashes of the burnt offering and placing them beside the altar, signifying the removal of sins. The fire on the altar must never go out, representing God's eternal presence.

The meat offering involves the sons of Aaron presenting flour, oil, and frankincense on the altar, with part of it burned and the remainder eaten by the priests in a holy place, emphasizing the sharing of God's provisions. This offering is a perpetual statute, highlighting the ongoing relationship between God and His people. The sin offering, also most holy, is to be eaten by the priests in a designated holy place, underscoring the sanctity of the offerings and the role of the priests as mediators between God and the Israelites.

The laws also specify how offerings should be prepared and consumed, ensuring that they are treated with reverence. The offerings, whether burnt, meat, sin, or trespass, are all considered most holy, and their handling is strictly regulated to maintain their sanctity. These rituals reinforce the importance of obedience, atonement, and the sanctification of the community through offerings made by fire to the LORD.Aaron and his remaining sons, Eleazar and Ithamar, were instructed to take the remaining meat offering from the LORD's fire offerings and eat it without leaven beside the altar, as it is most holy. They were to eat it in the holy place, as it was their due from the sacrifices made by fire, as commanded by the LORD. The wave breast and heave shoulder were to be eaten in a clean place by Aaron, his sons, and daughters, as their due from the peace offerings of the Israelites. Moses, concerned about the proper handling of the offerings, found the goat of the sin offering burnt and questioned Eleazar and Ithamar for not eating it in the holy place as it was most holy and meant for atonement. Aaron explained the day's events and his state of mourning, questioning if eating the sin offering would have been acceptable to the LORD. Moses was satisfied with Aaron's response.

The LORD then spoke to Moses and Aaron, detailing the dietary laws for the Israelites, specifying which animals, fish, and birds were clean and could be eaten, and which were unclean and should be avoided. This included instructions on cloven-footed animals, those that chew the cud, and those with fins and scales. The LORD also specified which flying insects were clean and could be eaten. Touching or carrying the carcasses of unclean animals would render a person unclean until the evening, requiring them to wash their clothes to become clean again. These laws distinguished between clean and unclean animals, guiding the Israelites on what was permissible to eat.The law of the sacrifice of peace offerings to the LORD includes offering unleavened cakes mingled with oil, unleavened wafers anointed with oil, and fried cakes of fine flour with oil. Leavened bread is also offered with the sacrifice of thanksgiving. A portion is given as a heave offering to the LORD, and the priests who sprinkle the blood of the peace offerings receive it. The flesh of the sacrifice must be eaten the same day for thanksgiving offerings, with no leftovers until the morning. Vow or voluntary offerings can be eaten the same day and the remainder the next day, but any remaining on the third day must be burnt. If any flesh is eaten on the third day, it will not be accepted, and the eater bears iniquity. Flesh touching anything unclean must be burnt; only the clean may eat of it. Eating the flesh while unclean, or eating any fat or blood, results in being cut off from the people. The LORD commands offerings made by fire, including the fat and the breast for a wave offering, and the right shoulder for a heave offering to the priests. This portion is for Aaron and his sons as a statute forever. The LORD outlines the laws for various offerings and consecrations, commanded at Mount Sinai. Moses is instructed to take Aaron, his sons, garments, anointing oil, a bullock for sin offering, two rams, and unleavened bread, and gather the congregation at the tabernacle's entrance, following the LORD's commands.The LORD detailed further laws regarding unclean animals, including various creeping things like the weasel, mouse, tortoise, ferret, chameleon, lizard, snail, and mole. These were declared unclean, and touching their dead bodies would render a person unclean until evening. Any object that a dead creature fell on must be washed to be cleansed. Earthen vessels contaminated in this way must be broken. Food or drink in contact with such water becomes unclean, as do ovens and cooking ranges, which must be destroyed. However, a spring or pit with plenty of water remains clean, though anything touching a carcass becomes unclean. Seeds contaminated by a carcass are clean unless they are wet when the carcass touches them. Touching or eating the carcass of a clean animal also requires washing and results in uncleanliness until evening.

Creeping things that move on the earth are not to be eaten and are considered abominable. The Israelites are instructed not to defile themselves with these creatures, to remain holy as the LORD is holy. This law distinguishes between clean and unclean animals and what may or may not be eaten.

The LORD then addresses purification after childbirth, stating a woman is unclean for seven days after bearing a son and for two weeks after a daughter. Circumcision occurs on the eighth day for a son. The purification period lasts thirty-three days for a son and sixty-six days for a daughter, during which the mother cannot touch anything sacred or enter the sanctuary. At the end of her purification, she must offer a lamb and a bird for a sin offering, or two birds if she cannot afford a lamb, to be cleansed of her blood issue.

The fat, rump, and right shoulder of this ram, along with unleavened bread, were waved as an offering before the LORD and then burnt on the altar. 

Moses then took the breast of the ram and waved it as a wave offering, keeping it as his portion. Aaron and his sons followed all the LORD's instructions through Moses. On the eighth day, Moses called Aaron, his sons, and the elders of Israel to continue with the ceremonies.The priest shall shut up the person with the plague for seven days. On the seventh day, if the plague has not spread and appears stable, the priest shall shut him up for another seven days. If the plague becomes somewhat dark and does not spread, the priest shall pronounce him clean after he washes his clothes. However, if the scab spreads after initial examination, the priest must examine him again. If the scab has spread, the priest shall pronounce him unclean due to leprosy. When leprosy is suspected, the person shall be brought to the priest, who will examine the symptoms, such as white rising, raw flesh, or if the hair has turned white. If these signs are present, it indicates leprosy, and the person is pronounced unclean.

If leprosy covers all the skin and turns white, the person is considered clean. Raw flesh appearing is a sign of uncleanness. If raw flesh turns white, the priest shall examine and possibly pronounce the person clean. Boils that heal but leave a white rising or reddish spot are to be shown to the priest, who will determine if it's leprosy. A burning spot that turns white or reddish may also indicate leprosy, requiring priest examination.

For plagues on the head or beard with yellow thin hair, the priest shall pronounce the person unclean. If the scall appears not deeper than the skin and lacks black hair, the person is shut up for seven days. If the scall does not spread or have yellow hair after seven days, the person is pronounced clean but must wash their clothes.Aaron was instructed to take a young calf for a sin offering and a ram for a burnt offering, both without blemish, to offer before the LORD. The LORD then instructed Aaron and his sons not to drink wine or strong drink when entering the tabernacle to avoid death, establishing this as a perpetual statute. This was to help them distinguish between the holy and the unholy, and the clean and the unclean, and to teach the Israelites all the LORD's statutes as conveyed by Moses.If the scall spreads in the skin after cleansing, the priest shall examine it. If the scall has spread, the priest shall not seek for yellow hair; the person is unclean. If the scall is stable and black hair has grown, it is healed, and the person is clean. Bright white spots on the skin are considered clean if they are darkish white. Baldness does not affect cleanliness unless there is a white reddish sore, which indicates leprosy. The leper must wear torn clothes, keep his head bare, cover his upper lip, and cry "Unclean, unclean." He shall live alone outside the camp. Garments with a leprosy plague, whether woolen or linen, in the warp or woof, or anything made of skin, must be shown to the priest. If the plague is greenish or reddish, it is unclean and must be burnt. If the plague has not spread after washing, it is still unclean and must be burnt. However, if the plague is gone after washing, the item is clean. This is the law for leprosy in garments or anything made of skin. The law for a leper's cleansing involves the priest, two clean birds, cedar wood, scarlet, and hyssop. One bird is killed over running water, and the living bird, along with cedar wood, scarlet, and hyssop, is dipped in the blood and used to sprinkle the person to be cleansed. The person must wash their clothes, shave all hair, and bathe to be clean.Aaron and his remaining sons, Eleazar and Ithamar, were instructed to take the remaining meat offering from the LORD's fire offerings and eat it without leaven beside the altar, as it was most holy. They were to eat it in the holy place, as it was their due from the sacrifices made by fire, as commanded by the LORD. The wave breast and heave shoulder were to be eaten in a clean place by Aaron, his sons, and daughters, as their due from the peace offerings of the Israelites. Moses was upset when he found that the goat of the sin offering was burnt and not eaten in the holy place by Eleazar and Ithamar, as it was meant to bear the iniquity of the congregation and make atonement before the LORD. Aaron explained that given the day's events, eating the sin offering might not have been accepted by the LORD. Moses was satisfied with Aaron's explanation.

The LORD then spoke to Moses and Aaron, outlining the animals that the Israelites could eat: those that have a split hoof and chew the cud. Animals that only chew the cud or only have a split hoof, like the camel, coney, hare, and swine, were deemed unclean. The Israelites were forbidden from eating their flesh or touching their carcasses. Fish with fins and scales were permitted, but all others were considered an abomination. Certain birds were also listed as abominations and not to be eaten. However, flying insects with legs above their feet for leaping were allowed, such as various types of locusts and grasshoppers. Touching the carcasses of unclean animals would make a person unclean until the evening, and they would need to wash their clothes.On the seventh day, the individual must shave all hair from the head, beard, and eyebrows, wash their clothes, and bathe in water to be clean. On the eighth day, they are to bring two male lambs without blemish, one ewe lamb of the first year without blemish, three-tenths of fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering, and one log of oil. The priest conducting the cleansing will present the individual and these offerings before the LORD at the tabernacle entrance. The priest will offer one male lamb as a guilt offering along with the log of oil, waving them as a wave offering before the LORD. The lamb is to be slaughtered in the sacred place where sin and burnt offerings are killed, as the guilt offering is very holy, just like the sin offering. The priest will apply some of the guilt offering's blood to the right ear, thumb, and big toe of the individual being cleansed, followed by pouring some oil into his left hand, dipping his right finger in the oil, and sprinkling it seven times before the LORD. The remaining oil in his hand will be put on the same parts of the individual's body as the blood, and the rest on the individual's head, making atonement for them before the LORD. After offering the sin offering to make atonement and cleansing from uncleanness, the priest will then offer the burnt offering and grain offering, completing the atonement, and the individual will be clean. If the individual is poor and cannot afford these, they may bring one lamb for a guilt offering, a tenth of an ephah of fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering, a log of oil, and two turtledoves or two young pigeons, one for a sin offering and the other for a burnt offering. The priest will make atonement with these offerings before the LORD. This is the law for anyone with a leprous disease who cannot afford the usual offerings for their cleansing.

When entering the land of Canaan, if a house is suspected of having leprosy, the owner must report it to the priest, who will inspect the house after it has been emptied to prevent the contents from becoming unclean.When inspecting a house for leprosy, if the priest finds greenish or reddish streaks on the walls, the house will be sealed for seven days. If the plague has spread upon re-inspection, the affected stones must be removed and discarded outside the city in an unclean place. The house is then to be scraped and plastered with new mortar. If the leprosy reappears, the house is deemed unclean and must be demolished, with its materials disposed of outside the city. Anyone entering the house while it is sealed is considered unclean until evening. If, after the house is plastered, the priest finds no spread of the plague, he will declare the house clean. To cleanse the house, two birds, cedar wood, scarlet yarn, and hyssop are used. One bird is killed over running water, and the living bird, along with the other items, is dipped in the blood and water, then used to sprinkle the house seven times. The living bird is then released into the open fields, signifying the house's cleansing. This law applies to all forms of leprosy and contamination. 

The LORD instructs Moses and Aaron on the laws concerning bodily discharges. Any discharge renders a person unclean, affecting everything they lie or sit on. Anyone touching these items must wash their clothes and bathe, remaining unclean until evening. The same applies to anyone touching the person with the discharge. If the person with the discharge spits on someone clean, that person must also wash and be considered unclean until evening. Any saddle or item used by the unclean person is also unclean. Vessels touched by the unclean person must be broken or rinsed in water. After the discharge stops, the person must wait seven days for cleansing, then offer two birds to the priest at the tabernacle for a sin and burnt offering to complete the cleansing process.Creeping things that move upon the earth, such as the weasel, mouse, tortoise, ferret, chameleon, lizard, snail, and mole, are unclean. Touching their dead bodies renders a person unclean until evening. Any object that a dead creature falls on becomes unclean and must be washed with water to be cleansed. Earthen vessels contaminated by them must be broken. Food or drink in contact with such water is unclean. Ovens and cooking ranges touched by their carcasses are to be destroyed. However, a spring or pit with plenty of water remains clean, but anything touching the carcass is unclean. Seeds sown are clean unless they get wet and touch a carcass, becoming unclean. Touching or eating the carcass of a clean animal that dies makes a person unclean until evening. Creeping things that crawl are not to be eaten and are considered abominable. The Israelites are instructed to be holy and not defile themselves with these creatures, as the LORD is holy and has brought them out of Egypt to be their God. This law distinguishes between clean and unclean animals and between those that may or may not be eaten.

If a woman gives birth to a son, she is unclean for seven days, and on the eighth day, the boy is to be circumcised. She remains in purification for 33 days for a son and 66 days for a daughter, without touching anything sacred or entering the sanctuary. After this period, she offers a lamb and a bird for her purification. If unable to afford a lamb, she may bring two birds. This law applies to both male and female births.

The LORD instructs Moses and Aaron on identifying leprosy. A person with a suspicious skin condition is to be examined by a priest. If the hair in the affected area turns white and the disease appears deeper than the skin, it is considered leprosy, and the person is unclean. If the spot is white but not deep, and the hair has not turned white, the person is observed for further signs of leprosy.If the affected area does not turn white, the priest will isolate the individual for seven days. On the seventh day, if the condition has not worsened, the individual will be isolated for another seven days. If the condition darkens but does not spread, the priest will declare the individual clean after they wash their clothes. However, if the condition spreads after initial examination, the priest must examine them again. If the condition has indeed spread, the individual is declared unclean due to leprosy. If the leprosy covers the entire body and turns white, the individual is considered clean. Raw flesh within the leprosy is deemed unclean. If the raw flesh turns white, the individual is clean. A healed boil that becomes a white or reddish spot and is shown to the priest, if deemed deeper than the skin with white hair, is considered leprosy. If there's no white hair and it's not deeper than the skin, the priest will isolate the individual for observation. A bright spot from a burn that turns white or reddish is leprosy if deeper than the skin. If a man or woman has a yellow thin hair in a plague on the head or beard, it is considered a dry scall, a form of leprosy. The priest will isolate someone with a scall for seven days for observation. If the scall does not spread and has no yellow hair, the individual is shaved except for the scall and isolated for another seven days. If the scall has not spread after this period, the individual is declared clean after washing their clothes.When inspecting a house for leprosy, if the priest finds greenish or reddish streaks on the walls, the house will be sealed for seven days. The LORD instructs Moses and Aaron on the laws concerning bodily discharges. Any discharge renders a person unclean, affecting everything they lie or sit on.
