To make an atonement for him before the LORD for his issue. If any man's seed of copulation goes out from him, then he shall wash all his flesh in water, and be unclean until the evening. Every garment, and every skin, whereon is the seed of copulation, shall be washed with water, and be unclean until the evening. The woman also with whom man shall lie with seed of copulation, they shall both bathe themselves in water, and be unclean until the evening. If a woman has an issue, and her issue in her flesh be blood, she shall be put apart seven days: and whosoever touches her shall be unclean until the evening. Everything that she lies upon in her separation shall be unclean: everything also that she sits upon shall be unclean. Whosoever touches her bed shall wash his clothes, and bathe himself in water, and be unclean until the evening. If any man lies with her at all, and her flowers be upon him, he shall be unclean seven days; and all the bed whereon he lies shall be unclean. If a woman has an issue of her blood many days out of the time of her separation, or if it runs beyond the time of her separation; all the days of the issue of her uncleanness shall be as the days of her separation: she shall be unclean. Every bed whereon she lies all the days of her issue shall be unto her as the bed of her separation: and whatsoever she sits upon shall be unclean, as the uncleanness of her separation. Whosoever touches those things shall be unclean, and shall wash his clothes, and bathe himself in water, and be unclean until the evening. But if she be cleansed of her issue, then she shall number to herself seven days, and after that she shall be clean. On the eighth day she shall take unto her two turtles, or two young pigeons, and bring them unto the priest, to the door of the tabernacle of the congregation. The priest shall offer the one for a sin offering, and the other for a burnt offering; and the priest shall make an atonement for her before the LORD for the issue of her uncleanness. Thus shall ye separate the children of Israel from their uncleanness; that they die not in their uncleanness, when they defile my tabernacle that is among them. This is the law of him that has an issue, and of him whose seed goes from him, and is defiled therewith; and of her that is sick of her flowers, and of him that has an issue, of the man, and of the woman, and of him that lies with her that is unclean.If the scall spreads in the skin after cleansing, the priest shall examine it. If the scall has spread, the priest shall not seek yellow hair; the person is unclean. However, if the scall is stable and black hair has grown, the scall is healed, and the person is clean. If a man or woman has bright white spots on their skin, the priest shall examine them. If the spots are darkish white, it is a freckled spot, and the person is clean. A bald man is clean, as is a man bald from the forehead back. If a white reddish sore appears on the bald area, it is leprosy. The priest shall examine it, and if the sore is white reddish, the person is unclean. A leper must wear torn clothes, leave their head bare, cover their upper lip, and cry out, "Unclean, unclean." They must live alone outside the camp. If a garment has a greenish or reddish plague, it is shown to the priest and isolated for seven days. If the plague spreads, the garment is unclean and must be burnt. If the plague does not spread after washing, it is still unclean and must be burnt. If the plague fades after washing, the garment is clean. This is the law for a leprous garment. The law for cleansing a leper involves bringing them to the priest, who will inspect them outside the camp. If healed, the priest commands a cleansing ritual involving two clean birds, cedar wood, scarlet, and hyssop. One bird is killed over running water, and the living bird, along with other items, is dipped in the blood and then used to sprinkle the cleansed person seven times. The cleansed person must wash their clothes, shave all hair, and bathe in water to be clean.On the seventh day, the person must shave all hair off their head, beard, and eyebrows, wash their clothes, and bathe to be clean. On the eighth day, they are to bring two unblemished male lambs, one unblemished ewe lamb, fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering, and oil to the priest at the tabernacle entrance. The priest offers one lamb as a guilt offering along with the oil as a wave offering before the LORD. The lamb is sacrificed in the holy place, and its blood is applied to the right ear, thumb, and big toe of the person being cleansed. The priest then pours some oil into his left hand, dips his right finger in it, and sprinkles oil seven times before the LORD. The remaining oil in the priest's hand is put on the same spots as the blood. The rest of the oil is poured on the person's head, making atonement for them before the LORD. The sin offering is then presented, and after that, the burnt offering and grain offering are made, completing the cleansing process. If the person is poor, they can bring one lamb and two birds, adjusting the offerings according to what they can afford. This is the law for anyone with leprosy who cannot afford the usual offerings.

When entering the land of Canaan, if a house is suspected of having leprosy, the owner must report it to the priest. The house is emptied before the priest inspects it to prevent the contents from becoming unclean. If leprosy is confirmed, specific cleansing rituals are prescribed.Sprinkle blood upon the mercy seat eastward seven times. Kill the goat of the sin offering for the people, bring its blood within the veil, and sprinkle it as with the bullock's blood on the mercy seat. Make atonement for the holy place due to the children of Israel's uncleanness and sins. No one shall be in the tabernacle during atonement until it is complete for the priest, his household, and all Israel. Atonement shall also be made for the altar, using the blood of the bullock and goat, cleansing and hallowing it from Israel's uncleanness. After reconciling the holy place, tabernacle, and altar, bring the live goat. Aaron shall confess all sins of Israel over it, then send it into the wilderness by a fit man to bear their iniquities. Aaron shall then remove his linen garments, wash, and offer burnt offerings for himself and the people. The fat of the sin offering is burned on the altar. The one releasing the scapegoat and the one burning the sin offerings shall wash and return to camp. On the tenth day of the seventh month, afflict your souls, do no work, and the priest shall make atonement to cleanse from all sins. This shall be a perpetual statute, with the priest in holy garments making atonement for the sanctuary, tabernacle, altar, priests, and all the congregation annually as commanded by the LORD. Instructions follow for offerings: any Israelite killing an ox, lamb, or goat must bring it to the tabernacle's door for an offering to the LORD, or be considered as shedding blood and cut off from the people. This ensures sacrifices are brought to the LORD at the tabernacle, offered by the priest as peace offerings, with the priest sprinkling the blood on the LORD's altar at the tabernacle's door.When inspecting a house for leprosy, if the priest finds greenish or reddish streaks that appear lower than the wall surface, the house is sealed for seven days. Upon re-inspection, if the plague has spread, the infected stones are removed and discarded outside the city in an unclean place. The house is then scraped and plastered with new mortar. If the leprosy reappears, showing the house is deeply infected, it must be demolished, and its materials disposed of outside the city. Anyone entering the house while it is sealed is considered unclean until evening. Those who sleep or eat in the house must wash their clothes. If, after the house is plastered, the priest finds no spread of leprosy, he declares the house clean. To cleanse the house, two birds, cedar wood, scarlet yarn, and hyssop are used in a ritual involving the killing of one bird over running water, dipping the live bird and other items in the mixture, and sprinkling the house seven times. The live bird is then released into the open fields, symbolizing the house's purification. This concludes the laws for leprosy concerning people, garments, and houses, detailing when they are considered clean or unclean. The text then transitions to regulations about bodily discharges, declaring any man with a discharge unclean. His bed, anything he sits on, and anyone who touches these or him must wash their clothes and bathe, remaining unclean until evening. If the unclean person touches someone without first rinsing their hands, that person must also wash and be considered unclean until evening. Earthen vessels touched by the unclean person must be broken, while wooden items should be rinsed. After the discharge stops, the person counts seven days for cleansing, washes their clothes, bathes in running water, and is then clean. On the eighth day, he brings two birds to the priest at the tabernacle for a sin offering and a burnt offering, completing his purification.To atone for his issue, a man must bring offerings to the LORD. If a man's semen is discharged, he and any garments or skins touched by it must be washed and are unclean until evening. Similarly, if a man lies with a woman, both must bathe and are unclean until evening. A woman with a menstrual issue is unclean for seven days, and anything or anyone she touches becomes unclean. After her period, if her bleeding continues beyond the normal time, she remains unclean. Once cleansed, she counts seven days, then brings two birds to the priest for offerings to complete her purification. These laws separate the Israelites from uncleanness to prevent defilement of the LORD's tabernacle. The text then describes the procedures for Aaron and his descendants to follow when entering the holy place to avoid death, including offerings and the wearing of holy garments. Aaron must make atonement for himself and his house with specific offerings. On the Day of Atonement, two goats are chosen: one for the LORD as a sin offering and the other as a scapegoat to carry away sins into the wilderness. Aaron must also bring a bull as a sin offering for himself, and perform rituals with incense and coals from the altar to protect himself from death before the LORD.The text describes the detailed rituals performed by Aaron, the high priest, for the atonement of the Israelites' sins. Aaron is to sprinkle blood upon the mercy seat and before it, symbolizing purification and reconciliation with God. The rituals include the sacrifice of a goat for the people's sins, the use of a live goat (the scapegoat) to carry away the sins into the wilderness, and various offerings and cleansing procedures for Aaron, his garments, and the altar. The text emphasizes the importance of these rituals in maintaining the sanctity of the holy place and ensuring the Israelites' cleanliness from sin. It concludes with instructions for the annual Day of Atonement, a time for the Israelites to afflict their souls, abstain from work, and be cleansed from their sins, establishing a perpetual statute for atonement. Additionally, it outlines the proper way to offer sacrifices to the LORD, emphasizing that offerings must be brought to the entrance of the tabernacle, with penalties for non-compliance, to ensure that sacrifices are made in a manner that honors God.Congregation, and burn the fat for a sweet savour unto the LORD. They shall no more offer their sacrifices unto devils, after whom they have gone a whoring. This shall be a statute forever unto them throughout their generations. And thou shalt say unto them, Whatsoever man there be of the house of Israel, or of the strangers which sojourn among you, that offereth a burnt offering or sacrifice, and bringeth it not unto the door of the tabernacle of the congregation, to offer it unto the LORD; even that man shall be cut off from among his people. And whatsoever man there be of the house of Israel, or of the strangers that sojourn among you, that eateth any manner of blood; I will even set my face against that soul that eateth blood, and will cut him off from among his people. For the life of the flesh is in the blood: and I have given it to you upon the altar to make an atonement for your souls: for it is the blood that maketh an atonement for the soul. Therefore I said unto the children of Israel, No soul of you shall eat blood, neither shall any stranger that sojourneth among you eat blood. And whatsoever man there be of the children of Israel, or of the strangers that sojourn among you, which hunteth and catcheth any beast or fowl that may be eaten; he shall even pour out the blood thereof, and cover it with dust. For it is the life of all flesh; the blood of it is for the life thereof: therefore I said unto the children of Israel, Ye shall eat the blood of no manner of flesh: for the life of all flesh is the blood thereof: whosoever eateth it shall be cut off. And every soul that eateth that which died of itself, or that which was torn with beasts, whether it be one of your own country, or a stranger, he shall both wash his clothes, and bathe himself in water, and be unclean until the even: then shall he be clean. But if he wash them not, nor bathe his flesh; then he shall bear his iniquity. And the LORD spake unto Moses, saying, Speak unto the children of Israel, and say unto them, I am the LORD your God. After the doings of the land of Egypt, wherein ye dwelt, shall ye not do: and after the doings of the land of Canaan, whither I bring you, shall ye not do: neither shall ye walk in their ordinances. Ye shall do my judgments, and keep mine ordinances, to walk therein: I am the LORD your God. Ye shall therefore keep my statutes, and my judgments: which if a man do, he shall live in them: I am the LORD. None of you shall approach to any that is near of kin to him, to uncover their nakedness: I am the LORD. The nakedness of thy father, or the nakedness of thy mother, shalt thou not uncover: she is thy mother; thou shalt not uncover her nakedness. The nakedness of thy father's wife shalt thou not uncover: it is thy father's nakedness. The nakedness of thy sister, the daughter of thy father, or daughter of thy mother, whether she be born at home, or born abroad, even their nakedness thou shalt not uncover. The nakedness of thy son's daughter, or of thy daughter's daughter, even their nakedness thou shalt not uncover: for theirs is thine own nakedness. The nakedness of thy father's wife's daughter, begotten of thy father, she is thy sister, thou shalt not uncover her nakedness. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of thy father's sister: she is thy father's near kinswoman. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of thy mother's sister: for she is thy mother's near kinswoman. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of thy father's brother, thou shalt not approach to his wife: she is thine aunt. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of thy daughter in law: she is thy son's wife; thou shalt not uncover her nakedness. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of thy brother's wife: it is thy brother's nakedness. Thou shalt not uncover the nakedness of a woman and her daughter, neither shalt thou take her son's daughter, or her daughter's daughter, to uncover her nakedness; for they are her near kinswomen: it is wickedness. Neither shalt thou take a wife to her sister, to vex her, to uncover her nakedness, beside the other in her lifetime. Also thou shalt not approach unto a woman to uncover her nakedness, as long as she is put apart for her uncleanness. Moreover thou shalt not lie carnally with thy neighbour's wife, to defile thyself with her. And thou shalt not let any of thy seed pass through the fire to Molech, neither shalt thou profane the name of thy God: I am the LORD. Thou shalt not lie with mankind, as with womankind: it is abomination. Neither shalt thou lie with any beast to defile thyself therewith: neither shall any woman stand before a beast to lie down thereto: it is confusion. Ye shall therefore keep my statutes and my judgments, and shall not commit any of these abominations; neither any of your own nation, nor any stranger that sojourneth among you: (For all these abominations have the men of the land done, which were before you, and the land is defiled;) That the land spue not you out also, when ye defile it, as it spued out the nations that were before you. And the LORD spake unto Moses, saying, Speak unto all the congregation of the children of Israel, and say unto them, Ye shall be holy: for I the LORD your God am holy. Ye shall fear every man his mother, and his father, and keep my sabbaths: I am the LORD your God. Turn ye not unto idols, nor make to yourselves molten gods: I am the LORD your God. And if ye offer a sacrifice of peace offerings unto the LORD, ye shall offer it at your own will. It shall be eaten the same day ye offer it, and on the morrow: and if ought remain until the third day, it shall be burnt in the fire. And if it be eaten at all on the third day, it is abominable; it shall not be accepted. Therefore every one that eateth it shall bear his iniquity, because he hath profaned the hallowed thing of the LORD: and that soul shall be cut off from among his people. And when ye reap the harvest of your land, thou shalt not wholly reap the corners of thy field, neither shalt thou gather the gleanings of thy harvest. And thou shalt not glean thy vineyard, neither shalt thou gather every grape of thy vineyard; thou shalt leave them for the poor and stranger: I am the LORD your God. Ye shall not steal, neither deal falsely, neither lie one to another. And ye shall not swear by my name falsely, neither shalt thou profane the name of thy God: I am the LORD. Thou shalt not defraud thy neighbour, neither rob him: the wages of him that is hired shall not abide with thee all night until the morning. Thou shalt not curse the deaf, nor put a stumblingblock before the blind, but shalt fear thy God: I am the LORD. Ye shall do no unrighteousness in judgment: thou shalt not respect the person of the poor, nor honor the person of the mighty: but in righteousness shalt thou judge thy neighbour. Thou shalt not go up and down as a talebearer among thy people: neither shalt thou stand against the blood of thy neighbour; I am the LORD. Thou shalt not hate thy brother in thine heart: thou shalt in any wise rebuke thy neighbour, and not suffer sin upon him. Thou shalt not avenge, nor bear any grudge against the children of thy people, but thou shalt love thy neighbour as thyself: I am the LORD. Ye shall keep my statutes. Thou shalt not let thy cattle gender with a diverse kind: thou shalt not sow thy field with mingled seed: neither shall a garment mingled of linen and woollen come upon thee. And whosoever lieth carnally with a woman, that is a bondmaid, betrothed to an husband, and not at all redeemed, nor freedom given her; she shall be scourged; they shall not be put to death, because she was not free. And he shall bring his trespass offering unto the LORD, unto the door of the tabernacle of the congregation, even a ram for a trespass offering. And the priest shall make an atonement for him with the ram of the trespass offering before the LORD for his sin which he hath done: and the sin which he hath done shall be forgiven him. And when ye shall come into the land, and shall have planted all manner of trees for food, then ye shall count the fruit thereof as uncircumcised: three years shall it be as uncircumcised unto you: it shall not be eaten of. But in the fourth year all the fruit thereof shall be holy to praise the LORD withal. And in the fifth year shall ye eat of the fruit thereof, that it may yield unto you the increase thereof: I am the LORD your God. Ye shall not eat any thing with the blood: neither shall ye use enchantment, nor observe times. Ye shall not round the corners of your heads, neither shalt thou mar the corners of thy beard. Ye shall not make any cuttings in your flesh for the dead, nor print any marks upon you: I am the LORD. Do not prostitute thy daughter, to cause her to be a whore; lest the land fall to whoredom, and the land become full of wickedness. Ye shall keep my sabbaths, and reverence my sanctuary: I am the LORD. Regard not them that have familiar spirits, neither seek after wizards, to be defiled by them: I am the LORD your God."Honor the elderly and fear your God: I am the LORD. Anyone cursing their parents or committing adultery shall be put to death. Acts of incest, bestiality, and other sexual immorality are strictly forbidden and will be punished. Keep all my statutes and judgments so the land will not expel you. Do not follow the practices of the nations I drove out before you. I have separated you from other peoples to be mine. Distinguish between clean and unclean animals and do not defile yourselves with them. You shall be holy to me, for I the LORD am holy."Household members of a priest may eat of his offerings, but if a priest's daughter marries outside, she loses this privilege unless widowed or divorced without children, returning to her father's house. Unintentional consumption of holy things requires restitution plus a fifth. Offerings must be without blemish; those with defects are unacceptable. Specific animals with abnormalities are not to be offered. Offerings from non-Israelites are not accepted due to potential defects. Newborn livestock must be at least eight days old before being offered. A mother and her young must not be killed on the same day. Offerings must be consumed on the day they are offered, with none left until the next day. God's commandments must be followed, and His name kept holy. God, who delivered Israel from Egypt, declares these laws. The text outlines the feasts of the Lord, including the Sabbath, Passover, and the Feast of Unleavened Bread, emphasizing the importance of holy convocations and offerings. Instructions for the firstfruits offering at harvest time are given, specifying the procedure and offerings required, underscoring the perpetual observance of these statutes. The text continues with the Feast of Weeks, detailing the counting of seven sabbaths from the day after the Sabbath of Passover, leading to the offering of new grain to the Lord. It describes the Feast of Trumpets as a day of rest with a special offering, and the Day of Atonement as a solemn day for atonement and rest, with no work to be done. The Feast of Tabernacles is described as a seven-day celebration with offerings and the first and eighth days as days of rest. The text emphasizes the importance of these feasts as statutes forever, to be observed by all generations, and concludes with instructions for the lighting of the lamps in the tabernacle.A man or woman with a familiar spirit or wizardry shall be put to death by stoning. Priests, the sons of Aaron, are instructed not to defile themselves for the dead, except for close kin. They must not shave their heads or make cuts in their flesh, maintaining holiness for they offer the LORD's offerings. Priests cannot marry a woman of ill repute or divorced; they must marry a virgin from their own people. The high priest, anointed and consecrated, must not defile himself, even for his parents, and must marry a virgin. Any descendant of Aaron with a blemish cannot offer the LORD's bread. Those with blemishes are restricted from approaching the offerings but can eat the holy bread. They must not profane the sanctuaries. Instructions are given to maintain separation from the holy things to not profane the LORD's name. Those unclean cannot partake in the holy things until they are clean. The holy things are for the priests and their bought servants or those born in his house, not for outsiders or hired servants.If a priest's daughter marries a non-priest, she cannot eat holy offerings. However, if she is widowed or divorced without children and returns to her father's house, she may eat of them, but no outsider can. Unintentional consumption of holy things requires adding a fifth of its value and giving it to the priest. The holy offerings of the Israelites must not be profaned, ensuring they do not bear guilt by eating their holy offerings improperly, as they are sanctified by the LORD. Offerings must be without blemish to be acceptable to the LORD, including vows and freewill offerings of cattle, sheep, or goats. Animals with defects are not acceptable for offerings. Certain animals with physical abnormalities can be offered as freewill offerings but not for vows. Offerings must not come from animals that are bruised, crushed, broken, or cut, and nothing from a foreigner's hand with such defects is acceptable. Newborn animals must be seven days with their mother before being eligible for offerings. A mother and her young must not be killed on the same day. Thanksgiving sacrifices must be eaten on the same day, with nothing left until morning, as commanded by the LORD. The LORD's name is to be kept holy, reminding the Israelites of their deliverance from Egypt. Instructions for observing the LORD's feasts include the Sabbath, Passover, and the Feast of Unleavened Bread, with specific days for holy gatherings and prohibitions on work. The Feast of Firstfruits involves offering the first harvest to the LORD, with specific sacrifices and offerings detailed, emphasizing the importance of these observances as perpetual statutes.The lamps are to be arranged on the pure candlestick before the LORD continuously, symbolizing an eternal statute for generations. Fine flour is used to bake twelve cakes, with two-tenth deals in each cake, arranged in two rows of six on the pure table before the LORD. Pure frankincense is placed on each row as a memorial, an offering made by fire to the LORD. Every Sabbath, this arrangement is to be set before the LORD continually, as part of an everlasting covenant with the children of Israel. It is designated for Aaron and his sons to consume in the holy place, being most holy among the offerings made by fire, as a perpetual statute.

A conflict arises when the son of an Israelite woman and an Egyptian man blasphemes the name of the LORD, leading to his detention and subsequent punishment by stoning, as commanded by the LORD through Moses. This incident underscores the severity of blasphemy and the equal application of the law to both Israelites and strangers within the land.

The LORD then introduces the concept of a land Sabbath, instructing that the land is to rest every seventh year, a sabbath to the LORD, during which no sowing or pruning is to occur. This sabbath year is meant to provide rest for the land and sustenance for the people, their servants, and the sojourners among them, as well as for the livestock and wild animals. This is followed by the introduction of the Jubilee year, occurring every fiftieth year, proclaimed by the sound of the trumpet during the Day of Atonement. The Jubilee year is a time of liberty, where every person is to return to their possession and family, emphasizing the restoration of property and familial bonds. It is a year of not sowing or reaping the self-grown harvest or gathering the grapes from unpruned vines, highlighting the land's holiness and the people's reliance on the LORD's provision. The Jubilee year also addresses fair trade and property transactions, ensuring no oppression and adjusting prices according to the number of years since the last Jubilee, fostering a community of fairness and respect for the divine commandments.The laws provided ensure fair treatment and economic stability within the community. They dictate that the price of land should decrease as the Jubilee year approaches, to prevent oppression and ensure reverence for God. These statutes guarantee safety and abundance for the people, promising divine blessings for obedience, especially concerning the Sabbath year's agricultural practices. The land, ultimately belonging to God, cannot be sold permanently, emphasizing the Israelites' temporary stewardship and the provision for land redemption to support those who fall into poverty. The Jubilee year further enforces this, allowing for the return of sold property and ensuring that families can reclaim their ancestral lands, maintaining social and economic balance.

Houses in walled cities have a one-year redemption period, after which they permanently belong to the buyer unless it's a Levitical city, where property reverts in the Jubilee. Levites have perpetual rights to their city houses and fields, underscoring their special status. The text also addresses the treatment of the poor and strangers, prohibiting usury and insisting on brotherly support. It outlines the conditions for servitude among Israelites, emphasizing their release in the Jubilee year, and contrasts this with the treatment of foreign slaves, who can be kept permanently. However, it mandates fair treatment for all, reflecting God's deliverance of Israel from Egypt and His desire for justice and mercy within the community.From the day after the Sabbath, count seven complete Sabbaths. On the day after the seventh Sabbath, number fifty days and present a new grain offering to the LORD. Bring from your homes two loaves made of two-tenths of an ephah of fine flour, baked with yeast, as firstfruits to the LORD. Along with the bread, offer seven lambs without defect, one young bull, and two rams as a burnt offering to the LORD, accompanied by grain and drink offeringsan offering made by fire, a pleasing aroma to the LORD. Then, sacrifice one goat for a sin offering and two lambs as a fellowship offering. The priest shall wave them with the bread of the firstfruits as a wave offering before the LORD; they are holy to the LORD for the priest. Proclaim this day as a holy gathering; do no regular work. It is a lasting ordinance for all your generations, wherever you live.

When harvesting, do not reap to the very edges of your field or gather the gleanings. Leave them for the poor and the foreigner. I am the LORD your God.

The LORD instructed Moses about the Feast of Trumpets on the first day of the seventh month, a day of rest, a memorial with trumpet blasts, a holy gathering. Do no regular work, but present an offering made by fire to the LORD. On the tenth day of this seventh month is the Day of Atonement, a holy gathering; you must deny yourselves and present an offering made by fire to the LORD. Do no work on that day, for it is the Day of Atonement, to make atonement for you before the LORD your God. Anyone who does not deny themselves or does any work will be cut off from their people.

From the evening of the ninth day of the month until the following evening, observe your Sabbath. The Feast of Tabernacles begins on the fifteenth day of the seventh month. For seven days, present offerings made by fire to the LORD. The first and eighth days are days of rest and holy gatherings. These are in addition to the LORD's Sabbaths and in addition to your gifts, vows, and freewill offerings.

On the fifteenth day of the seventh month, after you have gathered the crops of the land, celebrate the LORD's festival for seven days. The first and eighth days are days of rest. Take branches from luxurious trees and rejoice before the LORD your God for seven days. This is a lasting ordinance for the generations to come; celebrate it in the seventh month. Live in temporary shelters for seven days; all native-born Israelites are to live in such shelters so your descendants will know that I had the Israelites live in temporary shelters when I brought them out of Egypt. This is a lasting ordinance for the generations to come.This sale shall be according to the number of years, like the time of a hired servant. You shall not make idols or graven images, nor set up any stone image to bow down to it, for I am the LORD your God. Keep my Sabbaths and reverence my sanctuary. If you follow my statutes and commandments, I will give rain in due season, the land will yield its increase, and you will eat your bread to the full and dwell safely. Wild beasts will rob you of your children and destroy your cattle. If you still do not reform, I will punish you seven times more for your sins. I will bring a sword upon you to avenge my covenant, and when gathered, I will send pestilence among you. You will be delivered into the hand of the enemy. If you still do not listen but walk contrary to me, I will walk contrary to you in fury and chastise you seven times for your sins. You shall eat the flesh of your sons and daughters. Those left alive will feel faintness in their hearts; the sound of a shaken leaf will chase them, and they will flee as from a sword, falling when none pursues. You will have no power to stand before your enemies and shall perish among the heathen. Those remaining shall pine away in their iniquity and that of their fathers in your enemies' lands. If they confess their iniquity and accept their punishment, I will remember my covenant with Jacob, Isaac, and Abraham, and the land. The land shall enjoy her sabbaths while desolate, and they shall accept their punishment for despising my judgments. Yet, even in the land of their enemies, I will not cast them away or break my covenant, for I am the LORD their God. I will remember the covenant of their ancestors, whom I brought out of Egypt, that I might be their God. These are the statutes, judgments, and laws the LORD made with the children of Israel in Mount Sinai by Moses. 

Speak to the children of Israel about making a singular vow, valuing persons for the LORD by your estimation. The valuation shall differ based on age and gender, with specific shekels of silver assigned to each category. If poorer than the estimation, the priest shall value him according to his ability. Offerings of beasts to the LORD shall be holy, not to be altered or exchanged. If any unclean beast is presented, the priest shall value it. Sanctifying a house or part of a field to the LORD involves specific estimations and the possibility of redemption by adding a fifth part to the valuation.If a person sanctifies their field after the jubilee, the priest will calculate its value based on the remaining years until the next jubilee, reducing the initial estimation. If the person wishes to redeem the field, they must add a fifth of the estimated value. If the field is not redeemed or is sold to someone else, it cannot be redeemed again. At the jubilee, fields that are not redeemed become holy to the LORD and belong to the priests. If a field bought by a person is sanctified to the LORD, its value is calculated until the jubilee, and it becomes holy to the LORD. In the jubilee year, the field returns to its original owner. All valuations are based on the sanctuary shekel. Firstborn animals, which belong to the LORD, cannot be sanctified by anyone. If an unclean animal is sanctified, its value is determined, and a fifth is added if redeemed; otherwise, it is sold at its estimated value. Devoted things, including people, animals, or fields, cannot be sold or redeemed; they are most holy to the LORD. A person devoted to the LORD cannot be redeemed and must be put to death. All tithes of the land and produce are holy to the LORD. If someone wishes to redeem any of their tithes, they must add a fifth to it. The tithe of herds and flocks is determined by every tenth animal, which is holy to the LORD and cannot be exchanged or redeemed. These commandments were given by the LORD to Moses for the Israelites at Mount Sinai.

The LORD spoke unto Moses in mount Sinai, saying, "Speak unto the children of Israel, and say unto them, When ye come into the land which I give you, then shall the land keep a sabbath unto the LORD. Six years thou shalt sow thy field, and six years thou shalt prune thy vineyard, and gather in the fruit thereof; But in the seventh year shall be a sabbath of rest unto the land, a sabbath for the LORD: thou shalt neither sow thy field, nor prune thy vineyard. That which groweth of its own accord of thy harvest thou shalt not reap, neither gather the grapes of thy vine undressed: for it is a year of rest unto the land. And the sabbath of the land shall be meat for you; for thee, and for thy servant, and for thy maid, and for thy hired servant, and for thy stranger that sojourneth with thee. Nadab and Abihu, who died offering unauthorized fire before the LORD, had no children, leaving Eleazar and Ithamar to serve as priests under their father Aaron. The LORD instructed Moses to bring the Levites to Aaron so they could assist him and maintain the tabernacle's services, emphasizing the Levites' unique role among the Israelites. The Levites were chosen over the firstborn of Israel as a dedicated group to the LORD, following the divine claim on all firstborns since the plague in Egypt. Moses was to count the Levites by family and age, starting from a month old.

The Levites were divided into three main families: Gershon, Kohath, and Merari. The Gershonites were responsible for the tabernacle's fabrics and coverings, the Kohathites for the sacred objects including the ark and altars, and the Merari family for the tabernacle's structural components. Each family had specific duties and camping positions around the tabernacle, with Eleazar, Aaron's son, overseeing the Levites' work. The detailed organization underscores the importance of each group's role in the worship and community life of the Israelites.Moses, Aaron, and his sons camped before the tabernacle to the east, guarding the sanctuary on behalf of the Israelites. Any unauthorized person approaching was to be put to death. The Levites, numbered by Moses and Aaron as commanded by the LORD, totaled 22,000 males a month old and upward. The LORD instructed Moses to count all firstborn Israelite males from a month old and upward, with the Levites and their cattle to be taken in place of the firstborn of Israel and their cattle, signifying the Levites belonged to the LORD. The firstborn males numbered 22,273, exceeding the Levites by 273. To redeem these extra firstborn, five shekels per person were to be collected, according to the sanctuary's shekel, and given to Aaron and his sons. Moses collected 1,365 shekels for the redemption and handed it to Aaron and his sons as commanded by the LORD.

The LORD then instructed Moses and Aaron to count the Kohathites among the Levites, from thirty to fifty years old, responsible for the work in the tabernacle. Their duties included handling the most holy items: covering the ark of testimony with a veil, the table of shewbread, the candlestick, the golden altar, and other sacred vessels with cloths of blue, scarlet, and badgers' skins before transport. The Kohathites were warned not to touch the holy items directly to avoid death. Eleazar, Aaron's son, was responsible for the oil for the light, sweet incense, daily meat offering, anointing oil, and overseeing the tabernacle and its contents.The LORD instructed Moses and Aaron not to exclude the Kohathite families from the Levites, emphasizing the importance of their role in handling the most holy things. Aaron and his sons were to assign specific duties and burdens to them, ensuring they did not witness the covering of holy items to avoid death. The Gershonites, aged thirty to fifty, were also counted for their service in the tabernacle, responsible for carrying the tabernacle's curtains, coverings, and the entrance hangings, under the supervision of Aaron and his sons, specifically under Ithamar's oversight.

The Merarites were similarly numbered for their service, tasked with transporting the tabernacle's structural components like boards, bars, pillars, and their accessories. Moses, Aaron, and the congregation leaders counted the Kohathites, Gershonites, and Merarites, assigning them to their respective duties in the tabernacle service as commanded by the LORD. The Kohathites numbered 2,750, the Gershonites 2,630, and the Merarites 3,200, all dedicated to the service of the tabernacle from the age of thirty to fifty, as per the LORD's command through Moses.According to the LORD's command, they were numbered by Moses, each according to his service and burden. The LORD then instructed Moses to command the Israelites to expel from the camp anyone with leprosy, a discharge, or who is defiled by the dead, to prevent defilement of the camp where the LORD dwells. The Israelites complied with this command. Further instructions were given for individuals who commit sins to confess and make restitution, adding a fifth more to the principal amount, and if there's no relative, the restitution should go to the LORD, through the priest, along with a ram for atonement. All holy offerings brought to the priest by the Israelites would belong to him.

The LORD also addressed cases of marital unfaithfulness, prescribing a ritual for a husband who suspects his wife of infidelity. This involved the wife bringing an offering of barley meal to the priest, who would then make her drink "bitter water" that could cause a curse if she was guilty. If the woman was not guilty, she would be free from the curse and able to conceive children. This law aimed to address jealousy and maintain purity among the Israelites, with the priest executing the law upon the woman as prescribed.his sale shall be according unto the number of years, according to the time of an hired servant shall it be with him. If there be yet many years behind, according unto them he shall give again the price of his redemption out of the money that he was bought for. And if there remain but few years unto the year of jubile, then he shall count with him, and according unto his years shall he give him again the price of his redemption. And as a yearly hired servant shall he be with him: and the other shall not rule with rigour over him in thy sight. And if he be not redeemed in these years, then he shall go out in the year of jubile, both he, and his children with him. For unto me the children of Israel are servants; they are my servants whom I brought forth out of the land of Egypt: I am the LORD your God. Ye shall make you no idols nor graven image, neither rear you up a standing image, neither shall ye set up any image of stone in your land, to bow down unto it: for I am the LORD your God. Ye shall keep my sabbaths, and reverence my sanctuary: I am the LORD. If ye walk in my statutes, and keep my commandments, and do them; Then I will give you rain in due season, and the land shall yield her increase, and the trees of the field shall yield their fruit. And your threshing shall reach unto the vintage, and the vintage shall reach unto the sowing time: and ye shall eat your bread to the full, and dwell in your land safely. And I will give peace in the land, and ye shall lie down, and none shall make you afraid: and I will rid evil beasts out of the land, neither shall the sword go through your land. And ye shall chase your enemies, and they shall fall before you by the sword. And five of you shall chase an hundred, and an hundred of you shall put ten thousand to flight: and your enemies shall fall before you by the sword. For I will have respect unto you, and make you fruitful, and multiply you, and establish my covenant with you. And ye shall eat old store, and bring forth the old because of the new. And I set my tabernacle among you: and my soul shall not abhor you. And I will walk among you, and will be your God, and ye shall be my people. I am the LORD your God, which brought you forth out of the land of Egypt, that ye should not be their bondmen; and I have broken the bands of your yoke, and made you go upright. But if ye will not hearken unto me, and will not do all these commandments; And if ye shall despise my statutes, or if your soul abhor my judgments, so that ye will not do all my commandments, but that ye break my covenant: I also will do this unto you; I will even appoint over you terror, consumption, and the burning ague, that shall consume the eyes, and cause sorrow of heart: and ye shall sow your seed in vain, for your enemies shall eat it. And I will set my face against you, and ye shall be slain before your enemies: they that hate you shall reign over you; and ye shall flee when none pursueth you. And if ye will not yet for all this hearken unto me, then I will punish you seven times more for your sins. And I will break the pride of your power; and I will make your heaven as iron, and your earth as brass: And your strength shall be spent in vain: for your land shall not yield her increase, neither shall the trees of the land yield their fruits. And if ye walk contrary unto me, and will not hearken unto me; I will bring seven times more plagues upon you according to your sins. I will also send wild beasts among you, which shall rob you of your children, and destroy your cattle, and make you few in number; and your high ways shall be desolate. And if ye will not be reformed by me by these things, but will walk contrary unto me; Then will I also walk contrary unto you, and will punish you yet seven times for your sins. And I will bring a sword upon you, that shall avenge the quarrel of my covenant: and when ye are gathered together within your cities, I will send the pestilence among you; and ye shall be delivered into the hand of the enemy. And when I have broken the staff of your bread, ten women shall bake your bread in one oven, and they shall deliver you your bread again by weight: and ye shall eat, and not be satisfied. And if ye will not for all this hearken unto me, but walk contrary unto me; Then I will walk contrary unto you also in fury; and I, even I, will chastise you seven times for your sins. And ye shall eat the flesh of your sons, and the flesh of your daughters shall ye eat. And I will destroy your high places, and cut down your images, and cast your carcases upon the carcases of your idols, and my soul shall abhor you. And I will make your cities waste, and bring your sanctuaries unto desolation, and I will not smell the savour of your sweet odours. And I will bring the lAccording to the LORD's command, Moses was to instruct the Israelites on the vow of a Nazarite, dedicated to the LORD. This vow included abstaining from wine, strong drink, and anything made from grapes, not cutting their hair, avoiding contact with the dead, and maintaining holiness. If defiled, the Nazarite had to shave their head, offer sacrifices, and restart their vow. The completion of the vow required offerings of lambs, a ram, unleavened bread, and drink offerings. The priest would then make offerings to the LORD, and the Nazarite could drink wine again. This law detailed the offerings and procedures for a Nazarite's vow and separation to the LORD.

The LORD also instructed Moses on how to bless the Israelites, promising protection, grace, and peace. This blessing was to place the LORD's name upon the Israelites and ensure His blessing.

When Moses had set up and sanctified the tabernacle and all its instruments, the princes of Israel, representing their tribes, brought offerings of wagons and oxen to support the tabernacle's service. These were given to the Levites according to their duties, as commanded by the LORD through Moses.Two wagons and four oxen were given to the sons of Gershon for their service, and four wagons and eight oxen to the sons of Merari, under the supervision of Ithamar, Aaron's son. The sons of Kohath received none, as their duty involved carrying the sanctuary's items on their shoulders. The princes made offerings for the altar's dedication, each on their designated day, as instructed by the LORD through Moses.

Nahshon, from the tribe of Judah, was the first to offer. His offering included a silver charger weighing 130 shekels, a silver bowl of 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour and oil for a meat offering, a gold spoon of ten shekels full of incense, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for a burnt offering, a goat for a sin offering, and two oxen, five rams, five goats, and five lambs for peace offerings.

On the second day, Nethaneel of Issachar offered similar items, as did Eliab of Zebulun on the third day, Elizur of Reuben on the fourth day, Shelumiel of Simeon on the fifth day, Eliasaph of Gad on the sixth day, and Elishama of Ephraim on the seventh day. Each prince's offering consisted of a silver charger and bowl, a gold spoon full of incense, fine flour mixed with oil, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for a burnt offering, a goat for a sin offering, and animals for peace offerings.On the eighth day, Gamaliel, prince of Manasseh, offered his dedication gifts: a silver charger and a silver bowl, both filled with fine flour and oil for a meat offering, a golden spoon full of incense, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for a burnt offering, a goat for a sin offering, and for peace offerings, two oxen, five rams, five goats, and five lambs. Following him, on the ninth day, Abidan of Benjamin presented similar offerings. On the tenth day, Ahiezer of Dan made his offerings, and on the eleventh day, Pagiel of Asher did the same. The twelfth day saw Ahira of Naphtali offering identical gifts.

The dedication of the altar included twelve silver chargers and bowls, twelve golden spoons of incense, weighing a total of 120 shekels. The silver vessels collectively weighed 2,400 shekels. For burnt offerings, there were twelve bullocks, rams, and lambs, along with their meat offerings, and twelve goats for sin offerings. The peace offerings consisted of twenty-four bullocks, sixty rams, sixty goats, and sixty lambs. This marked the altar's dedication after its anointing.

When Moses entered the tabernacle to speak with God, he heard a voice speaking to him from above the mercy seat on the ark of testimony.The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell Aaron about the lighting of the lamps so that the seven lamps would illuminate the area in front of the candlestick. Aaron complied, lighting the lamps as commanded. The candlestick itself was made of beaten gold, crafted according to the pattern shown to Moses by the LORD.

The LORD then instructed Moses to take the Levites from among the Israelites and purify them. This purification process involved sprinkling them with water of purification, shaving their bodies, washing their clothes, and making a sin offering and a burnt offering of young bullocks. The Levites were to be presented before the LORD, with the Israelites laying their hands on them, symbolizing their dedication to the LORD's service. Aaron and his sons were to offer the Levites to the LORD, signifying their separation from the other Israelites to be dedicated to the LORD's service.

The Levites were given to Aaron and his sons as a gift from among the Israelites to perform the service of the tabernacle. This was to atone for the Israelites and prevent any plague from befalling them when they approached the sanctuary. Moses, Aaron, and the Israelites followed all the LORD's commands regarding the Levites, who were purified and began their service in the tabernacle.

The LORD also specified that Levites were to begin their service at the age of twenty-five and retire at the age of fifty, after which they could assist their brethren but not perform the service.

The LORD then instructed Moses to have the Israelites keep the Passover at its appointed time in the second year after leaving Egypt. Despite some being unable to participate due to impurity from contact with a dead body, the Passover was observed as commanded by the LORD, demonstrating the Israelites' obedience and the importance of observing the LORD's statutes."and into desolation: and your enemies which dwell therein shall be astonished at it. And the LORD spake unto Moses, saying, Speak unto the children of Israel, and say unto them, When a man shall make a singular vow, the persons shall be for the LORD by thy estimation. And if it be from five years old even unto twenty years old, then thy estimation shall be of the male twenty shekels, and for the female ten shekels. And if it be from sixty years old and above; if it be a male, then thy estimation shall be fifteen shekels, and for the female ten shekels. But if he be poorer than thy estimation, then he shall present himself before the priest, and the priest shall value him; according to his ability that vowed shall the priest value him. And if it be a beast, whereof men bring an offering unto the LORD, all that any man giveth of such unto the LORD shall be holy. He shall not alter it, nor change it, a good for a bad, or a bad for a good: and if he shall at all change beast for beast, then it and the exchange thereof shall be holy. And if it be any unclean beast, of which they do not offer a sacrifice unto the LORD, then he shall present the beast before the priest: And the priest shall value it, whether it be good or bad: as thou valuest it, who art the priest, so shall it be. But if he will at all redeem it, then he shall add a fifth part thereof unto thy estimation. And when a man shall sanctify his house to be holy unto the LORD, then the priest shall estimate it, whether it be good or bad: as the priest shall estimate it, so shall it stand. And if he that sanctified it will redeem his house, then he shall add the fifth part of the money of thy estimation unto it, and it shall be his. And if a man shall sanctify unto the LORD some part of a field of his possession, then thy estimation shall be according to the seed thereof: an homer of barley seed shall be valued at fifty shekels of silver. If he sanctify his field from the year of jubile, according to thy estimation it s"Moses instructed the Israelites on how to observe the Passover if they were unclean or on a journey, emphasizing the importance of keeping it on the fourteenth day of the second month with unleavened bread and bitter herbs, without leaving any until morning or breaking any bones. Those who were clean but did not observe Passover would be cut off from their people for not bringing the LORD's offering in its appointed season. A single ordinance was established for both the native-born and the sojourner who wished to keep the Passover.

When the tabernacle was set up, a cloud covered it by day and appeared as fire by night, guiding the Israelites on when to journey and when to camp. This divine presence indicated when they should move or stay, resting in their tents as long as the cloud remained. The LORD's commands were followed precisely, with the Israelites moving or camping at the LORD's command through Moses.

The LORD then instructed Moses to make two silver trumpets for calling the assembly and directing the movement of the camps. Different signals were designated for assembling the leaders or the community, for setting out on a journey, and for going to war, ensuring that the Israelites would be remembered and saved by the LORD. The trumpets were also to be used during celebrations, solemn days, and at the beginning of months over burnt offerings and peace offerings as a memorial before God.

On the twentieth day of the second month, in the second year, the cloud lifted from the tabernacle, signaling the Israelites to journey from the wilderness of Sinai to the wilderness of Paran, led by the standard of the camp of Judah, following the LORD's command through Moses.As the Israelites journeyed, leaders from each tribe were appointed to oversee their respective hosts. The tabernacle was disassembled and transported by the sons of Gershon and Merari, while the tribes moved in a specified order, each under its standard. The Kohathites carried the sanctuary, ensuring the tabernacle was set up at each new location. Moses invited his father-in-law, Hobab, to join them, offering him a share in the blessings God promised to Israel. Despite initially declining, Hobab's decision remains open to interpretation.

The ark of the covenant led the way, seeking out resting places. Moses invoked God's protection as they moved and prayed for their return as they rested. However, discontent arose among the people, leading to complaints about their hardships and longing for the foods of Egypt, despite the provision of manna. God's anger flared against their ingratitude, resulting in divine punishment. Moses, overwhelmed by the burden of leadership and the people's complaints, pleaded with God for relief. In response, God instructed Moses to gather seventy elders to share the leadership burden, promising to alleviate Moses' load and address the people's demands for meat.As the Israelites journeyed, God instructed Moses to select seventy elders to help bear the leadership burden. God promised to bestow a portion of the spirit that was upon Moses onto these elders to assist in governing the people. In preparation for this, the people were told to sanctify themselves for the coming of a divine provision of meat, responding to their complaints of lacking the foods of Egypt. Despite Moses' skepticism about providing enough meat for the multitude, God assured him of His power to fulfill this promise.

God's spirit descended upon the seventy elders, enabling them to prophesy, signifying their empowerment. However, Eldad and Medad, who were not present at the tabernacle, also received the spirit and prophesied within the camp. This event led to a discussion between Moses and Joshua, emphasizing Moses' wish that all of God's people could be prophets.

Following this, God sent a wind that brought quails from the sea to provide meat for the Israelites, fulfilling His promise. Yet, as the people indulged, God's wrath was kindled due to their insatiable desire, resulting in a severe plague that struck the people.

The narrative then shifts to Miriam and Aaron's criticism of Moses for marrying an Ethiopian woman, questioning Moses' unique role as God's messenger. God defended Moses' leadership and humility, rebuking Miriam and Aaron. Miriam was struck with leprosy as punishment, leading Aaron to plead with Moses for her healing. Moses interceded with God on Miriam's behalf, showcasing his compassionate leadership despite the criticism he faced."shall stand. And if he will not redeem the field, or if he have sold the field to another man, it shall not be redeemed anymore. But the field, when it goes out in the jubilee, shall be holy unto the LORD, as a field devoted; the possession thereof shall be the priests. And if a man sanctify unto the LORD a field which he hath bought, which is not of the fields of his possession; Then the priest shall reckon unto him the worth of thy estimation, even unto the year of the jubilee: and he shall give thine estimation in that day, as a holy thing unto the LORD. Only the firstling of the beasts, which should be the LORD's firstling, no man shall sanctify it; whether it be ox, or sheep: it is the LORD's. And if it be of an unclean beast, then he shall redeem it according to thine estimation, and shall add a fifth part of it thereto: or if it be not redeemed, then it shall be sold according to thy estimation. Notwithstanding no devoted thing, that a man shall devote unto the LORD of all that he hath, both of man and beast, and of the field of his possession, shall be sold or redeemed: every devoted thing is most holy unto the LORD. None devoted, which shall be devoted of men, shall be redeemed; but shall surely be put to death. And all the tithe of the land, whether of the seed of the land, or of the fruit of the tree, is the LORD's: it is holy unto the LORD. And if a man will at all redeem ought of his tithes, he shall add thereto the fifth part thereof. And concerning the tithe of the herd, or of the flock, even of whatsoever passeth under the rod, the tenth shall be holy unto the LORD. He shall not search whether it be good or bad, neither shall he change it: and if he change it at all, then both it and the change thereof shall be holy; it shall not be redeemed. These are the commandments, which the LORD commanded Moses for the children of Israel in mount Sinai. The Fourth Book of Moses: Called Numbers And the LORD spake unto Moses in the wilderness of Sinai, in the tabernacle of the congregation, on the first day of the second month, in the second year after they were come out of the land of Egypt, saying, Take ye the sum of all the congregation of the children of Israel, after their families, by the house of their fathers, with the number of their names, every male by their polls; From twenty years old and upward, all that are able to go forth to war in Israel: thou and Aaron shall number them by their armies. And with you there shall be a man of every tribe; every one head of the house of his fathers. And these are the names of the men that shall stand with you: of the tribe of Reuben; Elizur the son of Shedeur. Of Simeon; Shelumiel the son of Zurishaddai. Of Judah; Nahshon the son of Amminadab. Of Issachar; Nethaneel the son of Zuar. Of Zebulun; Eliab the son of Helon. Of the children of Joseph: of Ephraim; Elishama the son of Ammihud: of Manasseh; Gamaliel the son of Pedahzur. Of Benjamin; Abidan the son of Gideoni. Of Dan; Ahiezer the son of Ammishaddai. Of Asher; Pagiel the son of Ocran. Of Gad; Eliasaph the son of Deuel. Of Naphtali; Ahira the son of Enan. These were the renowned of the congregation, princes of the tribes of their fathers, heads of thousands in Israel. And Moses and Aaron took these men which are expressed by their names: And they assembled all the congregation together on the first day of the second month, and they declared their pedigrees after their families, by the house of their fathers, according to the number of the names, from twenty years old and upward, by their polls. As the LORD commanded Moses, so he numbered them in the wilderness of Sinai. And the children of Reuben, Israel's eldest son, by their generations, after their families, by the house of their fathers, according to the number of the names, by their polls, every male from twenty years old and upward, all that were able to go forth to war; Those that were numbered of them, even of the tribe of Reuben, were forty and six thousand and five hundred. Of the children of Simeon, by their generations, after their families, by the house of their fathers, those that were numbered of them, according to the number o"Miriam was isolated from the camp for seven days as punishment, and the Israelites did not move until she was brought back. Afterward, they journeyed to the wilderness of Paran. God instructed Moses to send men to explore Canaan, the land promised to the Israelites. One leader from each of the twelve tribes was chosen for this task. These scouts were to assess the land's fertility, the strength of its inhabitants, and the type of settlements there. Moses encouraged them to be courageous and bring back samples of the local produce.

The scouts returned after forty days, bringing evidence of the land's richness. However, they reported that the inhabitants were strong and the cities well-fortified, causing fear among the Israelites. Caleb tried to encourage the people to have faith and conquer the land, but the other scouts spread a negative report, saying the land devoured its inhabitants and was populated by giants, making the Israelites feel like grasshoppers in comparison.

This report led to the entire community rebelling against Moses and Aaron, wishing they had died in Egypt or the wilderness rather than face conquest in Canaan. They even proposed choosing a new leader to take them back to Egypt.Moses and Aaron, in despair, fell before the Israelite assembly. Joshua and Caleb, who had scouted the land, tore their clothes in distress and implored the people, describing the land as exceedingly good and urging trust in the LORD to deliver it into their hands, emphasizing that the inhabitants' protection was gone and the LORD was with Israel. However, the congregation reacted with hostility, threatening to stone them. At this moment, the LORD's glory appeared to all.

The LORD questioned Moses about the people's faithlessness despite witnessing numerous miracles and contemplated destroying them to create a greater nation from Moses. Moses, however, argued that such an action would tarnish the LORD's reputation among the Egyptians and other nations, suggesting it would imply the LORD's inability to fulfill His promise to Israel. He appealed to the LORD's mercy and history of forgiveness, asking for pardon for the people's iniquities.

The LORD agreed to pardon the people as Moses requested but declared that those who had seen His miracles yet remained disobedient would not see the promised land. Only Caleb, who showed unwavering faith, and his descendants would enter it. The LORD then instructed a return to the wilderness, indicating that the current generation, except for Caleb and Joshua, would perish there, and their children, once feared to be prey, would inherit the land. This generation would wander for forty years in the wilderness, bearing the consequences of their disbelief, mirroring the forty days of land exploration.

The men who spread the negative report about the land were struck down by a plague from the LORD, while Joshua and Caleb survived. Moses relayed these declarations to the Israelites, marking a pivotal moment of judgment and mercy in their journey.After receiving Moses' warnings, the Israelites mourned greatly. Despite their earlier refusal, they attempted to enter the promised land, ignoring Moses' caution that the LORD would not be with them. Consequently, they were defeated by the Amalekites and Canaanites. Following this, the LORD instructed Moses on offerings to be made by the Israelites upon entering their new land, detailing the specific sacrifices and their preparations to ensure they would be a pleasing aroma to the LORD. These instructions included offerings for both the community and any foreigners living among them, emphasizing a unified law for both groups. Additionally, guidelines were provided for unintentional sins, outlining the offerings required for atonement, ensuring forgiveness for the community and individuals alike. This established a clear and inclusive system for worship and atonement, reinforcing the importance of obedience and the possibility of forgiveness."f the names, by their polls, every male from twenty years old and upward, all that were able to go forth to war; Those that were numbered of them, even of the tribe of Simeon, were fifty and nine thousand and three hundred.
