But the Levites shall pitch round about the ta"After receiving Moses' warnings, the Israelites mourned greatly. Despite their earlier refusal, they attempted to enter the promised land, ignoring Moses' caution that the LORD would not be with them. Consequently, they were defeated by the Amalekites and Canaanites. Following this, the LORD instructed Moses on offerings to be made by the Israelites upon entering their new land, detailing the specific sacrifices and their preparations to ensure they would be a pleasing aroma to the LORD. These instructions included offerings for both the community and any foreigners living among them, emphasizing a unified law for both groups. Additionally, guidelines were provided for unintentional sins, outlining the offerings required for atonement, ensuring forgiveness for the community and individuals alike. This established a clear and inclusive system for worship and atonement, reinforcing the importance of obedience and the possibility of forgiveness. The LORD also addressed intentional sins, stating that those who act presumptuously against His commandments, whether native or foreigner, would be cut off from the community. A man found gathering sticks on the Sabbath was stoned to death as commanded by the LORD, illustrating the severity of violating the Sabbath. The LORD then instructed the Israelites to make fringes on their garments as a reminder to obey His commandments and not follow their own desires. The narrative shifts to Korah's rebellion against Moses and Aaron, challenging their leadership. Moses responded by proposing a test to determine whom the LORD has chosen, emphasizing the importance of being chosen by God for holy tasks. Korah and his followers were to present incense before the LORD, setting the stage for a divine judgment on their challenge. Moses rebuked Korah for not being content with the privileges already granted to the Levites and accused him and his followers of seeking the priesthood. Dathan and Abiram refused to meet with Moses, further escalating the conflict. Moses, angered by their rebellion, asked the LORD not to accept their offerings and defended his integrity. He then instructed Korah and his followers to present themselves before the LORD with their censers for a divine test. The entire congregation witnessed as Korah gathered them against Moses and Aaron, leading to a dramatic confrontation where the glory of the LORD appeared to all. Moses and Aaron were instructed by the LORD to separate themselves from the congregation, hinting at a forthcoming divine intervention.The children of Israel followed the LORD's commands as given to Moses. They camped by their own standards, each tribe with its ensign, around the tabernacle of the congregation. The camp of Judah, led by Nahshon son of Amminadab, was positioned to the east. Their numbers were seventy-four thousand six hundred. Next to them, the tribe of Issachar, led by Nethaneel son of Zuar, numbered fifty-four thousand four hundred. The tribe of Zebulun, under Eliab son of Helon, numbered fifty-seven thousand four hundred. The total for the camp of Judah was one hundred eighty-six thousand four hundred.

On the south, the camp of Reuben was led by Elizur son of Shedeur, numbering forty-six thousand five hundred. Adjacent were the tribe of Simeon, led by Shelumiel son of Zurishaddai, with fifty-nine thousand three hundred, and the tribe of Gad, led by Eliasaph son of Reuel, numbering forty-five thousand six hundred fifty. The total for the camp of Reuben was one hundred fifty-one thousand four hundred fifty.

The Levites, in charge of the tabernacle, camped in the middle. To the west, the camp of Ephraim was led by Elishama son of Ammihud, numbering forty thousand five hundred. With them were the tribe of Manasseh, led by Gamaliel son of Pedahzur, with thirty-two thousand two hundred, and the tribe of Benjamin, led by Abidan son of Gideoni, numbering thirty-five thousand four hundred. The total for the camp of Ephraim was one hundred eight thousand one hundred.

To the north, the camp of Dan, led by Ahiezer son of Ammishaddai, numbered sixty-two thousand seven hundred. Alongside were the tribe of Asher, led by Pagiel son of Ocran, with forty-one thousand five hundred, and the tribe of Naphtali, led by Ahira son of Enan, numbering fifty-three thousand four hundred. The total for the camp of Dan was one hundred fifty-seven thousand six hundred.

The total number of Israelites, excluding the Levites as commanded by the LORD, was six hundred three thousand five hundred fifty. The Israelites camped and moved forward as commanded, each by their standards and families. These are the generations of Aaron and Moses as recorded.The God of all flesh questioned if one man's sin should anger Him against the whole congregation. The LORD instructed Moses to tell the congregation to distance themselves from Korah, Dathan, and Abiram's dwellings. Moses, followed by elders, approached Dathan and Abiram, warning the congregation to avoid the sinners' possessions to not share in their punishment. Dathan and Abiram, with their families, stood defiantly as Moses declared that an unusual death for them would prove his divine commission. When he finished speaking, the earth opened and swallowed them, their households, and all associated with Korah, demonstrating divine judgment. This event caused fear among the Israelites, fearing they might also be swallowed. A fire from the LORD then consumed 250 men offering incense, further affirming divine authority. Eleazar was instructed to repurpose the sinners' censers into altar coverings as a memorial and warning against unauthorized offerings. Despite these events, the congregation blamed Moses and Aaron for the deaths, leading to a divine threat to consume them. Moses and Aaron interceded, with Aaron making atonement to stop a plague that had begun, saving the congregation from further wrath. The plague resulted in 14,700 deaths, not including those associated with Korah. The LORD then instructed Moses to collect rods from each tribe's leader, including Aaron's, to determine His chosen leader, promising that the chosen rod would blossom, thus ending the murmurs against Moses and Aaron. Each prince provided a rod, setting the stage for divine selection and peace among the Israelites.The LORD spoke to Moses on Mount Sinai, detailing the roles and duties of Aaron's sons, Nadab, Abihu, Eleazar, and Ithamar, as priests. Nadab and Abihu, however, died before the LORD for offering unauthorized fire, leaving Eleazar and Ithamar to serve as priests. The LORD instructed Moses to bring the Levites to Aaron so they could assist him and maintain the responsibilities of the tabernacle and its services, emphasizing that the Levites were dedicated to the LORD in place of all firstborn Israelites as a remembrance of the LORD's act in Egypt.

The Levites were to be counted and organized by their families: Gershon, Kohath, and Merari, each with specific duties related to the tabernacle's upkeep and service. The Gershonites, under Eliasaph son of Lael, were responsible for the tabernacle's fabrics and coverings. The Kohathites, led by Elizaphan son of Uzziel, were tasked with the care of sacred items like the ark and the altars. The Merarites, headed by Zuriel son of Abihail, managed the tabernacle's structural elements. Each family's duties were integral to the worship and mobility of the Israelite community, under the oversight of Eleazar, Aaron's son.Moses laid the twelve rods, including Aaron's, before the LORD in the tabernacle. The next day, Aaron's rod had budded, blossomed, and produced almonds, demonstrating the LORD's choice. This rod was to be kept as a sign against rebellion, to quell complaints against divine decisions. Despite witnessing this, the Israelites expressed fear of perishing for coming near the tabernacle. The LORD then outlined the responsibilities and privileges of Aaron and his sons, the priests, and the Levites, emphasizing their roles in the sanctuary and the priesthood. They were to bear the iniquity of the sanctuary and priesthood, ensuring the Israelites' offerings were made correctly to avoid divine wrath. The Levites were given to assist in the tabernacle's service, a gift from the LORD. Aaron and his sons were also granted a portion of the offerings and sacrifices, including the most holy things and firstfruits, as a perpetual ordinance. This was part of their inheritance, as they would have no land among the Israelites; the LORD Himself was their inheritance and portion.The LORD instructed Moses and Aaron to position themselves and their sons to the east of the tabernacle, guarding the sanctuary on behalf of the Israelites, with a strict warning that any outsider approaching would face death. The Levites, numbered by Moses and Aaron as commanded by the LORD, totaled 22,000 males aged one month and older. The LORD then directed Moses to count all firstborn Israelite males of the same age group, resulting in 22,273. The Levites were to be taken in place of these firstborn, with their livestock replacing the firstborn livestock of the Israelites, signifying that the Levites belonged to the LORD.

For the redemption of the 273 firstborn Israelites exceeding the number of Levites, Moses was to collect five shekels per person, using the sanctuary's shekel. This redemption money, totaling 1,365 shekels, was given to Aaron and his sons as commanded by the LORD.

The LORD further instructed Moses and Aaron to count the Kohathites among the Levites, focusing on those aged 30 to 50, who were eligible to work in the tabernacle. The Kohathites were responsible for the most sacred duties, including the transportation of the ark, the table of shewbread, the candlestick, the altars, and other holy items, ensuring they were properly covered and carried according to the LORD's instructions. Eleazar, Aaron's son, was assigned the oversight of the tabernacle, including the oil for the light, the sweet incense, the daily meat offering, and the anointing oil.The children of Levi were given all the tithes in Israel as an inheritance for their service in the tabernacle of the congregation. The Israelites were henceforth forbidden from approaching the tabernacle, to avoid sin and death. The Levites were tasked with the service of the tabernacle and were to bear their iniquity, having no inheritance among the children of Israel. The tithes offered by the Israelites as a heave offering to the LORD were given to the Levites. The LORD instructed Moses to tell the Levites to offer a tenth of these tithes as a heave offering to the LORD. This offering was to be considered as the produce of the threshing floor and the fullness of the winepress. The Levites were to offer a portion of their tithes to Aaron the priest as the LORD's heave offering. They were allowed to consume the remainder in any place, as a reward for their service. They were cautioned against desecrating the holy offerings of the Israelites, to avoid death.

The LORD then provided instructions for the purification ritual involving a red heifer without blemish, which was to be slaughtered outside the camp. Eleazar the priest was to sprinkle its blood in front of the tabernacle and then burn the heifer completely. The ashes were to be collected for the water of separation, a purification for sin. Anyone who touched a dead body was considered unclean for seven days and required purification with this water on the third and seventh days. Failure to purify oneself rendered a person unclean and excluded from the community. The law also covered the uncleanliness of tents, vessels, and individuals who came into contact with death, specifying the use of the ashes of the red heifer for purification.The LORD spoke to Moses and Aaron, instructing them not to exclude the Kohathites from the Levite duties. They were to be assigned specific roles and burdens to ensure their survival when handling the most sacred items. Aaron and his sons were responsible for overseeing this to prevent any deaths from improper handling. The Gershonites, also counted from thirty to fifty years old, were tasked with carrying the tabernacle's curtains, coverings, and the courtyard hangings, under the supervision of Aaron's sons. Their service was detailed, including all necessary equipment for their tasks.

The Merarites were similarly counted and assigned duties related to the tabernacle's structure, such as its boards, bars, pillars, and bases, ensuring they handled their specific burdens under Ithamar's oversight. Moses, Aaron, and the congregation leaders counted the Kohathites, Gershonites, and Merarites, determining their numbers and service roles according to the LORD's command. The Kohathites numbered 2,750, the Gershonites 2,630, and the Merarites 3,200, all serving from thirty to fifty years old, fulfilling the tabernacle service as commanded by the LORD through Moses.According to the commandment of the LORD, they were numbered by Moses, each according to his service and burden, as the LORD commanded. The LORD instructed Moses to command the Israelites to expel from the camp every leper, anyone with an issue, and anyone defiled by the dead, to prevent defilement of the camp where the LORD dwells. The Israelites complied with this command. Further instructions were given for when a man or woman commits a sin against the LORD, including confession and restitution, adding a fifth more to the principal amount, and if no kinsman is available, the restitution goes to the LORD, through the priest, along with a ram for atonement. All holy offerings brought to the priest by the Israelites shall belong to him.

The LORD also spoke to Moses about the law of jealousy. If a husband suspects his wife of infidelity without evidence, he is to bring her to the priest with an offering. The priest will then perform a ritual involving holy water and dust from the tabernacle floor, making the accused wife drink it. If she is guilty, the water will cause her physical affliction as a sign of her guilt; if innocent, she will be unharmed and able to conceive. This law applies when a wife is unfaithful or when a husband is overcome by a spirit of jealousy.A clean person shall sprinkle upon the unclean on the third and seventh days. On the seventh day, he shall purify himself, wash his clothes, and bathe in water to be clean by evening. However, an unclean person who does not purify himself will be cut off from the congregation for defiling the sanctuary of the LORD, as the water of separation has not been sprinkled on him. It is a perpetual statute that those who sprinkle the water of separation must wash their clothes, and anyone who touches the water shall be unclean until evening. Anything the unclean person touches becomes unclean, and anyone who touches it will be unclean until evening.

The children of Israel arrived in the desert of Zin in the first month, staying in Kadesh where Miriam died and was buried. Facing a lack of water, the congregation confronted Moses and Aaron, lamenting their fate and questioning why they were brought out of Egypt to die in the wilderness, a place without water or fertile land. Moses and Aaron sought the LORD's presence, where they were instructed to speak to a rock to bring forth water. Despite following the command, Moses struck the rock twice with his rod, causing water to flow but also leading to the LORD's decree that neither he nor Aaron would enter the promised land due to their lack of faith.

Moses then sent messengers to the king of Edom, seeking passage through his land but was refused, leading Israel to journey away from Edom towards Mount Hor. There, the LORD told Moses that Aaron would die because they rebelled at the water of Meribah. Aaron's priestly garments were transferred to his son Eleazar, and Aaron died on Mount Hor, witnessed by the congregation.The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing that when a man or woman vows to become a Nazarite, dedicating themselves to the LORD, they must abstain from wine, strong drink, and all products of the vine, and not cut their hair during the period of their vow. They must avoid contact with the dead, maintaining their purity. If they become defiled, they must shave their head, offer sacrifices, and restart their period of separation. The completion of the vow is marked by offerings and the shaving of the head, with the hair being placed in the fire of the peace offerings. The Nazarite then makes offerings, including a sin offering, a burnt offering, and peace offerings, along with unleavened bread, cakes, and wafers mingled with oil. The priest presents these before the LORD, and after the ceremony, the Nazarite may drink wine. This law outlines the commitments and offerings required of a Nazarite to the LORD.

The LORD also instructed Moses on how Aaron and his sons should bless the Israelites, invoking the LORD's protection, grace, and peace upon them. This blessing places the LORD's name upon the Israelites, ensuring His blessing.

Following the establishment of the tabernacle, the leaders of Israel, representing their tribes, brought offerings to the LORD, including wagons and oxen to aid in the service of the tabernacle. These were distributed to the Levites according to their duties in the service of the tabernacle, as directed by the LORD through Moses.Two wagons and four oxen were given to the sons of Gershon for their service, and four wagons and eight oxen to the sons of Merari, under the supervision of Ithamar, Aaron's son. The sons of Kohath received none, as their duty involved carrying the sanctuary items on their shoulders. The princes made offerings for the altar's dedication, each on his designated day. Nahshon from Judah offered a silver charger and bowl, both filled with fine flour and oil, a gold spoon with incense, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for a burnt offering, a goat for a sin offering, and two oxen, five rams, goats, and lambs for peace offerings. Nethaneel of Issachar and Eliab of Zebulun made similar offerings. Elizur of Reuben, Shelumiel of Simeon, and Eliasaph of Gad also presented their offerings, each including a silver charger and bowl, a gold spoon of incense, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for burnt offerings, a goat for a sin offering, and multiple animals for peace offerings. Elishama of Ephraim offered similar items on the seventh day.On the eighth day, Gamaliel, prince of Manasseh, offered his dedication gifts: a silver charger and a bowl, both filled with fine flour and oil for a meat offering, a golden spoon full of incense, a young bullock, a ram, a lamb for a burnt offering, a goat for a sin offering, and for peace offerings, two oxen, five rams, goats, and lambs. Following him, on the ninth day, Abidan of Benjamin presented similar offerings. Ahiezer of Dan made his offerings on the tenth day, including the same array of items. On the eleventh day, Pagiel of Asher and on the twelfth day, Ahira of Naphtali, each contributed identical offerings for the dedication of the altar.

The dedication ceremony concluded with the princes of Israel offering twelve silver chargers, bowls, and gold spoons. The total weight of the silver vessels was two thousand and four hundred shekels, according to the sanctuary's shekel. The gold spoons weighed a total of one hundred and twenty shekels. For burnt offerings, twelve bullocks, rams, and lambs were offered, along with twelve goats for sin offerings. The peace offerings consisted of twenty-four bullocks, sixty rams, goats, and lambs. This marked the completion of the altar's dedication.

When Moses entered the tabernacle to speak with God, he heard a voice speaking to him from above the mercy seat on the ark of testimony.20:29 And when all the congregation saw that Aaron was dead, they mourned for Aaron thirty days, even all the house of Israel. 21:1 And when king Arad the Canaanite, which dwelt in the south, heard tell that Israel came by the way of the spies; then he fought against Israel, and took some of them prisoners. 21:2 And Israel vowed a vow unto the LORD, and said, If thou wilt indeed deliver this people into my hand, then I will utterly destroy their cities. 21:3 And the LORD hearkened to the voice of Israel, and delivered up the Canaanites; and they utterly destroyed them and their cities: and he called the name of the place Hormah. 21:4 And they journeyed from mount Hor by the way of the Red sea, to compass the land of Edom: and the soul of the people was much discouraged because of the way. 21:5 And the people spake against God, and against Moses, Wherefore have ye brought us up out of Egypt to die in the wilderness? for there is no bread, neither is there any water; and our soul loatheth this light bread. 21:6 And the LORD sent fiery serpents among the people, and they bit the people; and much people of Israel died. 21:7 Therefore the people came to Moses, and said, We have sinned, for we have spoken against the LORD, and against thee; pray unto the LORD, that he take away the serpents from us. And Moses prayed for the people. 21:8 And the LORD said unto Moses, Make thee a fiery serpent, and set it upon a pole: and it shall come to pass, that every one that is bitten, when he looketh upon it, shall live. 21:9 And Moses made a serpent of brass, and put it upon a pole, and it came to pass, that if a serpent had bitten any man, when he beheld the serpent of brass, he lived. 21:10 And the children of Israel set forward, and pitched in Oboth. 21:11 And they journeyed from Oboth, and pitched at Ijeabarim, in the wilderness which is before Moab, toward the sunrising. 21:12 From thence they removed, and pitched in the valley of Zared. 21:13 From thence they removed, and pitched on the other side of Arnon, which is in the wilderness that cometh out of the coasts of the Amorites: for Arnon is the border of Moab, between Moab and the Amorites. 21:14 Wherefore it is said in the book of the wars of the LORD, What he did in the Red sea, and in the brooks of Arnon, 21:15 And at the stream of the brooks that goeth down to the dwelling of Ar, and lieth upon the border of Moab. 21:16 And from thence they went to Beer: that is the well whereof the LORD spake unto Moses, Gather the people together, and I will give them water. 21:17 Then Israel sang this song, Spring up, O well; sing ye unto it: 21:18 The princes digged the well, the nobles of the people digged it, by the direction of the lawgiver, with their staves. And from the wilderness they went to Mattanah: 21:19 And from Mattanah to Nahaliel: and from Nahaliel to Bamoth: 21:20 And from Bamoth in the valley, that is in the country of Moab, to the top of Pisgah, which looketh toward Jeshimon. 21:21 And Israel sent messengers unto Sihon king of the Amorites, saying, 21:22 Let me pass through thy land: we will not turn into the fields, or into the vineyards; we will not drink of the waters of the well: but we will go along by the kings high way, until we be past thy borders. 21:23 And Sihon would not suffer Israel to pass through his border: but Sihon gathered all his people together, and went out against Israel into the wilderness: and he came to Jahaz, and fought against Israel. 21:24 And Israel smote him with the edge of the sword, and possessed his land from Arnon unto Jabbok, even unto the children of Ammon: for the border of the children of Ammon was strong. 21:25 And Israel took all these cities: and Israel dwelt in all the cities of the Amorites, in Heshbon, and in all the villages thereof. 21:26 For Heshbon was the city of Sihon the king of the Amorites, who had fought against the former king of Moab, and taken all his land out of his hand, even unto Arnon. 21:27 Wherefore they that speak in proverbs say, Come into Heshbon, let the city of Sihon be built and prepared: 21:28 For there is a fire gone out of Heshbon, a flame from the city of Sihon: it hath consumed Ar of Moab, and the lords of the high places of Arnon. 21:29 Woe to thee, Moab! thou art undone, O people of Chemosh: he hath given his sons that escaped, and his daughters, into captivity unto Sihon king of the Amorites. 21:30 We have shot at them; Heshbon is perished even unto Dibon, and we have laid them waste even unto Nophah, which reacheth unto Medeba. 21:31 Thus Israel dwelt in the land of the Amorites. 21:32 And Moses sent to spy out Jaazer, and they took the villages thereof, and drove out the Amorites that were there. 21:33 And they turned and went up by the way of Bashan: and Og the king of Bashan went out against them, he, and all his people, to the battle at Edrei. 21:34 And the LORD said unto Moses, Fear him not: for I have delivered him into thy hand, and all his people, and his land.The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell Aaron about the lighting of the lamps so that the seven lamps would illuminate the area in front of the candlestick. Aaron followed these instructions, lighting the lamps as commanded. The candlestick itself was made of beaten gold, crafted according to the pattern shown to Moses by the LORD.

The LORD then instructed Moses to take the Levites from among the Israelites and purify them. This purification process involved sprinkling them with water of purification, shaving their bodies, and washing their clothes. After purification, the Levites were to offer a young bullock with a grain offering and another for a sin offering. The Levites were presented before the LORD, with the Israelites laying their hands on them, symbolizing their dedication to the LORD's service. The Levites then laid their hands on the bullocks, one of which was offered as a sin offering and the other as a burnt offering to atone for the Levites.

The Levites were set apart from the other Israelites and dedicated to the LORD. They were to serve in the tabernacle, replacing the firstborn of Israel who were originally sanctified to the LORD. The Levites were given to Aaron and his sons to assist in the service of the tabernacle and to make atonement for the Israelites, preventing plagues among them.

Moses, Aaron, and the Israelites followed the LORD's commands regarding the Levites, purifying them and integrating them into their service in the tabernacle. The Levites were to begin their service at the age of twenty-five and retire at the age of fifty, after which they could assist their brethren but not perform the service.

The LORD then instructed Moses about keeping the Passover in the wilderness of Sinai, emphasizing the importance of observing it at the appointed time with all its rites and ceremonies. Despite some Israelites being unable to participate due to impurity from contact with a dead body, the Passover was observed as commanded by the LORD.Moses instructed the Israelites on how to observe the Passover if they were unclean or on a journey, emphasizing the importance of keeping it on the fourteenth day of the second month with unleavened bread and bitter herbs, without leaving any until morning or breaking any bones. Those who were clean but did not observe Passover would be cut off from their people for not bringing the LORD's offering at the appointed time. Strangers among the Israelites were also allowed to keep the Passover, following the same rules.

When the tabernacle was set up, a cloud covered it by day and appeared as fire by night, guiding the Israelites on when to journey and when to camp. They followed the LORD's command, moving or staying based on the cloud's presence. If the cloud stayed, they did not journey, but when it lifted, they journeyed, regardless of the duration.

The LORD instructed Moses to make two silver trumpets for calling the assembly and directing the camps. Different signals were used for assembling the community, moving the camps, or preparing for war. The trumpets also marked times of gladness, solemn days, and the beginnings of months, serving as a memorial before God.

On the twentieth day of the second month, in the second year, the cloud lifted from the tabernacle, and the Israelites journeyed from Sinai to the wilderness of Paran, following the LORD's command through Moses. The camp of Judah led, followed by the other tribes in an organized manner.Nethaneel the son of Zuar led the tribe of Issachar. Eliab the son of Helon led the tribe of Zebulun. The tabernacle was taken down, and the sons of Gershon and Merari carried it. The camp of Reuben, led by Elizur the son of Shedeur, moved forward. Shelumiel the son of Zurishaddai led the tribe of Simeon. Eliasaph the son of Deuel led the tribe of Gad. The Kohathites carried the sanctuary, and the tabernacle was set up as they arrived. Elishama the son of Ammihud led the tribe of Ephraim. Gamaliel the son of Pedahzur led the tribe of Manasseh. Abidan the son of Gideoni led the tribe of Benjamin. The camp of Dan, the rear guard, was led by Ahiezer the son of Ammishaddai. Pagiel the son of Ocran led the tribe of Asher. Ahira the son of Enan led the tribe of Naphtali. This describes the organization of the Israelites' journey.

Moses invited Hobab, the son of Raguel the Midianite, to join them, promising the LORD's blessings. Hobab initially refused but was persuaded to guide them through the wilderness. They departed from the mount of the LORD, with the ark of the covenant leading to find a resting place. The cloud of the LORD was upon them by day.

When the ark set forward, Moses invoked the LORD's protection against enemies. When it rested, he prayed for the LORD's return to the people. The people's complaints about their hardships displeased the LORD, leading to a fire that consumed some of them. Moses prayed, and the fire was quenched. The place was named Taberah. The people lamented the lack of meat, reminiscing about the food in Egypt, despite the manna provided by the LORD. Moses, overwhelmed by the people's complaints, pleaded with the LORD for help, feeling unable to bear the burden alone. The LORD instructed Moses to gather seventy elders to share the burden of leadership."Thou shalt do to him as thou didst unto Sihon king of the Amorites, which dwelt at Heshbon. So they smote him, and his sons, and all his people, until there was none left him alive: and they possessed his land. And the children of Israel set forward, and pitched in the plains of Moab on this side Jordan by Jericho. And Balak the son of Zippor saw all that Israel had done to the Amorites. And Moab was sore afraid of the people, because they were many: and Moab was distressed because of the children of Israel. And Moab said unto the elders of Midian, Now shall this company lick up all that are round about us, as the ox licketh up the grass of the field. And Balak the son of Zippor was king of the Moabites at that time. He sent messengers therefore unto Balaam the son of Beor to Pethor, which is by the river of the land of the children of his people, to call him, saying, Behold, there is a people come out from Egypt: behold, they cover the face of the earth, and they abide over against me: Come now therefore, I pray thee, curse me this people; for they are too mighty for me: peradventure I shall prevail, that we may smite them, and that I may drive them out of the land: for I wot that he whom thou blessest is blessed, and he whom thou cursest is cursed. And the elders of Moab and the elders of Midian departed with the rewards of divination in their hand; and they came unto Balaam, and spake unto him the words of Balak. And he said unto them, Lodge here this night, and I will bring you word again, as the LORD shall speak unto me: and the princes of Moab abode with Balaam. And God came unto Balaam, and said, What men are these with thee? And Balaam said unto God, Balak the son of Zippor, king of Moab, hath sent unto me, saying, Behold, there is a people come out of Egypt, which covereth the face of the earth: come now, curse me them; peradventure I shall be able to overcome them, and drive them out. And God said unto Balaam, Thou shalt not go with them; thou shalt not curse the people: for they are blessed. And Balaam rose up in the morning, and said unto the princes of Balak, Get you into your land: for the LORD refuseth to give me leave to go with you. And the princes of Moab rose up, and they went unto Balak, and said, Balaam refuseth to come with us. And Balak sent yet again princes, more, and more honourable than they. And they came to Balaam, and said to him, Thus saith Balak the son of Zippor, Let nothing, I pray thee, hinder thee from coming unto me: For I will promote thee unto very great honour, and I will do whatsoever thou sayest unto me: come therefore, I pray thee, curse me this people. And Balaam answered and said unto the servants of Balak, If Balak would give me his house full of silver and gold, I cannot go beyond the word of the LORD my God, to do less or more. Now therefore, I pray you, tarry ye also here this night, that I may know what the LORD will say unto me more. And God came unto Balaam at night, and said unto him, If the men come to call thee, rise up, and go with them; but yet the word which I shall say unto thee, that shalt thou do. And Balaam rose up in the morning, and saddled his ass, and went with the princes of Moab. And God's anger was kindled because he went: and the angel of the LORD stood in the way for an adversary against him. Now he was riding upon his ass, and his two servants were with him. And the ass saw the angel of the LORD standing in the way, and his sword drawn in his hand: and the ass turned aside out of the way, and went into the field: and Balaam smote the ass, to turn her into the way. This describes the organization of the Israelites' journey.

Moses invited Hobab, the son of Raguel the Midianite, to join them, promising the LORD's blessings. Hobab initially refused but was persuaded to guide them through the wilderness. They departed from the mount of the LORD, with the ark of the covenant leading to find a resting place. The cloud of the LORD was upon them by day.

When the ark set forward, Moses invoked the LORD's protection against enemies. When it rested, he prayed for the LORD's return to the people. The people's complaints about their hardships displeased the LORD, leading to a fire that consumed some of them. Moses prayed, and the fire was quenched. The place was named Taberah. The people lamented the lack of meat, reminiscing about the food in Egypt, despite the manna provided by the LORD. Moses, overwhelmed by the people's complaints, pleaded with the LORD for help, feeling unable to bear the burden alone. The LORD instructed Moses to gather seventy elders to share the burden of leadership.

The LORD promised to take some of the spirit from Moses and put it upon the seventy elders to help bear the burden of the people. Moses was told to inform the people that they would eat meat until it became loathsome to them, as a response to their complaints. Despite Moses' doubts about providing meat for such a large number, the LORD assured him that His power was sufficient. The seventy elders prophesied when the spirit rested upon them. Eldad and Medad, who were not at the tabernacle, also prophesied in the camp, leading to a discussion about whether prophecy should be exclusive. Moses expressed a wish that all the LORD's people were prophets. A wind from the LORD brought quails to provide meat for the people, but while they were eating, the LORD struck them with a plague because of their desires. The narrative then shifts to Miriam and Aaron speaking against Moses because of his Cushite wife, questioning whether the LORD had spoken only through Moses. The LORD affirmed Moses' unique role and rebuked Miriam and Aaron, causing Miriam to become leprous. Aaron pleaded with Moses for forgiveness, and Moses prayed for Miriam's healing.Miriam was shut out from the camp for seven days due to her actions, and the people did not journey until she was brought back. The Israelites then moved from Hazeroth to the wilderness of Paran. The LORD instructed Moses to send men to scout the land of Canaan, assigning a leader from each tribe for this task. These scouts, including notable figures like Caleb son of Jephunneh and Oshea son of Nun (whom Moses renamed Joshua), were sent to assess the land's fertility, the strength of its inhabitants, and the nature of its cities.

Upon their return after forty days, the scouts reported that the land was indeed flowing with milk and honey, showcasing its fruitfulness. However, they also warned of the strong inhabitants and fortified cities, particularly noting the presence of giants, which caused fear among the Israelites. Caleb tried to encourage the people, believing they could conquer the land, but the majority of the scouts disagreed, fearing the inhabitants were too powerful.

This negative report led to widespread despair among the Israelites, who lamented their departure from Egypt and even proposed choosing a new leader to return to slavery. This reaction highlighted their lack of faith and trust in the LORD's promise and protection.Moses and Aaron, in response to the congregation's outcry, prostrated themselves before the assembly of Israel. Joshua and Caleb, scouts of the land, passionately defended its value, asserting it as exceedingly good and attainable if the LORD favored them. They urged against rebellion and fear of the land's inhabitants, emphasizing the LORD's support. Despite their faith, the congregation reacted violently, proposing to stone them. At this moment, the LORD's glory manifested in the tabernacle, confronting Moses with the people's continuous defiance and proposing to disinherit them for a new nation. Moses, however, interceded, arguing that such an act would tarnish the LORD's reputation among the Egyptians and other nations, who knew of His presence and miracles among Israel. He appealed for the LORD's mercy and forgiveness, highlighting His enduring patience and mercy. The LORD agreed to pardon the people as Moses requested but declared that those who doubted His power would not see the promised land, except for Caleb and Joshua, due to their steadfast faith. He then decreed that the Israelites would wander the wilderness for forty years, bearing the consequences of their disbelief, with only their children entering the promised land. The men who spread the negative report were struck down by a plague from the LORD, while Joshua and Caleb survived. Moses communicated these declarations to the Israelites, marking a pivotal moment of judgment and mercy.After mourning their fate, the Israelites impulsively attempted to enter the promised land without God's blessing, leading to their defeat by the Amalekites and Canaanites. God then instructed Moses on offerings to be made in the land He would give them, detailing the requirements for various sacrifices to maintain a relationship with Him. These instructions included offerings for unintentional sins, emphasizing the importance of atonement and the unity of law for both Israelites and foreigners living among them. The LORD also allocated offerings and holy things to Aaron and his descendants as provisions and for their service, including the most holy offerings, heave offerings, and firstfruits, which were to be consumed in a state of purity.

Moses also divided the other half of the spoils, which belonged to the rest of the Israelite community, ensuring a portion was given to the Levites who served the tabernacle of the LORD.

The officers of the Israelite army reported to Moses that not a single man was lost in battle and presented offerings of gold jewelry to make atonement before the LORD. The total gold offered was recorded and brought into the tabernacle as a memorial.

The narrative then shifts to the request of the Reubenites and Gadites, who, having a large number of cattle, saw the lands of Jazer and Gilead as suitable for livestock. They requested these lands as their possession instead of crossing over the Jordan into the Promised Land. Moses challenged their request, reminding them of the discouragement their ancestors caused among the Israelites when they refused to enter the Promised Land, invoking the LORD's anger. He highlighted the consequences of their refusal to follow the LORD fully, except for Caleb and Joshua, who were faithful. Moses warned them against repeating their ancestors' mistakes, which could provoke the LORD's anger and result in further punishment. The Reubenites and Gadites proposed a compromise, offering to build enclosures for their livestock and cities for their families while they themselves would go armed before the Israelites until they had secured their inheritance.The Reubenites and Gadites pledged to Moses that they would lead the Israelites into battle, ensuring their safety until the promised lands were secured. They agreed not to return to their homes until every Israelite had received their inheritance. They clarified that their inheritance lay on the east side of the Jordan, not in the lands across it. Moses responded, outlining conditions for their agreement: if they fulfilled their promise to fight alongside the Israelites until the land was conquered, they would be free of obligation and their lands on the east side of the Jordan would be theirs. However, failure to do so would be considered a sin against the LORD.

Moses commanded the construction of cities for their families and folds for their livestock, emphasizing the importance of fulfilling their vows. The tribes of Gad and Reuben committed to Moses's commands, ensuring their warriors would lead the battle before the LORD. Moses then instructed Eleazar the priest, Joshua, and the leaders of the Israelite tribes on how to integrate the lands of Gad, Reuben, and the half-tribe of Manasseh if they upheld their commitment.

The narrative details the construction of various cities and territories by the tribes of Gad and Reuben, as well as the conquests by the tribe of Manasseh. It concludes with a recounting of the Israelites' journey from Egypt under Moses and Aaron's leadership, highlighting significant locations and events, including the departure from Rameses, the crossing of the Red Sea, and encampments at various sites throughout their journey towards the Promised Land.The children of Levi were given all the tithes in Israel as an inheritance for their service in the tabernacle of the congregation. The Israelites were henceforth forbidden from approaching the tabernacle to prevent them from bearing sin and dying. The Levites were tasked with the service of the tabernacle and were to bear their iniquity, a statute to be observed forever, signifying that they would have no inheritance among the children of Israel. The tithes offered by the children of Israel as a heave offering to the LORD were given to the Levites as their inheritance. The LORD instructed Moses to tell the Levites that when they receive the tithes from the Israelites, they must offer a tenth of it as a heave offering to the LORD. This offering would be considered as the produce of the threshing floor and the fullness of the winepress. The Levites were to offer a heave offering from all their tithes to Aaron the priest. They were to offer the best part of their gifts as a heave offering to the LORD, and this would be counted to the Levites as the produce of the threshing floor and the winepress. They were allowed to eat it anywhere with their households as a reward for their service in the tabernacle. They were warned not to pollute the holy things of the children of Israel to avoid death.

The LORD then gave Moses and Aaron instructions regarding the red heifer, which was to be without defect and never yoked. Eleazar the priest was to oversee its slaughter outside the camp, and its blood was to be sprinkled in front of the tabernacle. The heifer was to be completely burned, and the priest was to include cedar wood, hyssop, and scarlet in the burning. The priest and the one who burned the heifer were to wash and be considered unclean until evening. The ashes of the heifer were to be collected and kept for the water of separation, a purification for sin, and this statute was to be for the children of Israel and the sojourning strangers forever. Touching a dead body rendered a person unclean for seven days, requiring purification with the water on the third and seventh days. Failure to purify oneself resulted in defilement of the LORD's tabernacle and exclusion from Israel. The law also covered the uncleanliness of tents, open vessels, and those who touch the dead in various contexts, outlining the use of the heifer's ashes and running water for purification.A clean person shall sprinkle upon the unclean on the third and seventh days. On the seventh day, he shall purify himself, wash his clothes, and bathe in water to be clean by evening. If a man remains unclean and does not purify himself, he shall be cut off from the congregation for defiling the sanctuary of the LORD; the water of separation has not been sprinkled on him, making him unclean. It shall be a perpetual statute that he who sprinkles the water of separation shall wash his clothes, and anyone who touches the water shall be unclean until evening. Whatever the unclean person touches becomes unclean, and anyone who touches it shall be unclean until evening.

The children of Israel, the whole congregation, came into the desert of Zin in the first month, and the people stayed in Kadesh. There, Miriam died and was buried. The congregation faced a lack of water, leading them to confront Moses and Aaron. They lamented their fate, questioning why they were brought into the wilderness to die and regretting their departure from Egypt. Moses and Aaron sought the LORD's presence, where they were instructed to speak to a rock to bring forth water for the congregation and their animals. However, Moses struck the rock twice with his rod instead of speaking to it, which led to water flowing out abundantly. Despite this, the LORD told Moses and Aaron that because they did not show faith to sanctify Him in front of the Israelites, they would not lead the congregation into the promised land.

Moses sent messengers to the king of Edom, seeking passage through his land but was denied. Edom threatened to confront them with force if they attempted to pass. Consequently, Israel turned away from Edom. The congregation then traveled from Kadesh to Mount Hor, where the LORD told Moses that Aaron would die because they rebelled against His command at the water of Meribah. Moses was instructed to take Aaron and Eleazar, his son, to Mount Hor, where Aaron's priestly garments were transferred to Eleazar before Aaron died. Moses and Eleazar then returned to the congregation.The Reubenites and Gadites pledged to Moses that they would lead the Israelites into battle, ensuring their safety until the promised lands were secured. They agreed not to return to their homes until every Israelite had received their inheritance, specifying that their inheritance lay on the east side of the Jordan, not in the lands across it. Moses outlined conditions for their agreement: if they fulfilled their promise to fight alongside the Israelites until the land was conquered, they would be free of obligation and their lands on the east side of the Jordan would be theirs. However, failure to do so would be considered a sin against the LORD.

Moses commanded the construction of cities for their families and folds for their livestock, emphasizing the importance of fulfilling their vows. The tribes of Gad and Reuben committed to Moses's commands, ensuring their warriors would lead the battle before the LORD. Moses instructed Eleazar the priest, Joshua, and the leaders of the Israelite tribes on how to integrate the lands of Gad, Reuben, and the half-tribe of Manasseh if they upheld their commitment.

The narrative details the construction of various cities and territories by the tribes of Gad and Reuben, as well as the conquests by the tribe of Manasseh. It concludes with a recounting of the Israelites' journey from Egypt under Moses and Aaron's leadership, highlighting significant locations and events, including the departure from Rameses, the crossing of the Red Sea, and encampments at various sites throughout their journey towards the Promised Land.

The Israelites encamped at multiple locations, including Rephidim, the wilderness of Sinai, Kibrothhattaavah, Hazeroth, Rithmah, and many others, eventually reaching the plains of Moab by Jordan near Jericho. The LORD instructed Moses in the plains of Moab, detailing the process for the Israelites to drive out the inhabitants of Canaan, destroy their idols, and divide the land among the tribes. The LORD warned of the consequences if the Israelites failed to drive out the inhabitants of the land. Further instructions were given regarding the borders of the land of Canaan, including the south quarter from the wilderness of Zin along by the coast of Edom, the western border with the great sea, and the north border from the great sea to mount Hor.The borders of the land designated for the Israelites were detailed, extending from Hazarenan to Zedad and further to the Sea of Chinnereth and the Jordan, culminating at the Salt Sea. This demarcation was to encompass the land allotted to the nine tribes and the half-tribe, as commanded by the LORD. The tribes of Reuben, Gad, and the half-tribe of Manasseh had already received their inheritance east of Jordan, near Jericho.

The LORD instructed Moses to appoint leaders from each tribe to oversee the division of the land. Notable figures included Eleazar the priest, Joshua son of Nun, and representatives from each tribe such as Caleb for Judah and Hanniel for Manasseh. These individuals were tasked with dividing the land among the Israelites in Canaan.

Furthermore, the LORD commanded the provision of cities for the Levites within the Israelites' inheritance, including suburbs for their livestock and belongings. A total of forty-eight cities were to be allocated to the Levites, with six designated as cities of refuge for those who accidentally caused a death, allowing them to seek asylum and avoid vengeance until a fair trial could be conducted. This system of cities of refuge was established to ensure justice and protection for all members of the community, including Israelites, strangers, and sojourners alike.And when all the congregation saw that Aaron was dead, they mourned for Aaron thirty days, even all the house of Israel. When king Arad the Canaanite, who dwelt in the south, heard that Israel came by the way of the spies, he fought against Israel and took some of them prisoners. Israel vowed a vow unto the LORD, saying, If thou wilt indeed deliver this people into my hand, then I will utterly destroy their cities. The LORD hearkened to the voice of Israel and delivered up the Canaanites; they utterly destroyed them and their cities, and called the name of the place Hormah. They journeyed from mount Hor by the way of the Red sea, to compass the land of Edom, and the soul of the people was much discouraged because of the way. The people spoke against God and Moses, questioning why they were brought up out of Egypt to die in the wilderness for lack of bread and water, and loathing the light bread provided. The LORD sent fiery serpents among the people, which bit them, causing many deaths. The people admitted their sin of speaking against the LORD and Moses, and asked Moses to pray to the LORD to take away the serpents. Moses prayed, and the LORD instructed him to make a fiery serpent and set it upon a pole, promising that anyone bitten who looked upon it would live. Moses made a serpent of brass, put it upon a pole, and those bitten who beheld the brass serpent lived. The children of Israel then journeyed and pitched in various locations, eventually reaching the valley of Zared, the other side of Arnon, and areas near Moab and the Amorites. They sang a song at Beer, where the LORD provided water. Israel sent messengers to Sihon king of the Amorites, seeking passage through his land without disturbing the fields, vineyards, or drinking water from the wells, but Sihon refused and fought against Israel. Israel defeated Sihon, possessed his land, and dwelt in the cities of the Amorites. Heshbon became a significant city for Israel, previously the city of Sihon, who had conquered it from the former king of Moab. The victory over Moab and the Amorites was celebrated, and Israel's dominance in the region was established. Moses sent spies to Jaazer, captured it along with its villages, and drove out the Amorites there. They then faced Og king of Bashan, whom the LORD promised Moses they would defeat, providing his land to Israel."Anyone who kills a person with a stone or a wooden weapon is considered a murderer and must be put to death. The avenger of blood has the right to kill the murderer upon encounter. However, if the killing was accidental, without enmity or premeditation, the congregation shall judge the case. The accidental killer may seek refuge in a city of refuge until the high priest's death, after which they can return to their land. This law serves as a statute of judgment for all generations. Witnesses are required for the execution of a murderer, and no compensation can be accepted for the life of a murderer or for allowing an accidental killer to return home before the high priest's death. The land must not be defiled by bloodshed, for it can only be cleansed by the blood of the one who shed it.

The families of Gilead, from the tribe of Manasseh, addressed an inheritance issue to Moses and the leaders, concerning the inheritance of Zelophehad's daughters. They were concerned that if Zelophehad's daughters married outside their tribe, their inheritance would transfer to another tribe. Moses, following God's command, instructed that women with inheritances marry within their tribe to prevent the transfer of land between tribes. This ensured that each tribe retained its allotted inheritance. The daughters of Zelophehad obeyed this command, marrying within their tribe, thus keeping their inheritance within the tribe of Manasseh."The commandments and judgments commanded by the LORD through Moses to the children of Israel were delivered in the plains of Moab by Jordan near Jericho. The transition to the Book of Deuteronomy begins with Moses addressing all of Israel in the wilderness, outlining the journey from Horeb to Kadeshbarnea and emphasizing the importance of obeying God's commands to possess the land promised to their ancestors, Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob.

Moses recounts the appointment of leaders and judges to assist in governing the people, emphasizing the importance of fair and impartial judgment. He reminds the Israelites of their journey from Horeb through the wilderness to the border of the Amorites, encouraging them to trust in the LORD and not be discouraged by the challenges ahead.

Despite God's assurances and the positive report from the spies sent to scout the land, the Israelites doubted and rebelled against God's command to enter the land. Moses urged them not to fear the inhabitants of the land, for the LORD would fight for them as He had in Egypt and throughout their journey in the wilderness. However, their lack of faith in the LORD's promise led to further challenges and delays in entering the promised land.The LORD guided the Israelites, showing the way by fire at night and by a cloud by day. The Israelites' journey continued through the wilderness, avoiding conflict with the Edomites as commanded by God, who provided for their needs. Did ever people hear the voice of God speaking out of the midst of the fire, as thou hast heard, and live? Or hath God assayed to go and take him a nation from the midst of another nation, by temptations, by signs, and by wonders, and by war, and by a mighty hand, and by a stretched out arm, and by great terrors, according to all that the LORD your God did for you in Egypt before your eyes? Unto thee it was showed, that thou mightest know that the LORD he is God; there is none else beside him. Out of heaven he made thee to hear his voice, that he might instruct thee: and upon earth he showed thee his great fire; and thou heardest his words out of the midst of the fire. And because he loved thy fathers, therefore he chose their seed after them, and brought thee out in his sight with his mighty power out of Egypt; To drive out nations from before thee greater and mightier than thou art, to bring thee in, to give thee their land for an inheritance, as it is this day. Know therefore this day, and consider it in thine heart, that the LORD he is God in heaven above, and upon the earth beneath: there is none else. Thou shalt keep therefore his statutes, and his commandments, which I command thee this day, that it may go well with thee, and with thy children after thee, and that thou mayest prolong thy days upon the earth, which the LORD thy God gives thee, forever. Then Moses severed three cities on this side Jordan toward the sunrising; That the slayer might flee thither, which should kill his neighbor unawares, and hated him not in times past; and that fleeing unto one of these cities he might live: Namely, Bezer in the wilderness, in the plain country, of the Reubenites; and Ramoth in Gilead, of the Gadites; and Golan in Bashan, of the Manassites. And this is the law which Moses set before the children of Israel: These are the testimonies, and the statutes, and the judgments, which Moses spoke unto the children of Israel, after they came forth out of Egypt. On this side Jordan, in the valley over against Bethpeor, in the land of Sihon king of the Amorites, who dwelt at Heshbon, whom Moses and the children of Israel smote, after they were come forth out of Egypt: And they possessed his land, and the land of Og king of Bashan, two kings of the Amorites, which were on this side Jordan toward the sunrising; From Aroer, which is by the bank of the river Arnon, even unto mount Sion, which is Hermon, And all the plain on this side Jordan eastward, even unto the sea of the plain, under the springs of Pisgah. And Moses called all Israel, and said unto them, Hear, O Israel, the statutes and judgments which I speak in your ears this day, that ye may learn them, and keep, and do them."Balak brought Balaam to the top of Peor, overlooking Jeshimon. Balaam requested seven altars and the preparation of seven bullocks and rams. Balak complied, offering a bullock and a ram on each altar. Observing the LORD's pleasure in blessing Israel, Balaam refrained from seeking enchantments and instead faced the wilderness. He saw Israel encamped by tribes and was moved by the spirit of God. Balaam's oracle praised Israel's beauty and strength, likening their spread to valleys, gardens by rivers, and trees planted by the LORD. He prophesied their abundant prosperity, their king's exaltation over Agag, and their victory over enemies. Balaam declared that God, who brought them out of Egypt, would enable them to defeat nations and remain unchallenged, blessing those who bless them and cursing those who curse them.

Angered by Balaam's blessings on Israel, Balak dismissed him, lamenting the lost opportunity for honor. Balaam reminded Balak of his adherence to the LORD's command, unable to say anything but what God instructed. He then predicted the future interactions between their peoples. Balaam's further prophecies spoke of a star and scepter arising from Jacob, defeating Moab and Edom, and establishing dominion. He foresaw the end of Amalek and the temporary security of the Kenites until their eventual defeat. His final prophecies warned of invasions and the ultimate downfall of Asshur and Eber.

Following these events, Israel engaged in idolatry with Moab, provoking the LORD's anger. God commanded Moses to execute the idolaters to quell His wrath. Amidst this, Phinehas acted decisively against an Israelite man and a Midianite woman, demonstrating zeal for the LORD's command.Phinehas, the son of Eleazar and grandson of Aaron the priest, acted zealously for God's sake among the Israelites, turning away God's wrath and preventing their destruction. For his zeal, God granted him a covenant of peace and an everlasting priesthood for him and his descendants. The Israelite man killed with the Midianite woman was Zimri, a Simeonite prince, and the woman was Cozbi, daughter of a Midianite leader. God then instructed Moses to confront the Midianites for their deception.

After the plague, God commanded Moses and Eleazar to take a census of the Israelite men able to go to war. The census included detailed family lineages and numbers from each tribe, starting with Reuben and listing his descendants, then Simeon, Gad, Judah, Issachar, Zebulun, and Joseph's sons Manasseh and Ephraim, among others. The census aimed to organize the tribes and assess their military strength, continuing the narrative of the Israelites' journey and preparation for entering the Promised Land.The Machirites descended from Machir, who begat Gilead, leading to the Gileadites. The sons of Gilead included the families of the Jeezerites, Helekites, Asrielites, Shechemites, Shemidaites, and Hepherites. Zelophehad, son of Hepher, had only daughters: Mahlah, Noah, Hoglah, Milcah, and Tirzah. The Manasseh families numbered 52,700. Ephraim's descendants were the Shuthalhites, Bachrites, and Tahanites, with the Eranites descending from Shuthelah, totaling 32,500. The Benjaminites included the Belaites, Ashbelites, Ahiramites, Shuphamites, and Huphamites, with Ard and Naaman from Bela, totaling 45,600. Dan's sole family was the Shuhamites, numbering 64,400. Asher's families were the Jimnites, Jesuites, and Beriites, with a daughter named Sarah, totaling 53,400. Naphtali's families were the Jahzeelites, Gunites, Jezerites, and Shillemites, totaling 45,400. The total Israelite count was 601,730. The land was to be divided by inheritance, with larger shares for larger families and smaller shares for smaller ones, determined by lot. The Levites, including the Gershonites, Kohathites, Merarites, Libnites, Hebronites, Mahlites, Mushites, and Korathites, were not given land inheritance. Among the Levites, Amram, married to Jochebed, fathered Aaron, Moses, and Miriam. Aaron's sons were Nadab, Abihu, Eleazar, and Ithamar. Nadab and Abihu died offering unauthorized fire before the Lord. The Levites numbered 23,000 males over a month old. These were counted by Moses and Eleazar in Moab, near Jericho. None of those counted in Sinai survived to enter the land, except Caleb and Joshua. The daughters of Zelophehad then approached Moses.LORD our God made a covenant with us in Horeb. The LORD made not this covenant with our fathers, but with us, who are all here alive this day. The LORD talked with you face to face in the mount out of the midst of the fire, (I stood between the LORD and you at that time, to show you the word of the LORD: for you were afraid by reason of the fire, and went not up into the mount;) saying, I am the LORD thy God, which brought thee out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage. Thou shalt have none other gods before me. Thou shalt not make thee any graven image, or any likeness of anything that is in heaven above, or that is in the earth beneath, or that is in the waters beneath the earth: Thou shalt not bow down thyself unto them, nor serve them: for I the LORD thy God am a jealous God, visiting the iniquity of the fathers upon the children unto the third and fourth generation of them that hate me, And showing mercy unto thousands of them that love me and keep my commandments. Thou shalt not take the name of the LORD thy God in vain: for the LORD will not hold him guiltless that taketh his name in vain. Keep the sabbath day to sanctify it, as the LORD thy God hath commanded thee. Six days thou shalt labour, and do all thy work: But the seventh day is the sabbath of the LORD thy God: in it thou shalt not do any work, thou, nor thy son, nor thy daughter, nor thy manservant, nor thy maidservant, nor thine ox, nor thine ass, nor any of thy cattle, nor thy stranger that is within thy gates; that thy manservant and thy maidservant may rest as well as thou. And remember that thou wast a servant in the land of Egypt, and that the LORD thy God brought thee out thence through a mighty hand and by a stretched out arm: therefore the LORD thy God commanded thee to keep the sabbath day. Honour thy father and thy mother, as the LORD thy God hath commanded thee; that thy days may be prolonged, and that it may go well with thee, in the land which the LORD thy God giveth thee. Thou shalt not kill. Neither shalt thou commit adultery. Neither shalt thou steal. Neither shalt thou bear false witness against thy neighbour. Neither shalt thou desire thy neighbour's wife, neither shalt thou covet thy neighbour's house, his field, or his manservant, or his maidservant, his ox, or his ass, or anything that is thy neighbour's. These words the LORD spake unto all your assembly in the mount out of the midst of the fire, of the cloud, and of the thick darkness, with a great voice: and he added no more. And he wrote them in two tables of stone, and delivered them unto me. And it came to pass, when you heard the voice out of the midst of the darkness, (for the mountain did burn with fire,) that you came near unto me, even all the heads of your tribes, and your elders; And you said, Behold, the LORD our God hath showed us his glory and his greatness, and we have heard his voice out of the midst of the fire: we have seen this day that God doth talk with man, and he liveth. Now therefore why should we die? for this great fire will consume us: if we hear the voice of the LORD our God any more, then we shall die. For who is there of all flesh, that hath heard the voice of the living God speaking out of the midst of the fire, as we have, and lived? Go thou near, and hear all that the LORD our God shall say: and speak thou unto us all that the LORD our God shall speak unto thee; and we will hear it, and do it. And the LORD heard the voice of your words, when you spake unto me; and the LORD said unto me, I have heard the voice of the words of this people, which they have spoken unto thee: they have well said all that they have spoken. O that there were such a heart in them, that they would fear me, and keep all my commandments always, that it might be well with them, and with their children forever! Go say to them, Get you into your tents again. But as for thee, stand thou here by me, and I will speak unto thee all the commandments, and the statutes, and the judgments, which thou shalt teach them, that they may do them in the land which I give them to possess it. Ye shall observe to do therefore as the LORD your God hath commanded you: ye shall not turn aside to the right hand or to the left. Ye shall walk in all the ways which the LORD your God hath commanded you, that ye may live, and that it may be well with you, and that ye may prolong your days in the land which ye shall possess. Now these are the commandments, the statutes, and the judgments, which the LORD your God commanded to teach you, that ye might do them in the land whither ye go to possess it: That thou mightest fear the LORD thy God, to keep all his statutes and his commandments, which I command thee, thou, and thy son, and thy son's son, all the days of thy life; and that thy days may be prolonged. Hear thereforeThe daughters of Zelophehad, Mahlah, Noah, Hoglah, Milcah, and Tirzah, approached Moses, Eleazar the priest, and the Israelite leaders, requesting an inheritance among their father's brothers, as he had died without sons. The Lord instructed Moses to grant them their father's inheritance, establishing a precedent for inheritance laws in Israel: if a man dies without a son, his inheritance passes to his daughters; if no children, to his brothers; if no brothers, to his paternal uncles; and if no uncles, to his closest relative. Moses was then told to ascend Mount Abarim to view the Promised Land he would not enter, similar to Aaron's death. God commanded Moses to appoint Joshua, son of Nun, as his successor to lead the people, with Eleazar the priest to consult the Urim for decisions. Moses did as commanded, laying hands on Joshua to invest him with leadership. God detailed the offerings the Israelites were to make, including daily burnt offerings, additional Sabbath offerings, and offerings at the beginning of each month. These offerings included lambs, bullocks, and rams, accompanied by grain and drink offerings, all as a pleasing aroma to the Lord.

The instructions continued with specific offerings for various occasions, such as the Passover and the Feast of Unleavened Bread, where sacrifices made by fire were to be offered without blemish. The offerings included young bullocks, rams, lambs, and a goat for a sin offering to make atonement. These offerings were to be made in addition to the daily burnt offerings, with specific instructions for meat and drink offerings. The Feast of Firstfruits and the seventh month also had designated offerings, including a day of blowing trumpets and a holy convocation where no servile work was to be done. On subsequent days, offerings varied in number but maintained the requirement for animals without blemish and included accompanying meat and drink offerings. The sequence of offerings culminated in a solemn assembly on the eighth day, emphasizing burnt offerings, sacrifices made by fire, and sin offerings, alongside the continual burnt offering. These practices were to be observed during the Lord's set feasts, in addition to vows, freewill offerings, and peace offerings.

Moses communicated these commands to the children of Israel as directed by the Lord. Additionally, regulations concerning vows were detailed, specifying conditions under which vows made by men and women would be binding or voidable, highlighting the importance of one's word and the conditions under which vows could be annulled, particularly in the context of familial and marital relationships. These instructions underscored the value of commitment and the seriousness with which vows to the Lord were to be treated."Hear, O Israel, and observe to do it; that it may be well with thee, and that ye may increase mightily, as the LORD God of thy fathers hath promised thee, in the land that floweth with milk and honey. Hear, O Israel: The LORD our God is one LORD: And thou shalt love the LORD thy God with all thine heart, and with all thy soul, and with all thy might. And these words, which I command thee this day, shall be in thine heart: And thou shalt teach them diligently unto thy children, and shalt talk of them when thou sittest in thine house, and when thou walkest by the way, and when thou liest down, and when thou risest up. And thou shalt bind them for a sign upon thine hand, and they shall be as frontlets between thine eyes. And thou shalt write them upon the posts of thy house, and on thy gates. And it shall be, when the LORD thy God shall have brought thee into the land which he sware unto thy fathers, to Abraham, to Isaac, and to Jacob, to give thee great and goodly cities, which thou buildedst not, And houses full of all good things, which thou filledst not, and wells digged, which thou diggedst not, vineyards and olive trees, which thou plantedst not; when thou shalt have eaten and be full; Then beware lest thou forget the LORD, which brought thee forth out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage. Thou shalt fear the LORD thy God, and serve him, and shalt swear by his name. Ye shall not go after other gods, of the gods of the people which are round about you; (For the LORD thy God is a jealous God among you) lest the anger of the LORD thy God be kindled against thee, and destroy thee from off the face of the earth. Ye shall not tempt the LORD your God, as ye tempted him in Massah. Ye shall diligently keep the commandments of the LORD your God, and his testimonies, and his statutes, which he hath commanded thee. And thou shalt do that which is right and good in the sight of the LORD: that it may be well with thee, and that thou mayest go in and possess the good land which the LORD sware unto thy fathers. To cast out all thine enemies from before thee, as the LORD hath spoken. And when thy son asketh thee in time to come, saying, What mean the testimonies, and the statutes, and the judgments, which the LORD our God hath commanded you? Then thou shalt say unto thy son, We were Pharaohs bondmen in Egypt; and the LORD brought us out of Egypt with a mighty hand: And the LORD shewed signs and wonders, great and sore, upon Egypt, upon Pharaoh, and upon all his household, before our eyes: And he brought us out from thence, that he might bring us in, to give us the land which he sware unto our fathers. And the LORD commanded us to do all these statutes, to fear the LORD our God, for our good always, that he might preserve us alive, as it is at this day. And it shall be our righteousness, if we observe to do all these commandments before the LORD our God, as he hath commanded us. When the LORD thy God shall bring thee into the land whither thou goest to possess it, and hath cast out many nations before thee, the Hittites, and the Girgashites, and the Amorites, and the Canaanites, and the Perizzites, and the Hivites, and the Jebusites, seven nations greater and mightier than thou; And when the LORD thy God shall deliver them before thee; thou shalt smite them, and utterly destroy them; thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor shew mercy unto them: Neither shalt thou make marriages with them; thy daughter thou shalt not give unto his son, nor his daughter shalt thou take unto thy son. For they will turn away thy son from following me, that they may serve other gods: so will the anger of the LORD be kindled against you, and destroy thee suddenly. But thus shall ye deal with them; ye shall destroy their altars, and break down their images, and cut down their groves, and burn their graven images with fire. For thou art an holy people unto the LORD thy God: the LORD thy God hath chosen thee to be a special people unto himself, above all people that are upon the face of the earth. The LORD did not set his love upon you, nor choose you, because ye were more in number than any people; for ye were the fewest of all people: But because the LORD loved you, and because he would keep the oath which he had sworn unto your fathers, hath the LORD brought you out with a mighty hand, and redeemed you out of the house of bondmen, from the hand of Pharaoh king of Egypt. Know therefore that the LORD thy God, he is God, the faithful God, which keepeth covenant and mercy with them that love him and keep his commandments to a thousand generations; And repayeth them that hate him to their face, to destroy them: he will not be slack to him that hateth him, he will repay him to his face. Thou shalt therefore keep the commandments, and the statutes, and the judgments, which I command thee this.""Wherefore it shall come to pass, if ye hearken to these judgments, and keep, and do them, that the LORD thy God shall keep unto thee the covenant and the mercy which he sware unto thy fathers: And he will love thee, and bless thee, and multiply thee: he will also bless the fruit of thy womb, and the fruit of thy land, thy corn, and thy wine, and thine oil, the increase of thy kine, and the flocks of thy sheep, in the land which he sware unto thy fathers to give thee. Thou shalt be blessed above all people: there shall not be male or female barren among you, or among your cattle. And the LORD will take away from thee all sickness, and will put none of the evil diseases of Egypt, which thou knowest, upon thee; but will lay them upon all them that hate thee. And thou shalt consume all the people which the LORD thy God shall deliver thee; thine eye shall have no pity upon them: neither shalt thou serve their gods; for that will be a snare unto thee. If thou shalt say in thine heart, These nations are more than I; how can I dispossess them? Thou shalt not be afraid of them: but shalt well remember what the LORD thy God did unto Pharaoh, and unto all Egypt; The great temptations which thine eyes saw, and the signs, and the wonders, and the mighty hand, and the stretched out arm, whereby the LORD thy God brought thee out: so shall the LORD thy God do unto all the people of whom thou art afraid. Moreover the LORD thy God will send the hornet among them, until they that are left, and hide themselves from thee, be destroyed. Thou shalt not be affrighted at them: for the LORD thy God is among you, a mighty God and terrible. And the LORD thy God will put out those nations before thee by little and little: thou mayest not consume them at once, lest the beasts of the field increase upon thee. But the LORD thy God shall deliver them unto thee, and shall destroy them with a mighty destruction, until they be destroyed. And he shall deliver their kings into thine hand, and thou shalt destroy their name from under heaven: there shall no man be able to stand before thee, until thou have destroyed them. The graven images of their gods shall ye burn with fire: thou shalt not desire the silver or gold that is on them, nor take it unto thee, lest thou be snared therein: for it is an abomination to the LORD thy God. Neither shalt thou bring an abomination into thine house, lest thou be a cursed thing like it: but thou shalt utterly detest it, and thou shalt utterly abhor it; for it is a cursed thing. All the commandments which I command thee this day shall ye observe to do, that ye may live, and multiply, and go in and possess the land which the LORD sware unto your fathers. And thou shalt remember all the way which the LORD thy God led thee these forty years in the wilderness, to humble thee, and to prove thee, to know what was in thine heart, whether thou wouldest keep his commandments, or no. And he humbled thee, and suffered thee to hunger, and fed thee with manna, which thou knewest not, neither did thy fathers know; that he might make thee know that man doth not live by bread only, but by every word that proceedeth out of the mouth of the LORD doth man live. Thy raiment waxed not old upon thee, neither did thy foot swell, these forty years. Thou shalt also consider in thine heart, that, as a man chasteneth his son, so the LORD thy God chasteneth thee. Therefore thou shalt keep the commandments of the LORD thy God, to walk in his ways, and to fear him. For the LORD thy God bringeth thee into a good land, a land of brooks of water, of fountains and depths that spring out of valleys and hills; A land of wheat, and barley, and vines, and fig trees, and pomegranates; a land of oil olive, and honey; A land wherein thou shalt eat bread without scarceness, thou shalt not lack any thing in it; a land whose stones are iron, and out of whose hills thou mayest dig brass. When thou hast eaten and art full, then thou shalt bless the LORD thy God for the good land which he hath given thee.
